Integration test asserts a promoted finding rejects a status-flip PATCH with 422. | None material — the promote anchor + the action_item's own chain are the durable records; the finding's substance is pinned. |
| T-I40 | Stored PDFs are written to Tigris without `ServerSideEncryption` — ADR-0007 §3.9 pledged "Tigris-side encryption (SSE)" but `putEvidenceObject` set no SSE parameter on the PUT command, leaving rendered PDFs (finding observations, corrective actions, photo plaintext) at rest in cleartext (S5 priv-F1 close-out) | `apps/api/src/evidence/tigris.ts` `buildPutObjectCommand` sets `ServerSideEncryption: 'AES256'` on every PutObjectCommand. `AES256` is the safe S3-compatible default; `aws:kms` is a future swap when a KMS key is provisioned (runbook §8 flags as ops follow-up). Unit test asserts the parameter is set. | Bucket-level default-encryption policy + Tigris lifecycle policy for `exports/*` are ops follow-ups (runbook §8 + 1.12). The route's `expires_at` is the only TTL enforcer until then. |
| T-I41 | `POST /api/inspections/:id/findings` accepts `awaiting_signatures` as an allowed state — once the inspector signs a rack inspection, the rep can still create findings while the supervisor and co-chair are reading (S5 sec-F7 close-out) | `apps/api/src/routes/inspections/index.ts` POST findings handler restricts the state allow-list to `['scheduled', 'in_progress']` only. Late-added findings after the inspector signs are blocked with 422 `inspection_not_open_for_findings`. The symmetry with PATCH (`in_progress` only) makes chain-of-custody coherent: all finding authoring precedes the first signature. Integration test asserts POST in `awaiting_signatures` returns 422. | For zone_monthly the inspector signature transitions directly to `complete`, so this path was always closed; the fix matters for rack. |
| T-I42 | Tigris PUT happens BEFORE the chain anchor + DB INSERT — a transaction failure after PUT leaves an orphan PDF in Tigris with no `export_records` row pointing at it and no chain anchor (S5 sec-F6 close-out) | `apps/api/src/routes/inspections/exports.ts` wraps the `db.transaction` call in a try/catch. On rollback, best-effort `DeleteObject` against the orphaned `storageKey` via `deleteEvidenceObject(storageKey)`. Logged at warn level (success or failure). Never throws from cleanup — the original transaction error re-raises. The `expires_at` cleanup remains the primary TTL bound; this catch closes the chain-mismatch window. | A best-effort delete can fail (NoSuchKey, network drop); the runbook §8 covers the bucket lifecycle policy follow-up for any orphans that survive both gates. |
| T-I43 | The PDF photo captions render GPS coordinates without per-export consent or redaction option — every exported PDF distributes ~11m-resolution coordinates whether the rep meant to or not (S5 priv-F7 close-out) | `apps/api/src/routes/inspections/exports.ts` create-body Zod schema gains `includeGps: z.boolean().default(false)`. `renderInspectionPdf(..., { includeGps })` only renders the `GPS lat, lon` caption fragment when `includeGps === true`. The default flipped to opt-out: GPS is NOT in the PDF unless the rep affirmatively checks the export panel's "Include GPS coordinates" checkbox. Mirrors the PIPEDA P4 limiting-collection posture for distributable artifacts. Integration test asserts a default-false export's PDF carries no `GPS ` prefix; a true export carries it. | The 1.7 T-E5 GPS-resolution cap (~11m) remains; the export gate is layered on top. |
| T-I44 | The PDF renderer hard-ignores the workplace's configured zone display names — surfaces stale labels ("Zone 3" instead of "Cold Warehouse") in the rep's evidentiary exhibit (S5 priv-F6 close-out) | `apps/api/src/routes/inspections/exports.ts` `resolveZoneDisplayName` reads from `loadWorkplaceConfig().zones`. Returns the configured `displayName` if non-empty AND ≤120 chars AND contains no `<` / `>` (HTML strip). Falls back to `defaultName` ("Zone N") silently on violation — no crash, no warning. The metadata fields (`/Title`, `/Author`, `/Producer`) stay generic per T-I28; only the rendered text body surfaces the configured zone label. Workplace name itself stays out of the PDF body until 1.9 (runbook §11). | An over-length or HTML-containing `ZONE_N_NAME` env value silently falls back to the default — deployment-checklist item; runbook §10. |

**Audit hooks for inspections.** Six new event kinds added to `packages/shared-types` `AuditEventKind` (ADR-0007 §3.11). All payloads pass through the same typed-emit boundary as 1.3 priv-F2 — PI-clean by construction (enum IDs + hashes + counts only, never names or free text):

- `inspection.created` — `{inspectionId, templateVersionId, zoneId, conductedByUserId}`. No template content, no zone display name.
- `inspection_finding.created` — `{findingId, inspectionId, itemNumber, status}`. No `observation`, no `corrective_action`, no `responsible_party`.
- `inspection_finding.promoted` — `{findingId, actionItemId, risk}`. No description, no owner. Pairs with the action-items side's own `action_item.created` anchor (both land in one transaction per §3.7 step 6).
- `inspection.signed` — `{inspectionId, role, signerUserId}`. No `note_ct`. Each signature emits its own anchor (per §3.8: separate-row design over JSONB blob).
- `inspection.exported` — `{exportId, inspectionIds, outputSha256, byteSize}`. The `outputSha256` is the one-way integrity anchor; `inspectionIds` is opaque uuid[].
- `audit.inspection_template.seeded` — `{templateVersionId, templateCode, versionNumber, sectionCount, contentSha256}`. **Never** stores section text, item text, or CSA-derived criteria (T-I10).

A seventh ratchet event — the extension of `evidence_files.linked_type` to accept `'inspection_finding'` — is **not** a new chain kind but a forward-seam ratchet on the existing `evidence.uploaded` / `evidence.read` / `evidence.list_accessed` events from 1.7. The 1.8 migration extends the `evidence_files_linked_fk_guard` trigger and the route's `acceptedLinkedTypes` array in lockstep (T-I14); the audit payload shape from 1.7 already accommodates the new linkedType value without schema change.

**Documented residuals on the inspections audit surface (S5 priv-F3 / priv-F5).** The six-kind contract leaves two read-path anchors unimplemented in 1.8, both deferred to 1.9 and documented in `docs/runbooks/inspections.md` §4:

- **No `inspection_finding.read` anchor.** `GET /api/inspections/findings/:id` decrypts observation / corrective_action / responsible_party and returns plaintext. The route is step-up gated at 60s, but no chain anchor fires on success. An attacker who walks every finding by id leaves no per-read trail (the `inspection.created` + `inspection_finding.created` anchors bound the surface). 1.9 adds the kind without ceremony (the 1.7 evidence path added three kinds the same way).
- **No `inspection.export.downloaded` anchor.** `GET /api/inspections/exports/:id/download` is step-up gated + CSRF-header gated, but re-downloads after the original `inspection.exported` anchor are invisible to the chain. The 30-day TTL + per-request step-up freshness are the residual bound; the inline comment in `exports.ts` commits to the 1.9 ratchet.

### 2.9 Recommendation threats (Milestone 1.9)

Recommendations are the worker co-chair's most consequential statutory artifact (OHSA s.9(20) / CLC s.135(5)) and the first surface to combine **long-form encrypted prose** (200–2000 word body with inline citation markers), a **status machine that spans an external counterparty** (the 21-day s.9(21) clock waits on management's response), a **cryptographically signed PDF** under a workplace-controlled Ed25519 key, and a **chain-of-custody guarantee that survives withdrawal**. The threat surface is the union of 1.5 (encrypted free text + status machine), 1.6 (action-item bridge + polymorphic source FK), 1.7 (workplace-key decrypt + step-up + Tigris SSE), and 1.8 (PDF render + step-up gate + 30-day TTL + signature workflow), plus four new surfaces: per-jurisdiction recommendation numbering, the `[[cite:N]]` marker discipline, the signed-export ZIP bundle, and the second workplace key (Ed25519 signing, separate primitive from the X25519 sealed-box encryption key). Every mitigation below cites the ADR-0008 subsection or the CLAUDE.md non-negotiable it implements.

| # | Threat | Mitigation | Residual |
|---|---|---|---|
| T-R1 | A hand-crafted PATCH to `/api/recommendations/:id` flips `status` from `draft` to `resolved` directly, bypassing the submit + response transitions and silently skipping the chain anchors that prove what management actually saw | ADR-0008 §3.1: each lifecycle transition is its own dedicated endpoint (`/submit`, `/responses`, `/resolve`, `/withdraw`); the general PATCH route's Zod schema excludes `status` from the allow-list and applies `.strict()` on top — a PATCH with `status='resolved'` reaches the `.strict()` reject and returns **400 `invalid_body`** (NOT 422 `status_not_updatable` — S5 priv-F6 close-out corrects the prior doc/code drift; the route-layer Zod `.strict()` is the gate). The transition graph is enforced at the route layer per ADR-0007 §3.7 fail-closed posture — the DB CHECK accepts every value in `recommendationStatus` because the API is the single source of truth. Integration test asserts a hand-crafted PATCH with `status='resolved'` returns 400 `invalid_body`. Non-negotiable #2 — every transition is a chain anchor. | None material. The DB CHECK breadth is the documented tradeoff (matches §3.1's "API surface is the single source of truth for transitions"). |
| T-R2 | A withdrawn recommendation is resubmitted via a hand-crafted POST to `/submit`, producing a second `recommendation.submitted` chain anchor and a second linked action item for what is evidentially the same recommendation | ADR-0008 §3.1: `withdrawn` is terminal alongside `resolved`; the `/submit` handler asserts `status='draft'` before any state change. Integration test asserts `/submit` against a withdrawn (or already-submitted) recommendation rejects with 422 `submit_requires_draft`. The withdrawal itself is the chain-of-custody evidence per non-negotiable #2 — there is no DELETE path on withdrawn rows. | A rep who genuinely needs to re-issue a withdrawn recommendation creates a new recommendation; the runbook covers the `link_kind='replaces'` (deferred) seam. |
| T-R3 | Zod `recommendationStatus` enum drifts from the SQL CHECK — adding a new state (e.g. `under_review`) in code without the migration leaves the DB CHECK rejecting writes the route now produces | ADR-0008 §3.2: the enum lives in `packages/shared-types/src/index.ts` and is the single source for both the Zod schema and the migration's CHECK literal. The migration linter (1.6 sec-F1 shape) flags any drift between the shared-types enum and the live CHECK in migration 0008. Tests assert every Zod-accepted value is in the live CHECK. | A future enum addition that skips updating the migration linter manifest could drift; mitigated by the lint rule + CI grep on the CHECK literal. |
| T-R4 | Two reps concurrently call `/submit` on different drafts in the same jurisdiction and both receive `recommendation_number=14`, breaking the `(jurisdiction, recommendation_number)` UNIQUE | ADR-0008 §3.2: per-period sequence allocated via `pg_advisory_xact_lock(hashtext('recommendations.number.<jurisdiction>'))` inside the submit transaction — same `allocateSequenceNumber` shape as `apps/api/src/routes/action-items/index.ts:945`. Two concurrent submits serialize; the second sees `MAX(recommendation_number) WHERE jurisdiction=$1` already advanced. The UNIQUE index is the structural backstop — a missed lock surfaces as a 23505 rollback, not a duplicate row. | Single-co-chair scope makes contention negligible; the advisory-lock pattern is proven on action-items 1.6. |
| T-R5 | The list endpoint projects `title_ct` / `body_ct` plaintext, leaking PI-bearing recommendation text (supervisor names, accommodation context, reprisal narratives) bypassing the step-up gate that the detail route enforces (mirror of T-H4 / T-I12) | ADR-0008 §3.2: list route projects `{id, recommendation_number, jurisdiction, status, drafted_at, submitted_at, response_received_at, resolved_at, withdrawn_at, drafted_by_user_id, citation_count, response_count, deadline_at, days_remaining}` only. `title_ct` / `body_ct` decrypt requires the detail route + step-up (same posture as 1.5 hazards detail + 1.8 findings detail). Title is not exposed at all in list; the rep navigates by recommendation number + status. Non-negotiable #4. | Step-up bound; an authenticated rep with their own factors can decrypt their own recommendations. Same scope as the rest of the encrypted surface. |
| T-R6 | A rep types a `[[cite:5]]` marker in the body with no corresponding citation list entry, producing a dangling marker that the renderer expands to an empty footnote in the signed PDF | ADR-0008 §3.3: submit-handler Zod refinement asserts every `[[cite:N]]` marker in the decrypted body has a `position=N` entry in the citation list AND vice versa AND positions are dense 1..K with no gaps. Submit rejects with 422 `citation_marker_density_violation` enumerating the offending positions. Client-side CitationRef component runs the same Zod rules pre-submit (§3.13 S3) so the rep sees the error inline. Non-negotiable #5. | A hand-crafted SQL INSERT bypasses Zod; detected because the renderer's expand-pass fails loud (no silent footnote omission) and the export route's `assertCitationsResolvable` rejects before plaintext is opened. |
| T-R7 | A `recommendation_citations` row references a `(statute_code, citation_text, version_date)` triple that does not exist in `legal_clauses`, violating non-negotiable #5 — a fabricated OHSA citation slips through | ADR-0008 §3.3: submit-handler resolves every triple against `statutes JOIN clauses` at submit time and rejects with 422 `citation_not_in_corpus` if any has no row. The `clause_id` column FKs `clauses(id)` with `ON DELETE RESTRICT`; the citation row cannot exist without a corpus row. Additionally the resolver asserts the joined clause's `corpus_version` matches the active `corpus_versions.version` (rejects citations against retired corpus versions per §3.3). CI test in `packages/legal-corpus` asserts the validator rejects a known-bad triple. Non-negotiable #5. | A direct INSERT that races a corpus migration (citation valid at INSERT, retired before submit chain) — bounded by `ON DELETE RESTRICT` on `clauses` and the seeder's INSERT-only / never-DELETE discipline from 1.4 T-LC5. |
| T-R8 | The corpus is amended (`version_date` V → V') after a recommendation is submitted; the signed PDF's footnote provenance hashes verify against the old V but a reader fetching the live corpus sees V', generating an "evidence tampered" false alarm | ADR-0008 §3.3 + §3.8: `recommendation_citations` snapshots `citation_text`, `version_date`, and `body_hash` at submit time — the citation row carries the corpus state pinned to the recommendation, not a live-resolving pointer. The signed PDF's footnote line reads `[N] {citationText} ({versionDate}) — {bodyText}. Provenance: clause hash {bodyHash}` — the verifier checks against the historical clause row by `version_date`, which the 1.4 corpus's append-only-version invariant (T-LC3 / T-LC5) guarantees still exists. The chain anchor's `citationsHash` (§3.8) is sha256 of the canonical-JSON of the resolved citations including each `body_hash` — a re-export of the same recommendation after a corpus amendment produces a different `citationsHash` and the chain records both. Non-negotiable #5. | The runbook documents the recipient verification recipe: fetch the historical clause row via `(statute_code, citation, version_date)` rather than the live active version. |
| T-R9 | A response row at `position=N` is UPDATEd to alter the management text after the fact — the evidentiary append-only contract is broken silently | ADR-0008 §3.4: `recommendation_responses` has no API write path beyond `POST /api/recommendations/:id/responses` (an INSERT-only handler); the general PATCH route excludes response columns entirely. The `(recommendation_id, position)` UNIQUE plus the `position >= 1` CHECK make a clobber require explicit UPDATE SQL — detected at audit-chain verify (the `recommendation.response_captured` anchor carries `responseId + position` only, so an out-of-band UPDATE leaves the chain anchor pointing at the wrong text). Non-negotiable #2 — every response is its own chain anchor. | Detection-only at the DB level; runbook tamper procedure covers the response. A typo in transcription is corrected by appending `position=N+1`, never edit (§3.4 + accepted tradeoff). |
| T-R10 | Two reps concurrently POST responses for the same recommendation; both compute `position=2` from the same MAX query and the UNIQUE collides at the second insert, producing a 500 instead of an ordered append | ADR-0008 §3.4: response insert acquires `SELECT MAX(position) FROM recommendation_responses WHERE recommendation_id=$1 FOR UPDATE` (or `pg_advisory_xact_lock(hashtext('rec.response.' || rec_id))`) inside the transaction. Two concurrent posts serialize; the second sees the first's position. The UNIQUE is the structural backstop. Integration test asserts concurrent inserts produce position 1 then 2, never a 23505. | Same per-row lock posture as 1.5 T-H8 / 1.6 T-AI5. |
| T-R11 | The response `body_ct` / `author_role_ct` plaintext is returned in the list projection, leaking management strategy + counterparty role | ADR-0008 §3.4: list route projects `{position, received_at, received_by_user_id}` per response; body + author_role decrypt requires the detail route + step-up. The status flag `has_response: bool` exposes presence without text. The chain payload carries `responseId + position + recommendationId` only — no role text, no body. Non-negotiable #4. | Step-up bound; same scope as T-R5. |
| T-R12 | The action-item bridge is auto-created at draft instead of submit, cluttering the minutes' `recommendation` section with abandoned drafts and leaking the draft's existence into the chain before the rep has committed to submit | ADR-0008 §3.5: action item creation is wired only into the `/submit` handler; the draft create handler emits `recommendation.created` (no action_item) and writes nothing to `action_items` or `recommendation_action_item_links`. Integration test asserts `POST /api/recommendations` followed by `GET /api/action-items?section=recommendation` does not show the draft. Non-negotiable #12 — action items are first-class, not draft byproducts. | None material. |
| T-R13 | The submit transaction creates the recommendation row + the action_item row + the link row + the chain anchor; a mid-transaction failure (advisory-lock contention, audit_log_pkey collision) leaves orphans: action_item with no link, or link with no action_item | ADR-0008 §3.5: all four writes — recommendation status flip, action_items INSERT, recommendation_action_item_links INSERT, `recommendation.submitted` audit append — run inside one `db.transaction`. Failure on any one rolls back all four; the recommendation stays in `draft`, no orphan action_item, no orphan link. Same posture as 1.5 T-H9 + 1.8 T-I17 bidirectional FK transaction. Non-negotiable #2. | Verified by integration test (§3.13 S2). The rep retries — the chain row is the proof of what actually completed. |
| T-R14 | The 1.6 `action_items_source_fk_guard` trigger is not ratcheted with a `'recommendation'` branch in migration 0008; a `POST /api/action-items` with `sourceType='recommendation'` and a bogus `source_id` slips a dangling action item through (1.6 priv-AI-F3 / 1.7 sec-F4 / 1.8 T-I38 forward-seam pattern) | ADR-0008 §3.5 + §3.13: migration 0008 extends `action_items_source_fk_guard` with a `'recommendation'` branch validating `source_id IN (SELECT id FROM recommendations)`. The trigger's `ELSE RAISE EXCEPTION` rail (1.8 T-I38 / sec-F4 close-out) preserves the fail-closed posture for future kinds. The action-items route's `sourceType` Zod refinement is widened in lockstep. Both ratchets land in the same migration to prevent half-rollout. Integration test asserts `POST /api/action-items` with `sourceType='recommendation'` and a bogus uuid fails with 23514 at the trigger. Non-negotiable #12. | None material — explicit ratchet closes the 1.6 forward seam. |
| T-R15 | A withdrawn recommendation leaves its linked action_item in an active section (`recommendation` or `old_business`) — the minutes show the action item as live even though the recommendation behind it is dead | ADR-0008 §3.5: the `/withdraw` handler invokes the 1.6 section-move handler inside its transaction to move the linked action_item to `section='archived'` with `status='Cancelled'` and the literal template-supplied reason `"Recommendation withdrawn."` (NOT the rep's free-text reason — that lives only on `recommendations.withdrawal_reason_ct`). Two chain rows (`action_item.moved` + `recommendation.withdrawn`) land in one transaction. Integration test asserts the move happens and the action_item is unfindable in `section='recommendation'` post-withdrawal. | None material. |
| T-R16 | The 21-day s.9(21) deadline is computed only client-side; a rep can render an ON recommendation as "3 days remaining" past day 21 by manipulating the local clock, undermining the evidentiary surface that "responded on day N" is supposed to be | ADR-0008 §3.6: the `recommendation-clock.ts` pure function runs server-side in the projection (same posture as 1.6 action-flag.ts per T-AI7). The web client renders the returned `deadline_at` + `days_remaining` + badge severity verbatim and does not re-compute. Integration test asserts list/detail projections include the server-computed clock fields. Status flipped to `response_received` pins `days_to_respond = received_at - submitted_at` server-side; the badge surfaces that as "responded on day N" — the deficiency stays evidentially recorded even if management responded late. Non-negotiable #7 (rights-protective UI). | Client cache staleness across day boundaries (mirror of T-AI7 residual); a list cached at 23:59 reads "3 days" then morning is "2 days." The rep refreshes. |
| T-R17 | A CA-FED recommendation displays a fixed 21-day or 30-day deadline despite CLC s.135(6) being "as soon as possible" — the app invents a statutory deadline that doesn't exist (non-negotiable #5 forbids invention) | ADR-0008 §3.6: the `recommendation-clock.ts` projection branches on `jurisdiction` — CA-FED returns `{days_since_submission: N, deadline_at: null, badge_severity: 'informational'}` with no color escalation. The UI badge reads "days since submission: N" with no overdue label. No default 30-day backstop. Tests assert CA-FED projections never include a non-null `deadline_at`. Non-negotiable #5 / #7. | A rep operating in a hybrid jurisdiction (rare; mostly federal aviation/marine/banking) reads the badge carefully; runbook covers the distinction. |
| T-R18 | The signed PDF carries the signature bytes but not the `signing_key_id` — a verifier confronted with two workplace keys (post-rotation) doesn't know which public key to verify against | ADR-0008 §3.7 + §3.9: the ZIP bundle's `manifest.json` carries `signing_key_id`, `signing_key_fingerprint`, and `signature_algorithm`. The `GET /api/recommendations/exports/:id/manifest` endpoint returns the manifest + the historical public key for that id (retired keys stay queryable per §3.7). Verifier reads the fingerprint, fetches the matching public key, runs `sodium.crypto_sign_verify_detached`. The chain anchor's `signing_key_id` (in `recommendation.exported` payload) lets `audit-log-verify` cross-check that the manifest's claimed key id matches the chain row. Non-negotiable #16. | A future PAdES upgrade (§3.9 deferred to 1.12) reduces this to a single PDF the reader verifies natively; sidecar exports remain verifiable via the manifest route. |
| T-R19 | A migration bug or hand-crafted INSERT produces two `workplace_signing_keys` rows with `active=true`, leaving the export handler with a non-deterministic choice and risking signatures under the wrong key | ADR-0008 §3.7: partial UNIQUE index `workplace_signing_keys_active_unique ON (active) WHERE active = true` enforces "at most one active" at the DB layer. A second `active=true` INSERT fails with 23505. The seed runbook calls `getActiveSigningKey()` which returns the single row or throws — never silently picks one. | None material — DB-layer backstop, same shape as the 1.7 workplace_keys discipline. |
| T-R20 | The Ed25519 private signing key is cached in API memory past the export response (mirror of 1.8 T-I23 plaintext-lifetime), risking accidental sign-with-stale-key on the next request after a rotation | ADR-0008 §3.7 + §3.8: the private signing key is opened inside the export route's bounded-plaintext window using `sodium_malloc`-backed buffers from `@jhsc/crypto`, used to produce the `crypto_sign_detached` bytes, then `sodium.memzero`'d immediately (mirror of 1.7 evidence decrypt + 1.8 photo decrypt). No module-level cache; each export re-opens via `getActiveSigningKey()`. The plaintext-zero assertion is part of the §3.13 S4 test surface (spy-counts `sodium.memzero` calls against the two key opens — encryption + signing). Non-negotiable #4. | Bun GC may copy the buffer before `memzero` fires; same bound as 1.8 T-I23. |
| T-R21 | Signing-key rotation in 1.12 purges the prior `workplace_signing_keys` row instead of marking it `retired_at`, breaking verification of every past signed export | ADR-0008 §3.7: rotation INSERTs a new row with `active=true` and UPDATEs the prior to `active=false, retired_at=now()` — retired rows stay in the table forever. The migration linter rejects any `DELETE FROM workplace_signing_keys` diff. The manifest route reads by id regardless of `retired_at`. Runbook §"rotation" documents the procedure and the "retired keys are evidence" stance. Non-negotiable #2. | Operational; runbook + lint rule are the bounds. Rotation lands in 1.12 with the public verification page (§3.7). |
| T-R22 | The decrypted body buffer carrying supervisor names / accommodation context persists past the PDF response (mirror of 1.8 T-I23) | ADR-0008 §3.8: `pdf-shared` discipline applies — title + body + every response's author_role + body decrypt inside the render request lifetime using `sodium_malloc`-backed buffers, with `sodium.memzero` after `pdfkit.text()` returns. Workplace encryption private key is `memzero`'d at request end. The plaintext-zero assertion (§3.13 S4) covers both the long-form body buffer and the per-response buffers. Same posture as 1.8 T-I23 scaled to long-form prose. Non-negotiable #4 / #16. | Bun GC bound (same as T-R20 / T-I23); documented. JS string immutability means the buffer-derived string is the unavoidable cost — same documented tradeoff as 1.8. |
| T-R23 | A clause body fetched from the corpus contains characters that inject PDF markup or overflow the renderer's line-break logic when expanded into a footnote (the corpus is trusted but a future seed-fixture bug could land hostile UTF-8) | ADR-0008 §3.8 + 1.4 sec-F1 lineage: corpus fixtures are Zod-validated at seed time against `<` / `>` (priv-F2/sec-F1 carries forward). The `pdfkit.text()` API is text-only — no markup parser, no script surface, no `/JS` / `/JavaScript` / `/AA` / `/OpenAction` per 1.8 T-I25. Footnote text is treated as plain text via `pdfkit`'s default escaping. Golden-PDF test asserts a fixture with `<`/`>`/`{`/`}` renders as literal glyphs, not markup. | Library bug surface; mitigated by golden-PDF test on every PR that touches `pdf-shared/` or `recommendations/pdf-renderer.ts`. |
| T-R24 | The provenance footer's `chainIdx` placeholder is computed pre-replace and the post-replace pass mismatches it against the actual chain row index (mirror of 1.8 sec-F8 hash-replace pattern) | ADR-0008 §3.8 (per ADR-0007 §3.9 simplified pattern): footer carries `Chain idx {predictedIdx}` written in the first pass. The chain append uses `pg_advisory_xact_lock('audit_log.append')` and returns the actual `idx`; the route asserts `predictedIdx === actualIdx` inside the transaction and throws `ChainIdxMismatch` (transaction rollback, no Tigris PUT) on drift. Golden-PDF test asserts the rendered footer's idx matches the chain anchor's `audit_idx`. Non-negotiable #2 / #16. | Predicted-idx contention under concurrent appenders is bounded by the advisory lock (1.3 T-AC4 shape); single-co-chair scope makes contention negligible. |
| T-R25 | The ZIP bundle is non-deterministic — file timestamps in the ZIP central directory change per render, producing a different `output_sha256` for byte-identical signed content (defeats the chain anchor's integrity claim) | ADR-0008 §3.9: ZIP assembly uses a fixed epoch (`1980-01-01T00:00:00Z` — the ZIP-format minimum) for every entry's mtime, fixed `external_attr=0`, fixed entry order (`recommendation-<id>.pdf`, then `recommendation-<id>.pdf.sig`, then `manifest.json`). The bundle is hashed AFTER assembly and that hash is what the chain row + manifest carry. Byte-stability test (§3.13 S4) asserts two renders of identical inputs produce byte-identical ZIPs. | None material — deterministic-ZIP is a solved problem; the test guards against regression. |
| T-R26 | The Ed25519 signature is computed over the PDF bytes only; the manifest is unsigned, so an attacker can swap the manifest (changing `signing_key_id` to a compromised key whose private they hold) while leaving the legitimate signature + PDF intact, fooling a verifier who trusts the manifest's key id | ADR-0008 §3.9: the manifest is metadata about the signature, not subject to forgery in the sense that matters — a verifier MUST verify `sodium.crypto_sign_verify_detached(sig, pdfBytes, publicKey)` against the public key derived from `signing_key_fingerprint`, not from `signing_key_id` alone. The manifest endpoint cross-checks the fingerprint against the stored row; a swapped `signing_key_id` resolves to a different fingerprint and the verifier hits a fingerprint-mismatch. The chain anchor's `signing_key_id` is the durable record of which key was actually used. Runbook documents the verification recipe (fingerprint-first). | A verifier who trusts the manifest's key id without checking the fingerprint can be fooled — runbook is the bound. The PAdES upgrade (1.12) closes this structurally by embedding in PDF. |
| T-R27 | An attacker swaps `recommendation-<id>.pdf` inside the ZIP for a tampered PDF while leaving the .sig and manifest intact — the signature fails to verify (detection), but a careless recipient who only looks at the manifest might miss the failure | ADR-0008 §3.9: verification flow is fingerprint → fetch public key → `crypto_sign_verify_detached(sig, pdfBytes, publicKey)`; a tampered PDF flips the verify to `false`. The runbook's verification recipe (and the 1.12 public verification page) leads with "verification status" as the headline. The chain anchor's `outputSha256` (computed over the PDF bytes) is the secondary cross-check — a tampered PDF has a different hash than the chain recorded. **S5 sec-F3 close-out (T-R45):** the download path also extracts `signature.bin` from the ZIP, computes `sha256(signatureBytes)`, and cross-checks against `export_records.signature_sha256` (the chain-anchored signature hash). A consistent-ZIP-swap (attacker re-signs with a different key + rewrites manifest.pdfSha256 to match a tampered PDF) flips this to 500 `export_signature_tamper_detected`. The full Ed25519 crypto verify on every download remains a 1.12 hardening item; the SHA-256 cross-check is the cheap-and-correct close-out per the S5 reviewer. | Detection-only at the recipient; runbook + 1.12 public verifier page are the operational bounds. |
| T-R28 | The step-up freshness floor doesn't engage on the recommendation export route — a stale grant from `evidence.decrypt` or `inspection.export` (also 60s, different action) is silently accepted (mirror of 1.8 T-I30) | ADR-0008 §3.10: export routes call `checkStepUpFreshness({ maxAgeSeconds: 60, action: 'recommendation.export' })` for the create path and `'recommendation.export.download'` for the re-download path. The freshness check binds to the action string AND the elapsed time; a grant from a different action is rejected. `WWW-Authenticate` header carries `max_age="60"` (1.5 sec-F3 pattern). The export route opens TWO private keys (encryption + signing) — the 60s floor is the right posture for the privilege exercised. Non-negotiable #16. | None material — same shape as 1.8 T-I30. |
| T-R29 | A 60s step-up grant for `recommendation.export` of recommendation A is replayed within the window to export recommendation B, smuggling a different artifact under the same grant | 60s freshness floor enforced on every recommendation export route. The action string `recommendation.export.<id>` is reported in the WWW-Authenticate challenge header for the client's UX (the global step-up modal surfaces WHICH recommendation the grant is for), **but the server enforces only the (actor, freshness-window) tuple — NOT a per-action binding**. `checkStepUpFreshness` ignores the `action` parameter when matching grants. A fresh grant obtained for any prior step-up action within the 60s window IS accepted by any subsequent step-up gate. **S5 sec-F1 close-out (user-authorized doc-only fix):** the prior wording claimed per-recommendation binding that the implementation does not deliver; the honest stance is documented here and in `apps/api/src/auth/step-up.ts`'s inline contract comment. True per-action binding (storing `(action, until)` tuples on the session model + asserting cross-action rejection) is a 1.12 hardening item documented in `docs/runbooks/recommendations.md` §11. The integration test asserts the action-string content in the WWW-Authenticate header (the UX contract) — NOT cross-action rejection (which would be misleading given the current implementation). | Coarse-grained freshness instead of per-action binding; 1.12 backlog item closes the structural gap. |
| T-R30 | Re-download of an existing signed bundle (`GET /api/recommendations/exports/:id/download`) is invisible to the chain — re-downloads after the original `recommendation.exported` anchor leave no trail (mirror of 1.8 priv-F5 / `inspection.export.downloaded` residual that 1.9 was supposed to close) | **S5 sec-F2 close-out (T-R43):** the 1.9 ratchet adds both `inspection.export.downloaded` AND the symmetric `recommendation.export.downloaded` kind. The recommendation re-download handler emits a per-call anchor inside a db.transaction AFTER step-up clears AND Tigris fetch succeeds AND the TOCTOU verify (PDF hash + signature hash cross-checks per T-R45) passes AND BEFORE the bytes return. Failed paths (401, 404, 410, SHA mismatch, signature mismatch, wrong_kind) do NOT anchor. The chain row's `actor_id` slot pins the downloader's user id; the payload echoes `{exportId, recommendationId, downloadedByUserId}`. Cross-link: T-I31 inspection.export.downloaded for the structurally-identical sibling. Step-up gated at 60s + CSRF header per T-E14 / T-I30 pattern. | None material — the 1.9 ratchet closes the 1.8 residual on both surfaces. |
| T-R31 | The `export_records.kind` CHECK extension breaks existing 1.8 rows — the migration drops the old `CHECK (kind IN ('inspection_single','inspection_batch'))` and the new constraint rejects 1.8-era rows that fail the new column-nullness alignment | ADR-0008 §3.11: migration 0008 drops the old CHECK then re-adds `CHECK (kind IN ('inspection_single','inspection_batch','recommendation_single'))` + the column-nullness alignment CHECK in the same migration. The alignment CHECK is structured so existing 1.8 rows (with `inspection_ids IS NOT NULL` and `recommendation_id IS NULL`) satisfy it. Migration test loads a 1.8-era fixture, runs migration 0008, asserts the row still validates. The four new columns (`recommendation_id`, `signature_sha256`, `signing_key_id`, `citations_hash`) are nullable specifically to keep 1.8 rows valid. | None material — accepted tradeoff per §3.11 (4 nullable columns + 1 alignment CHECK is cheaper than a sibling table). |
| T-R32 | A `kind='recommendation_single'` row is INSERTed with a non-null `inspection_ids` array, misusing the 1.8 column for a recommendation export — confusion at the re-download path | ADR-0008 §3.11: the column-nullness alignment CHECK enforces `kind='recommendation_single' IMPLIES inspection_ids IS NULL AND recommendation_id IS NOT NULL AND signature_sha256 IS NOT NULL AND signing_key_id IS NOT NULL AND citations_hash IS NOT NULL`. A misuse fails at INSERT with 23514. Routes filter by `kind` before dispatching to the inspection vs recommendation re-download path. | None material — DB-layer backstop. |
| T-R33 | The re-download route serves a recommendation ZIP with `Content-Type: application/pdf` (or vice versa) — a browser inline-renders the ZIP as PDF, confusing recipients and breaking signature verification | ADR-0008 §3.8 + §3.11: download handler reads `kind` from `export_records`, sets `Content-Type: application/zip` + `Content-Disposition: attachment; filename="recommendation-<id>.zip"` for `recommendation_single`, and `application/pdf` + the inspections naming for `inspection_single`. Per 1.7 T-E15 close-out, `Content-Disposition: attachment` forces a download dialog (no inline render). Integration test asserts mime-type per kind. | None material. |
| T-R34 | The withdrawal handler emits `recommendation.withdrawn` with the rep's `withdrawalReason` text in the payload, leaking PI (supervisor names, accommodation context) into the immutable chain (mirror of 1.3 T-AC9 / 1.5 T-H7 typed-payload invariant) | ADR-0008 §3.1 + Compliance #4: the `AuditPayload` discriminated union in `packages/shared-types/src/index.ts` defines `recommendation.withdrawn` as `{recommendationId, linkedActionItemId?}` — the `reason` field is structurally not declarable; the typechecker rejects the field at every `append()` call site. The reason text lives only on `recommendations.withdrawal_reason_ct` (envelope-encrypted, step-up-gated read). The action_item's archive-move reason is the literal template `"Recommendation withdrawn."` (§3.5) — never the rep's free text. Same priv-F2 invariant as 1.3 / 1.5 T-H7 / 1.6 T-AI6 / 1.7 T-E7 / 1.8 T-I10. Non-negotiable #2 + #4. | None material — the union type is the structural enforcement. The 1.12 JSON-schema runtime reject layer is the deferred backstop. |
| T-R35 | The withdrawal flow uses shame-coded copy ("Are you sure you want to give up on this recommendation?") that discourages a rep from exercising their s.9(20) authority appropriately | ADR-0008 §3.1 + Compliance #7: the withdraw-confirm copy reads `"Withdraw recommendation. The linked action item will be archived. This action is recorded in the audit chain."` — no "are you sure," no "give up." Status-machine transitions are framed as record-keeping, not advocacy. The drafting form copy never discourages submission. Reviewed at S5 by the same rights-protective gate as 1.5 / 1.8 (per §3.13). Non-negotiable #7. | None material — copy is fixed in the route + UI; reviewer gate is the bound. |
| T-R36 | Tigris stores the signed ZIP bundle without `ServerSideEncryption` — the bundle (containing the signed PDF whose body decrypts to supervisor names and accommodation context) sits at rest in cleartext on Tigris (mirror of 1.8 priv-F1 close-out) | ADR-0008 §3.8: identical posture to 1.8 T-I40 close-out — `apps/api/src/evidence/tigris.ts` `buildPutObjectCommand` sets `ServerSideEncryption: 'AES256'` on the recommendation export PUT. The shared put-helper covers both kinds; no recommendation-specific bypass. Unit test asserts the SSE parameter is set on the recommendation export PUT. Non-negotiable #4 / #16. | Bucket-level default-encryption policy + Tigris lifecycle policy for `exports/*` deferred to 1.12 (mirror of 1.8 ops follow-up). |
| T-R37 | The route-level `expires_at = now() + 30 days` is the only TTL — without a Tigris bucket lifecycle policy, the cleartext-on-disk ZIPs survive past 30 days if the route-level cleanup misses them | ADR-0008 §3.8: `expires_at` is the primary TTL enforcer in 1.9 (same posture as 1.8 T-I40 close-out). The Tigris bucket lifecycle policy for `exports/<id>/*` is a 1.12 ops follow-up per the runbook. A 1.9 nightly sweep best-effort `DeleteObject`s any `export_records` row past `expires_at` (lands in S4). | Best-effort cleanup can miss; 1.12 bucket lifecycle is the structural close-out. Same residual shape as 1.8. |
| T-R38 | `evidence_files.linked_type` does not extend to `'recommendation'` in migration 0008 — the rep cannot attach evidence to a recommendation, leaving the polymorphic-FK ratchet's final value unconsumed (the 1.7 forward seam per `packages/shared-types/src/index.ts:260`) | ADR-0008 §3.13 + Consequences: migration 0008 opens `'recommendation'` at both the route allow-list AND the `evidence_files_linked_fk_guard` trigger in lockstep (same simultaneous-ratchet posture as 1.8 T-I14 for `'inspection_finding'`). Integration test asserts a `linkedType='recommendation' linkedId=<bogus uuid>` finalize call fails with 422 at the route, and a hand-crafted INSERT fails with 23514 at the trigger. Closes the fifth and final accepted `linkedType`. Non-negotiable #2. | None material — explicit ratchet; the runbook documents that future `linkedType` additions follow the same three-step recipe. |
| T-R39 | The retroactive `inspection_finding.read` audit kind leaves prior reads unanchored — 1.8 reads that decrypted findings before 1.9 deploy have no per-read chain rows, producing an apparent "gap" in the chain for findings accessed pre-1.9 | ADR-0008 §3.12: the `inspection_finding.read` kind is forward-only — pre-1.9 reads are bounded by the existing `inspection.created` + `inspection_finding.created` anchors (per 1.8 priv-F3 residual). The 1.9 runbook documents the discontinuity explicitly: post-1.9 finding reads carry per-read anchors; pre-1.9 reads are bounded by the 1.8 surface anchors and the step-up gate (which IS audited via `auth_events` → `audit_log` for the factor verification itself). No backfill of phantom anchors. Non-negotiable #2 — the chain is append-only. | Documented residual; the 1.8 T-AC2 phantom-row invariant (no inserted rows except via `append()`) is preserved. |
| T-R40 | The `responsible_party_user_id` migration on `inspection_findings` is data-destructive — adding the column drops the existing `responsible_party_ct` rows or breaks queries that expect the old shape | ADR-0008 §3.12: migration 0008 ADDs the `responsible_party_user_id uuid` column as nullable (no DEFAULT, no NOT NULL); the existing `responsible_party_ct` column is untouched. Pre-1.9 rows read as `responsible_party_user_id IS NULL + responsible_party_ct IS NOT NULL` per §3.12. New writes prefer `user_id` for internal owners; the encrypted-name path remains for external. CLAUDE.md "migrations are append-only" honored. Integration test loads a 1.8-era fixture, runs migration 0008, asserts every pre-1.9 row reads identically. | None material — additive migration, no UPDATE / DROP. |
| T-R41 | The `--check-inspections` flag on `audit-log-verify.ts` produces false positives — cross-referencing `inspection.exported` payloads against `export_records.output_sha256` flags legitimate rows because the comparison logic doesn't account for the 1.8 close-out's hash-replace pattern (T-I27) | ADR-0008 §3.12: the verifier reads `export_records.output_sha256` AS the canonical hash (the same value the chain anchor carries) — the 1.8 hash-replace is a one-pass operation; the stored `output_sha256` is what was anchored. The verifier does not re-render PDFs. Test fixture covers a known-good 1.8 export and asserts the verifier reports zero discrepancies. | None material — the verifier compares stored hash to stored hash. |
| T-R42 | A pathological response chain (>20 amendments) exceeds reasonable PDF render time, producing timeouts or memory pressure during signed export | ADR-0008 Risks: soft cap of 50 responses per recommendation, enforced at the route layer with 422 `response_cap_exceeded`. The cap is configurable per the runbook; the rationale (amendment-war pathological scenario) is documented. The renderer's response-appendix pass is bounded by the cap. | Cap is the bound; raising it is a deliberate config change. |
| T-R43 | Re-downloads of a recommendation export ZIP after the original `recommendation.exported` anchor leave no chain trail — a rep cannot prove "I downloaded it the day before I served it on the employer" (S5 sec-F2 close-out, mirror of T-R30) | The download handler emits a `recommendation.export.downloaded` chain anchor inside a db.transaction AFTER step-up clears AND Tigris fetch succeeds AND the TOCTOU verify (PDF hash + signature hash cross-checks per T-R45) passes AND BEFORE bytes return. Failed paths (401, 404, 410, SHA mismatch, signature mismatch, wrong_kind) do NOT anchor. PI-clean payload: `{exportId, recommendationId, downloadedByUserId}`. Mirror of the 1.8 `inspection.export.downloaded` retrofit. Integration test asserts the anchor fires on happy path AND does NOT fire on 401 / signature-mismatch paths. | None material — explicit ratchet. |
| T-R44 | Draft-state PATCH mutations on a recommendation leave no chain trail — a bad-faith rep can replace a citation while preserving the body wording, and the swap is invisible until export time (S5 sec-F4 close-out) | The PATCH handler computes `priorCitationsHash` from the existing `recommendation_citations` rows BEFORE any DELETE, then `newCitationsHash` from the new citation set AFTER INSERT (or the prior hash if citations are unchanged). Both hashes come from `computeCitationRowsHash` (a JOIN-free pure helper in `apps/api/src/recommendations/citations.ts` over the raw `(statute_code, clause_id, version_date, position)` triples). The `recommendation.draft_patched` chain row carries `{recommendationId, recommendationNumber, priorCitationsHash, newCitationsHash, bodyChanged}` — PI-clean. Emitted inside the PATCH transaction; failed PATCHes (404 / 422) do NOT anchor. `bodyChanged` is a boolean tracking whether the request included a `body` field (pragmatic — the route does not decrypt the existing body just to compare; the boolean is sufficient for the forensic surface the chain anchor records). Integration test asserts the anchor fires on citation-only change AND on body-only change. | None material — the union type in `packages/shared-types` is the structural backstop for the payload shape. |
| T-R45 | A Tigris-side attacker swaps the entire ZIP for a re-signed bundle (different signing key + recomputed manifest.pdfSha256 against the swapped PDF) — the manifest-PDF cross-check passes but the chain-anchored signing key id no longer matches what's in Tigris (S5 sec-F3 close-out) | The download handler extracts `signature.bin` from the ZIP alongside `manifest.json` and `recommendation.pdf`, computes `sha256(signatureBytes)`, and cross-checks against `export_records.signature_sha256` (the chain-anchored value). Mismatch returns 500 `export_signature_tamper_detected` with `reason: 'signature_sha_mismatch'`. The chain anchor's `signature_sha256` exists precisely to catch this — the SHA-256 cross-check is the cheap-and-correct close-out per the S5 reviewer. Full `crypto_sign_verify_detached` on every download is a 1.12 hardening item (runbook §11). The TOCTOU verify now spans THREE hashes (manifest's pdfSha256 == chain's outputSha256, observed PDF sha == chain's outputSha256, observed signature sha == chain's signature_sha256); any mismatch aborts before bytes return. Integration test simulates a tampered signature.bin in Tigris (mock) and asserts the 500. | Detection-only at the server; a 1.12 full crypto verify closes the structural gap. |

**Audit hooks for recommendations.** **Eleven** new event kinds added to `packages/shared-types` `AuditEventKind` (nine from ADR-0008 §3.13 S1 + two added in S5: `recommendation.draft_patched` and `recommendation.export.downloaded`). All payloads pass through the same typed-emit boundary as 1.3 priv-F2 — PI-clean by construction (IDs + hashes + counts + enums only, never names or free text):

- `recommendation.drafted` — `{recommendationId, jurisdiction}`. No title, no body. Emitted on draft create (the `recommendation.created` sub-state of `draft` per §3.1).
- `recommendation.draft_patched` (NEW S5) — `{recommendationId, recommendationNumber, priorCitationsHash, newCitationsHash, bodyChanged}`. PI-clean — two SHA-256 digests + a boolean. Emitted on every successful `PATCH /api/recommendations/:id` that mutated something (T-R44). The two hashes capture citation churn between PATCHes without exposing the citation text.
- `recommendation.submitted` — `{recommendationId, recommendationNumber, jurisdiction, citationCount, linkedActionItemId}`. No title, no body, no citation text. The `recommendationNumber` is the per-jurisdiction sequence (non-PI; identifies which Notice of Recommendation in the workplace's own series).
- `recommendation.response_captured` — `{recommendationId, responseId, position}`. No author role text, no body text. The `position` is the append index (§3.4).
- `recommendation.resolved` — `{recommendationId, linkedActionItemId, daysToResolve}`. Pairs with the action-items side's own `action_item.moved` anchor in the same transaction (§3.5).
- `recommendation.withdrawn` — `{recommendationId, linkedActionItemId?, fromStatus}`. No reason text (T-R34); reason is encrypted on the row. The `linkedActionItemId` is optional because withdrawal from `draft` has no linked action item (per §3.5).
- `recommendation.exported` — `{recommendationId, exportId, outputSha256, signatureSha256, byteSize, citationsHash, signingKeyId}`. The hashes are one-way integrity anchors; `citationsHash` is sha256 of the canonical-JSON of the resolved citations including each `body_hash` (§3.8) — this binds the exported PDF to the exact corpus state it was rendered against.
- `recommendation.export.downloaded` (NEW S5) — `{exportId, recommendationId, downloadedByUserId}`. PI-clean (T-R43 close-out, mirror of the 1.8 `inspection.export.downloaded` retrofit). Emitted on every successful re-download of a recommendation export ZIP after step-up + Tigris fetch + TOCTOU verify (PDF + signature) all pass.
- `inspection_finding.read` — `{findingId, inspectionId, readerUserId}`. PI-clean (§3.12 absorbs the 1.8 priv-F3 residual). Emitted on every successful `GET /api/inspections/findings/:id` after step-up.
- `inspection.export.downloaded` — `{exportId, downloaderUserId}`. PI-clean (§3.12 absorbs the 1.8 priv-F5 residual). Emitted on every re-download of an inspection export ZIP/PDF. The recommendation re-download path emits a structurally identical anchor scoped to the recommendation export (T-R30).
- `audit.workplace_signing_key.seeded` — `{signingKeyId, fingerprint, createdAt}`. Emitted by the first-run seed of the initial Ed25519 signing keypair (§3.7); a future 1.12 rotation will pair an `audit.workplace_signing_key.rotated` kind on the same template. The `fingerprint` is `SHA-256(public_key)` — a public, non-PI integrity anchor.

**Corpus-amendment invalidation is handled structurally, not by the recommendation surface.** A recommendation's citation rows pin to the exact `(statute_code, clause_id, version_date)` triple at submit time (T-R8); the corpus's append-only-version invariant (1.4 T-LC3 + T-LC5) guarantees that historical triple remains queryable forever; the signed PDF's footnote provenance and the chain anchor's `citationsHash` both encode that pinned state. A re-seed that publishes an amendment produces a different `citationsHash` on a fresh export of the same recommendation, and the chain records both — the original signed PDF remains verifiable against the historical clause row, and the verifier recipe (runbook) leads with "resolve `(statute_code, citation, version_date)` against the corpus, not the live active version."

### 2.10 Offline-first sync threats (Milestone 1.10)

Offline sync is the first surface that moves data through **three trust zones in one logical write**: the rep's untrusted-at-rest IndexedDB on a phone that can be lost, stolen, or seized; the `sync_queue` envelope that crosses the network when the bar returns; and the server-side `sync_idempotency` ledger + chain anchor that lands at queue-drain time, NOT at type-time. The threat surface is the union of 1.5–1.9 (every prior route is now offline-queueable and takes a `clientId` + `Idempotency-Key` + `If-Match` ratchet), plus four new surfaces: the local Dexie store that holds envelope-encrypted ciphertext + plaintext metadata for every entity, the queue retry curve + 48h dead-letter ceiling, the three-way merge conflict UI that requires step-up for encrypted fields, and the service worker that intercepts `/api/*` mutations to return synthetic 202 / 503 responses while offline. The most consequential semantic shift is on the chain anchor itself: the chain proves "server received this operation at time T," not "rep typed this at time T'" — the 21-day s.9(21) clock measures from server `submitted_at` (§3.12), and the runbook surfaces the arbitration framing. Every mitigation below cites the ADR-0009 subsection or the CLAUDE.md non-negotiable it implements.

| # | Threat | Mitigation | Residual |
|---|---|---|---|
| T-S1 | A rep's phone is lost, stolen, or seized — forensic dump of IndexedDB recovers rep-typed sensitive fields across hazards, action items, inspection findings, recommendations (CLAUDE.md #4) | **Honest stance (priv-F1 close-out, S5 fix bundle):** sensitive fields rep-typed offline (hazard descriptions, reporter identities, location detail, action item descriptions, recommended actions, raised-by, follow-up owner, recommendation titles + bodies, inspection observations, corrective actions, responsible party text, signature notes) sit as PLAINTEXT in IndexedDB on the rep's device — both in `sync_queue.payload` JSON and in the optimistic entity row's unsealed columns. The `workplace_keys_cache` table that was reserved for client-side sealed-box at-rest encryption is NOT populated in 1.10 (removed from the schema in the S5 fix bundle to avoid leaving misleading dead code). Full client-side envelope encryption requires refactoring every prior milestone's wire format to accept ciphertext (massive blast radius across 1.5–1.9) and is deferred to 1.12. Evidence captures ARE sealed under the workplace public key at capture time (1.7 sealed-box) so `evidence_pending_uploads._local_ciphertext_b64` remains ciphertext on the device — evidence captures are SAFER on the device than rep-typed drafts. The 1.12 hardening backlog (docs/runbooks/offline-sync.md §12) covers the structural fix: WebAuthn PRF / session-derived Dexie at-rest encryption that wraps the entire database transparently without changing wire formats. | The rep treats the device as carrying sensitive data; lost-device incident response is **revoke-the-session** per the auth runbook + cross-ref docs/runbooks/offline-sync.md §11 ("Lost or stolen device"). PIPEDA P10 self-notification may apply for data fitting the "real risk of significant harm" threshold; consult counsel. Until 1.12 lands the at-rest encryption, this is a known residual the rep is informed of via the runbook + the file-header comment in `apps/web/src/sync/db.ts`. |
| T-S2 | The same forensic dump recovers plaintext non-PI metadata — GPS coordinates on `evidence_files` local rows, entity ids, timestamps, status enums, severity, citation markers `[[cite:N]]`, recommendation numbers, `has_observation` / `has_corrective_action` booleans, queue-typed-at times, attempt counts — and the pattern-of-life leak (when the rep typed, where they were, which entity touched which) is a tracking surface independent of the encrypted bodies | ADR-0009 §3.1 + §"Negative tradeoffs" + **priv-F1 close-out update:** the metadata leakage is the documented tradeoff. The local projection shape mirrors the server's projection — no new plaintext field is introduced on the client that wasn't already projected on the server. GPS is capped at NUMERIC(8,4) (~11m, 1.7 T-E5) before it lands in the cache, so the cached coordinate set has the same resolution bound as Tigris. In 1.10 the rep-typed sensitive bodies are ALSO plaintext (see T-S1 honest stance); the metadata-vs-body distinction blurs until 1.12 lands at-rest encryption. The runbook (docs/runbooks/offline-sync.md §4 + §11) frames the rep's incident-response posture. | Pattern-of-life + rep-typed bodies both visible to a forensic adversary in 1.10; structural fix deferred to 1.12 per the §"Don't" guardrail. Documented in the runbook + the file-header comment in `apps/web/src/sync/db.ts`. |
| T-S3 | A future PR adds a convenience helper that caches decrypted plaintext in Dexie ("just for the active session, for performance"), breaking the never-persist-decrypted contract and turning the stolen-phone bound from ciphertext to plaintext | ADR-0009 §3.1: decrypted plaintext lives in JS heap memory only for the lifetime of a reveal view; it is NOT persisted to Dexie. The reveal route is always live-fetched from the server. The Dexie store's TypeScript shape exports no `*_pt` column on any entity table — the typechecker rejects a PR that tries to add one. The 1.7 sec-F9 close-out's `sodium.memzero` pattern carries over: the encrypt-write closes out the plaintext buffer on the queue-write path too (§3.2). | Type discipline is the bound; runtime check is deferred to 1.12 (same posture as 1.3 priv-F2 typed-emit boundary). |
| T-S4 | The queue retries on 5xx / network failure; without idempotency a retry that drained but failed to return the response (network blip on the response leg) double-writes — two hazards, two `position=2` response rows, two `action_item.moved` chain anchors for what is evidentially one move (CLAUDE.md #2) | ADR-0009 §3.4: `Idempotency-Key` middleware wired BEFORE auth, body, and rate-limit in `apps/api/src/index.ts` so a replay short-circuits BEFORE consuming auth or rate budget. The key is the queue's `payload_hash = sha256(canonical_json(payload))`. Cache hit returns the prior `response_status_code` + `response_body` verbatim WITHOUT re-running the handler — the chain anchor was emitted on the first run and is NOT re-emitted. The 1.7 `evidence.uploaded` + 1.6 `action_item.moved` + 1.9 `recommendation.submitted` chain anchors all preserve their once-per-logical-operation invariant. | Cross-machine drift: if the chain landed, the response was lost, AND the idempotency row was lost (e.g., DB restore from before the cache write), a replay re-emits. Bounded by the 48h dead-letter + the 7-day TTL window (T-S6); documented residual. |
| T-S5 | The middleware order is wrong on a future deploy (auth runs first) — a retry that lands on the idempotency cache still consumes the rep's auth-attempt budget + the per-IP rate-limit tokens; a malicious actor probes the cache by spamming keys, draining the rate limit for legitimate retries (ADR-0009 §3.4) | ADR-0009 §3.4 specifies the exact order in `apps/api/src/index.ts`: `csrfHeaderGuard()` → `idempotencyKeyGuard()` → `authMiddleware()` → `rateLimit()` → route handlers. The idempotency middleware short-circuits BEFORE auth on a cache hit. The cache lookup is keyed on `(key, user_id)` — an unauthenticated probe cannot hit a cached row because there's no `user_id`. Integration test asserts a replay returns the cached response without bumping `login_attempts` or the rate-limit token bucket. | A misconfigured middleware order would re-introduce the budget consumption; CI integration test is the bound. |
| T-S6 | `sync_idempotency` TTL is 7 days; a queue operation that survives a 48h dead-letter + manual rep intervention + a long network outage hits the cleared idempotency row 8+ days later, re-runs the handler, double-emits the chain anchor for an operation that already landed (ADR-0009 §3.4) | ADR-0009 §3.4: the 48h dead-letter ceiling (T-S10) is well inside the 7-day TTL window, so no operation drains via the queue worker past the TTL. The pathological case is a rep who manually retries a dead-letter row after >7 days — runbook covers this: the dead-letter UI surfaces the original `payload_hash`; a manual retry re-uses the same key; if the server has cleared the row, the handler re-runs. Single-tenant at single-co-chair scope makes this near-zero. The TTL sweep job is 1.12 (the table grows monotonically through 1.10); until then the practical TTL is effectively unbounded. | Documented residual; runbook §"Dead-letter recovery" covers it. |
| T-S7 | Two reps' devices (or one rep's two devices) edit the same hazard / action_item / inspection / recommendation; one drains first, the second's PATCH overwrites silently — the chain anchor records the second write as canonical, the first rep's edit vanishes with no conflict surface (CLAUDE.md #2) | ADR-0009 §3.7: every updatable entity table gains a server-side `version` integer (auto-incremented via trigger on UPDATE). PATCHes carry `If-Match: <etag>` where the etag is base64(`version`); server `SELECT version FOR UPDATE`, returns 409 `{error: 'version_conflict', server_version, server_state, base_version}` on mismatch. The client's queue worker writes a `sync_conflicts` row + flips `_sync_state='conflicting'`; the amber sync-status chip surfaces the conflict for manual resolution. A PATCH without `If-Match` returns 428 `precondition_required`. | The web client + queue worker always set `If-Match`; a hand-crafted unauthenticated client cannot bypass (auth gates the route). Integration test asserts a stale-etag PATCH returns 409. |
| T-S8 | The three-way merge UI loses the base state — Dexie eviction under quota pressure (or a fresh-install on a new device that doesn't have `_base_state`) degrades the merge to two-way; the rep can't see what they changed from, so "keep mine" silently overwrites a real edit the rep doesn't remember making (ADR-0009 §3.7) | ADR-0009 §3.7: `_base_state` is the snapshot of the row at last `clean`, written on every successful sync. On eviction (or on a device that never had the base), the conflict UI degrades gracefully to a two-column "yours vs theirs" diff with explicit copy: _"The base version is no longer available on this device. Compare your local state against the server's current state."_ The rep makes an informed choice; no silent merge. The chain anchors both pre- and post-resolution states (the PATCH that lands carries the merged result + a fresh `If-Match` matching the server's current version). | Two-way degradation is a UX bound, not a security bound; documented in the runbook. |
| T-S9 | The single-thread queue worker drains out of order — operation A (create finding) and operation B (promote that finding to action_item) race; B drains before A and the server FK fails because the finding doesn't exist yet (ADR-0009 §3.2) | ADR-0009 §3.2: the queue worker runs in the main thread (Dexie does not transfer across the structured-clone boundary; no Web Worker). Hot loop pulls batches of 10 rows ordered by `next_attempt_at` ASC then by `id` ASC (creation order); operations enqueued in causal order drain in causal order. A foreign-key failure at drain (race against a still-pending parent) marks the child as 5xx-retry, the parent drains on the next pass, the child retries successfully. The advisory-lock + transaction discipline from 1.6 T-AI5 + 1.9 T-R10 (per-section sequence allocation) is unchanged — the queue layer is plumbing, not provenance. | A bug in the queue worker that re-orders mid-batch would break causal order; covered by integration test (S4) that drains a finding-then-promote pair under simulated network flap. |
| T-S10 | A malicious server (or a misconfigured one) returns 503 to every drain attempt; the queue exhausts the backoff curve and rows land in the 48h dead-letter; the rep loses confidence that anything is syncing (ADR-0009 §3.2) | ADR-0009 §3.2: backoff curve is `[1s, 5s, 30s, 5min, 30min, 2h, 12h, 24h]` (pure function in `apps/web/src/sync/backoff.ts`); after 8 attempts (~48h) the row is `dead_letter = true`. The dead-letter UI in `apps/web/src/sync/sync-status-view.tsx` surfaces every row with the server's error code + a "retry" / "delete local" action. The amber paused chip is the rep's signal. The rep is the authority on recovery — the app does not auto-decide. | A rep who ignores the amber chip for >48h loses chain anchors on critical events (signed recommendations, signed inspections); the runbook covers operator-side dead-letter recovery for common error codes. |
| T-S11 | A `SyncOperation` is captured + replayed (e.g., via dev tools network log or a malicious browser extension); the server re-processes the operation and emits a duplicate chain anchor (CLAUDE.md #2) | ADR-0009 §3.4: every mutation carries `Idempotency-Key: <payload_hash>`. A replay hits the `sync_idempotency` cache and returns the cached response without re-emitting the chain anchor. The `(key, user_id)` cache key prevents a malicious replay from a different actor (a different rep with the same captured key is a different cache miss; the route still runs but the auth check rejects an unauthenticated replay; an authenticated replay from a different actor produces a different chain row with that actor's user_id — same shape as any legitimate write from that actor). | Same-actor replay is structurally one chain row; cross-actor replay produces a chain row attributed to the replaying actor — the chain captures the truth. Documented. |
| T-S12 | A buggy client RNG (or a deliberately-tampered dev-tools fingerprint) generates predictable `_local_id` UUID v4s that collide with existing rows; the server's 409 `id_collision` path is hit, but the rep's UI doesn't surface a clean recovery (ADR-0009 §3.3) | ADR-0009 §3.3: the server validates `clientId: z.string().uuid()` (rejects non-RFC-4122 strings); rejects duplicates with 409 `id_collision`. The client-side queue worker marks 409 `id_collision` as `dead_letter = true` (auto-retry would produce the same rejection) and the dead-letter UI prompts the rep to "regenerate id and retry" — a one-tap action that allocates a fresh `_local_id`, copies the local row's content to the new id, re-enqueues, and deletes the old conflicting row. 122 bits of entropy in a healthy RNG makes accidental collision ~0; a deliberately-tampered RNG is detected by the server's UNIQUE constraint. | A rep with a fully-compromised browser has many worse problems; documented. |
| T-S13 | A client supplies a `clientId` that doesn't match any `_local_id` in the local store — a hand-crafted forgery — and the server INSERTs the row with the forged id; the chain anchor binds whatever the client sent (ADR-0009 §3.3) | ADR-0009 §3.3: the server cannot distinguish a forged `clientId` from a legitimate device-generated one (both are UUID v4 strings). The mitigation is structural: the actor's `user_id` is bound by the auth cookie + the JWT, NOT by the client; the chain anchor records `actor_id = auth.userId` regardless of what `clientId` was supplied. A forged `clientId` therefore attributes a row to the actor who sent the request — same shape as any legitimate write. The multi-rep concern (a rep aliases another rep's id) is deferred to the multi-rep forward seam (1.5 T-H10 / 1.6 T-AI9 / 1.9 T-R21); single-co-chair scope makes this non-actionable in 1.10. | Multi-rep forward seam; documented. |
| T-S14 | A foreign-key write order race: operation A enqueues a finding with `inspection_id = <_local_id>`; operation B (create inspection) is enqueued AFTER A; the queue drains A first, the server FK fails (ADR-0009 §3.2 + §3.3) | ADR-0009 §3.2: the queue worker is single-thread and drains in enqueue order (`id ASC` within the same `next_attempt_at` window). Within a session a child create cannot be enqueued before its parent because the optimistic-UI flow requires the parent's `_local_id` to exist in Dexie before the child references it. A 5xx FK failure on a race (e.g., a rare ordering inversion from a manual cache poke) marks the child for retry; the parent drains, the child retries, the FK resolves. The 1.7 → 1.8 polymorphic FK ratchet posture (T-I14 / sec-F4) is unchanged — the route layer + the trigger validate at drain time. | Documented; integration test covers the inspection→finding chain. |
| T-S15 | The cached idempotency response carries `Set-Cookie` (a step-up grant, a session refresh) that no longer applies — a replay returns the cached headers and re-applies a stale grant (ADR-0009 §3.4) | ADR-0009 §3.4: the cached `response_body` is the JSON body only; `response_status_code` is the status; `Set-Cookie` headers are NOT cached. The idempotency-replay path returns the cached body + status but freshly minted (or absent) cookies from the current request context. Step-up grants live in the session JWT's claims (not in the response body) — a replay never re-grants step-up. Auth refresh has its own dedicated route which is NOT queueable (per §3.6 "require-online" list), so no auth-lifecycle response is ever cached. | None material — the cache is body+status only. |
| T-S16 | Payload-hash collision: the queue's `payload_hash` doesn't include `action_kind` + `entity_local_id` + `actor_id`, so two structurally-different operations could collide on body alone (ADR-0009 §3.4) | ADR-0009 §3.4: `payload_hash = sha256(canonical_json(payload))` where the canonical payload includes the action kind, the route, the body fields, and (server-side) the `(key, user_id)` cache key. The middleware cross-checks `payload_hash` on cache hit — if the rep replays the same key with a different body (extremely unlikely; the queue derives the key from the body), the middleware returns 409 `idempotency_key_payload_mismatch` rather than the cached response. Defense against a future bug in key derivation. | SHA-256 collision probability is negligible; the cross-check is the defense against a derivation bug. |
| T-S17 | An endpoint claimed "queueable" actually needs a server-side capability that can't run offline — e.g., the action_item per-section sequence allocation needs `pg_advisory_xact_lock` at drain time, but the queue serializes the lock acquisition into a single drained insert (ADR-0009 §3.6) | ADR-0009 §3.2 + §3.6: the queue worker is single-thread; the lock allocation happens server-side at drain time inside the route's transaction (same shape as 1.6 T-AI5 sequence allocation). The optimistic UI shows "Action item #pending" until the drain completes; the canonical sequence number lands when the chain anchor fires. The `recommendation_number` allocation (1.9 T-R10) uses the same pattern. Integration test asserts a queued create with a pending sequence drains correctly and the chain anchor carries the allocated number. | The optimistic-UI "pending" state is the rep-visible bound; documented in §3.12 copy. |
| T-S18 | A `reveal` endpoint is queued accidentally (a UI bug calls the typed client's queue path for a GET-decrypt) — the queue stores the reveal request, replays it on network return, and the rep is shown stale-at-best plaintext (ADR-0009 §3.6) | ADR-0009 §3.6 + §3.9: the service worker classifies routes; every `reveal` / decrypt route is in the "require-online" list. An offline call returns a synthetic 503 `network_required` body — the SW does NOT enqueue. The typed client's read-path also bypasses the queue (reads are not mutations; the SW only queues mutations). A UI bug that calls the queue path for a reveal hits a route Zod schema that doesn't accept queued reveals — the queue worker would dead-letter on 400. Integration test asserts a `GET /api/recommendations/:id/reveal` while offline returns synthetic 503 + the UI shows "Network required." | UI bound; the SW's classification is the defense. |
| T-S19 | A PDF export is attempted offline — the rep taps "Export" expecting it to queue, the SW returns synthetic 503, the rep tries again offline and sees the same error (ADR-0009 §3.6 + CLAUDE.md #16) | ADR-0009 §3.6: PDF exports are require-online (step-up + workplace private key + server-side render + Tigris SSE PUT + signed-bundle assembly — none of these have offline analogues). The SW returns synthetic 503 `network_required` and the UI shows a "Network required to export" banner per §3.11. The rep cannot accidentally bypass step-up + the chain anchor by queueing an export. CLAUDE.md #16 (step-up + audit on every export) is preserved structurally. | UX bound; the runbook covers the rep-facing framing. |
| T-S20 | A recommendation `submit` is queued offline; the rep believes the 21-day s.9(21) clock starts when they typed at 10:14am; the queue drains at 02:47am the next day and the chain anchor records `submitted_at = 02:47am`; the rep miscounts the deadline by the queue-delay window and misses the response window (CLAUDE.md #2 + ADR-0009 §3.12) | ADR-0009 §3.12: the optimistic submit view shows _"Recommendation submitted (pending sync). 21-day clock starts on sync."_ When the queue drains, the view updates to _"Recommendation submitted 02:47am on 2026-06-03. 21 days remaining. Response due by 2026-06-24."_ The chain anchor's `submitted_at` is the canonical legal timestamp; `computeRecommendationDeadline` (1.9 T-R10) is a pure function in `packages/shared-types` that reads from server-stamped `submitted_at`. The runbook documents the OHSA s.9(21) legal reasoning — the clock starts when the rep delivers to management, which is structurally after the queue drains. | Rep discipline is the bound on miscounting before the drain copy updates; documented. |
| T-S21 | An inspection signature is captured offline at 10am; the queue drains at 8pm; the chain anchor records 8pm as the signature time; in arbitration the signature's "when" diverges from the rep's reality (CLAUDE.md #2 + ADR-0009 §3.6) | ADR-0009 §3.2 + §3.6: the chain anchor binds the SERVER's `now()`, which is when the operation actually landed in the canonical record. The local Dexie row carries `_local_created_at` (the rep's device clock) as a UI-only hint, NOT as evidence. The runbook documents the arbitration framing: the chain proves server-receipt time; the rep can produce queue-typed-at via their device-side `created_at` column on the queue row + corroborating evidence (location, witnesses), but the chain is the canonical evidentiary surface. Non-negotiable #2 — every chain row's `ts_ms` is server-side and tamper-evident. | Two timestamps in evidence (queue-typed-at + chain `ts_ms`); arbitration adjudicators are guided by the runbook. |
| T-S22 | The reveal endpoint plaintext is cached in Dexie by a misconfigured background refresh — a list-view refresh fetches `/api/recommendations` and the response carries some decrypted preview field that lands in Dexie (ADR-0009 §3.1 + §3.5) | ADR-0009 §3.1: list projections from the server are non-PI metadata only (status enums, ids, timestamps, citation markers, `has_observation` booleans). No reveal-decrypt response is ever cached by the SW (§3.9 — `decrypt` URLs are explicitly excluded from cache). The background-refresh path (§3.5) writes to Dexie only the same shape as the server's list projection — no plaintext bodies. TypeScript shape rejects a list-row with a `*_pt` field at the typechecker boundary. | Type discipline + SW exclusion list are the defenses; same as T-S3. |
| T-S23 | A list view reads from Dexie and renders a stale row; the rep makes a decision (promote a finding, withdraw a recommendation) based on stale data; the chain anchor records the decision but the rep's reality was a different state (ADR-0009 §3.5) | ADR-0009 §3.5: every read fires a background refresh; the conflict-resolution model (T-S7) catches a divergent state at write time via `If-Match`. The PATCH carrying the rep's decision includes the etag the rep saw on Dexie; if the server has moved forward, the 409 surfaces and the conflict UI lets the rep re-decide against fresh state. The chain anchor never records a write that was based on a now-impossible state because the version check is server-side. | Stale reads inform a rep's choice but cannot land an inconsistent write; documented. |
| T-S24 | Local cache poisoning via XSS — a malicious script in the page writes garbage to Dexie; the next read returns garbage; an authenticated rep with their own factors writes the garbage back to the server, attributing it to themselves in the chain (CLAUDE.md #2) | ADR-0009 §3.1 + §3.9: the strict CSP from 1.2 §"Headers & Transport" + the 1.4 sec-F1 close-out (no `dangerouslySetInnerHTML`, strict XSS pre-filter on all user-supplied text in the legal corpus + 1.5–1.9 fields) bound the XSS surface. The SW's same-origin scope prevents a cross-origin script from registering itself. A successful XSS that writes garbage to Dexie is an XSS-class problem with the same posture as any session-bound exfil — the rep's session is the bound, not the cache. The chain anchor records the actor's intent (the actor whose session signed the request) regardless of cache poisoning. | XSS-class residual; same bound as the rest of the app. |
| T-S25 | A `_sync_state = 'clean'` row diverges from the server silently — the background refresh failed (network error, server 500, SW cache stale) and the rep reads from the local-stale row indefinitely (ADR-0009 §3.5) | ADR-0009 §3.5: background refresh fires on view mount, window focus, every successful drain, pull-to-refresh, and manual sync. A refresh failure logs to the sync-status chip's "last refresh failed" hint; the chip stays green only when the last refresh succeeded. The 30-second poll while online + non-empty queue (§3.2) catches a network blip; a stuck refresh moves the chip to "Offline" within one poll window. | Documented; the sync-status chip is the rep-facing signal. |
| T-S26 | Workplace public key has rotated between offline-capture and finalize; the rep's offline-typed body is encrypted under the OLD key; the server's finalize rejects at the 1.7 sec-F5 active-key check (ADR-0009 §3.8 + 1.7 sec-F5) | ADR-0009 §3.8: the workplace public key is cached in the SW (§3.9); cache refresh on every successful sync. A rotation produces a new `workplaceKeyId`; the rep's first online connection refreshes the cache; further offline-capture happens under the new key. The pathological window is "rotation happens during an offline session that started before rotation" — the queue's finalize call hits 422 `workplace_key_retired`, the queue marks `dead_letter = true`, the dead-letter UI prompts the rep to "re-capture under fresh key" (the original ciphertext on the device is re-encrypted under the new public key + re-enqueued). The 1.12 rotation script (1.7 T-E8) seals the structural gap. | A rep offline through a rotation must re-capture; documented in the runbook's KEK rotation procedure. |
| T-S27 | The three-step evidence upload (presign → PUT → finalize) leaves orphan ciphertext in Tigris when finalize fails (mirror of 1.7 T-E11 / sec-F11 orphan ciphertext, made worse by per-step queue retries) (ADR-0009 §3.8) | ADR-0009 §3.8: the three steps are one `sync_queue` row with an internal `step` counter; a failure at step (c) finalize retries finalize (not re-PUTs the ciphertext). Tigris-side orphans (PUT succeeded, finalize never landed) inherit the same residual as 1.7 — the 1.12 nightly orphan-sweep script reaps them via `evidence_files` left-join `Tigris ListObjects`. Until 1.12, an orphan is bounded by the bucket-side `expires_at` lifecycle policy (1.8 sec-F6 close-out + 1.7 sec-F11 inline comment).
