The chain anchor never fires for an orphaned upload — `evidence.uploaded` is emitted inside the finalize transaction after the row insert. | Documented; runbook §8 covers the cleanup follow-up. |
| T-S28 | Plaintext capture buffer lifetime in the offline encrypt+queue path is longer than the 1.7 sec-F9 close-out promises — the encrypt-then-queue is slower than encrypt-then-network and the plaintext bytes live longer in JS heap (ADR-0009 §3.8 + 1.7 sec-F9) | ADR-0009 §3.8: the encrypt call is the only consumer of plaintext bytes; immediately after `crypto_box_seal` returns, the plaintext buffer is `sodium.memzero`'d (same shape as 1.7 sec-F9). The queue write takes the ciphertext only — `sync_queue.payload_ct` carries the sealed bytes; `_local_ciphertext_b64` on the evidence row is the same sealed bytes. The queue-write latency does not extend plaintext lifetime; the zero happens before the queue insert. Integration test (S4) spy-counts `memzero` calls against the capture count. | Same bound as 1.7 sec-F9; Bun GC copy-before-zero is the residual. |
| T-S29 | The `_local_ciphertext_b64` field carries the same sealed-box envelope as Tigris-side ciphertext; a forensic dump that recovers it has the same posture as a Tigris compromise — but the local field also reveals which evidence has been captured but not yet uploaded, leaking timing of capture (ADR-0009 §3.8) | ADR-0009 §3.8: `_local_ciphertext_b64` is deleted from the Dexie row immediately after the finalize step lands successfully (the ciphertext is now on Tigris; keeping a local copy is unnecessary disk pressure). Pre-drain captures retain the local ciphertext; this is structurally the same posture as Tigris-side ciphertext (1.7 T-E1). Capture timing is part of the metadata leak (T-S2) — accepted residual. | Same bound as T-S1 / T-S2; documented. |
| T-S30 | A compromised CI pipeline ships a poisoned service worker — the SW intercepts every `/api/*` mutation and exfiltrates the (encrypted) queue payloads or rewrites them under an attacker-controlled key (ADR-0009 §3.9 + CLAUDE.md #3) | ADR-0009 §3.9: the SW is generated by `vite-plugin-pwa` at build time; the generated `sw.js` is build-hash-addressed; the source for the SW is in-repo. CI is the supply-chain bound — the same posture as any front-end build. The queue payloads are sealed under the workplace public key; even a poisoned SW that exfiltrates the queue ciphertext gets only sealed bytes (workplace private key on the server). A poisoned SW that rewrites the queue under an attacker-controlled public key would produce ciphertext the server cannot decrypt — finalize 422s, the chain anchor doesn't fire. CI integrity is governed by the existing pre-merge controls (gitleaks, pnpm audit, lockfile review, no analytics SDKs). | Supply-chain bound — same as the rest of the app. |
| T-S31 | The SW serves a stale app shell indefinitely while the rep stays offline — a critical security fix shipped yesterday is not on the device; the rep operates on a known-vulnerable bundle (ADR-0009 §3.9) | ADR-0009 §3.9: `vite-plugin-pwa` defaults include `skipWaiting + clientsClaim` and a `controllerchange` UI toast on bundle change. While the rep stays offline they cannot fetch the new bundle — the stale shell is the bound. Online return triggers the SW update; the toast surfaces "Update available" within seconds. The runbook covers force-refresh and the bundle-version check (the `GET /api/health` response carries the expected client version; a mismatch dumps the rep to a forced reload). 1.12 absorbs the SW rotation procedure for KEK rotation events. | Documented residual; online return closes the window. |
| T-S32 | The legal corpus cached in the SW is stale (the corpus was amended overnight; the rep drafts a recommendation offline citing a clause that's been retired) (ADR-0009 §3.9 + 1.4 T-LC3) | ADR-0009 §3.9: legal corpus has a 24h TTL OR per-session refresh whichever sooner; the SW catches new versions on background-refresh. The 1.9 T-R8 corpus-amendment-invalidation behavior is the server-side gate — at submit time the route re-validates the citation triple against the live corpus and rejects retired versions with `citation_not_in_corpus`. A rep who drafts offline against a retired clause hits this 422 at drain time; the dead-letter UI surfaces the rejection + the rep updates the citation. The 1.4 T-LC5 append-only-version invariant guarantees historical triples remain queryable for legitimate pinned citations. | Wasted drafting time is the bound, not a chain-of-custody issue; documented. |
| T-S33 | Tigris cross-origin PUTs are not intercepted by the SW; a malicious browser extension intercepts the cross-origin PUT and exfiltrates ciphertext or substitutes a different blob (ADR-0009 §3.8 step b + §3.9) | ADR-0009 §3.8 + §3.9: SW scope is the app origin only; Tigris PUTs are foreground `fetch` from the queue worker. The presign URL is 5-min TTL (1.7 T-E9); the finalize step verifies `ciphertext_sha256` against what the legitimate browser computed — a substituted blob fails the SHA-256 cross-check and finalize 422s. A browser-extension-class attack has the same posture as 1.7 T-E9 + T-E14 (the `X-Requested-With` header gate). | Same bound as 1.7 evidence upload; the SHA verification is the integrity anchor. |
| T-S34 | The synthetic 202 response for offline mutations confuses the typed API client — a route handler downstream of the client expects 200/201 only and the offline-write path silently fails (ADR-0009 §3.9 follow-on) | ADR-0009 §3.9: the typed client is wrapped to treat 202 as "queued, not committed" — the response body carries the optimistic local row + a `queued: true` flag. Integration test asserts every prior 1.5–1.9 route's client wrapper handles 202; the type system rejects a consumer that destructures the response as if it were 200/201. The SW's synthetic 202 body matches the schema the route returns on a real 201 (id + the optimistic state) so the UI renders the optimistic row identically. | None material — type system + integration test are the defense. |
| T-S35 | The synthetic 503 body returned by the SW for require-online endpoints leaks payload that mimics a real server response (the UI confuses real 503 from a server outage with synthetic 503 from offline) (ADR-0009 §3.9 follow-on + §3.11) | ADR-0009 §3.9: synthetic 503 carries `{error: 'network_required', source: 'service-worker'}` — the `source` field disambiguates from a real server 503. The UI's "Network required" banner reads the `source` field; a real 503 surfaces a different "Server unavailable" banner. The chain anchor never sees a synthetic 503 (the request never left the device). | None material — explicit body disambiguation. |
| T-S36 | The SW's stored request replay (the queued operation) omits the `X-Requested-With: jhsc-web` CSRF header from 1.7 sec-F2 / T-E14, opening the queued operation to passive cross-origin element loaders at replay time (ADR-0009 §3.9 follow-on + 1.7 sec-F2) | ADR-0009 §3.9: the SW stores the full request including all headers when queueing; the replay reconstructs the request with the original headers + injects the `Idempotency-Key`. The `X-Requested-With` header is preserved. Integration test asserts a queued POST replayed at drain time carries `X-Requested-With: jhsc-web`. The SW does NOT serve `<img src>` / `<iframe src>` from the queue — only same-origin `fetch` from the typed client paths enqueue. | None material — header preservation is part of the queue contract. |
| T-S37 | PWA install prompt phishing — a malicious overlay on a same-origin page mimics the native install prompt to capture credentials (ADR-0009 §3.10) | ADR-0009 §3.10: Chrome's native `beforeinstallprompt` dialog is browser-chrome (unspoofable from page content); iOS has no programmatic install at all — the rep follows the share-sheet → Add to Home Screen flow which is OS-chrome. A page-level overlay cannot replicate browser chrome. The app's "Install" button is text + a Lucide icon (no marketing flourish per CLAUDE.md #10); the click triggers the native prompt (Android) or a documentary modal (iOS). Documented as low-risk. | Browser-chrome bound; same as any PWA. |
| T-S38 | PWA-installed-mode permission scope diverges from browser-tab — camera permission persists longer in PWA mode and a rep grants once, subsequent unprompted captures fire (ADR-0009 §3.10) | ADR-0009 §3.10: this is OS-level permission semantics, not actionable in our code. The capture-to-record button shows a permission-state indicator (Lucide camera icon + a small status dot) so the rep can see whether camera is granted. The 1.7 evidence capture flow's "capture happens in-page, not via OS picker" (1.7 T-E4) is unchanged — the camera permission is the rep's grant, not an OS-picker auto-routing. | OS-level semantics; documented in the runbook. |
| T-S39 | Sync chip false-Synced — the chip reads from local state and shows "Synced" while 5 operations are in flight; the rep believes everything is safe and powers down the phone (ADR-0009 §3.11) | ADR-0009 §3.11: chip state machine reads from Dexie's `_sync_state` aggregate (counts of `dirty_*` + `conflicting` + dead-letter rows). "Synced" requires ZERO non-clean rows AND the queue worker is idle AND the last health probe succeeded. Operations in flight keep the chip on "Syncing" until the response lands AND the entity row is marked clean in the same transaction (Dexie + queue row delete are one Dexie transaction). The 30-second poll catches a stuck worker. | None material — the chip is read-from-Dexie atomic with the drain. |
| T-S40 | Pull-to-refresh DoS — a rep mashes the refresh trigger; the queue worker fires multiple concurrent drains; two drains race the same queue row, sending the operation twice (ADR-0009 §3.2 + §3.11) | ADR-0009 §3.2: the queue worker is single-thread + has a `running` flag that short-circuits concurrent invocations — a second pull-to-refresh while a drain is in flight is a no-op. The hot loop's `SELECT … LIMIT 10` + per-row processing is sequential. Even if a duplicate fire happened, the idempotency middleware (T-S4) catches the same `payload_hash` on the server. Integration test asserts ten concurrent pull-to-refresh fires produce exactly one drain pass. | None material — single-thread + idempotency are belt-and-suspenders. |
| T-S41 | A rep ignores the dead-letter UI for >48h after a critical operation (signed recommendation, signed inspection) lands in dead-letter; the chain anchor never fires and the operation is evidentially lost (ADR-0009 §3.11 + CLAUDE.md #2) | ADR-0009 §3.11: dead-letter rows surface in the sync-status chip's amber "Paused" state with the count of conflicts + dead-letter rows. Tap-to-open shows each row with the server's error code + a "retry" / "fix" / "delete local" action. The rep is the authority on recovery. For signed operations (recommendation submit, inspection signature), the local Dexie row carries the rep-trusted signature data + ciphertext; a rep who needs to recover the operation has the bytes — they can copy the body into a fresh draft + re-submit. The runbook covers common error codes (citation_marker_density_violation, citation_not_in_corpus, signatures_incomplete, idempotency_key_payload_mismatch) and the operator-side recovery procedure. | Rep discipline is the bound; the chain captures only what actually landed, by design (non-negotiable #2). |
| T-S42 | The per-route `clientId` + `Idempotency-Key` + `If-Match` ratchet is incomplete — one POST route in 1.5–1.9 doesn't honor `clientId`, the offline-write path for that entity silently fails (the optimistic local id is server-overwritten on drain, breaking FK references in dependent local rows) (ADR-0009 §3.13) | ADR-0009 §3.13 S2: every existing POST handler is ratcheted in the same slice; the route-table in §3.3 enumerates the nine handlers that take `clientId`. Integration tests assert that for each route, a POST with `clientId` returns a row with `id = clientId`; a POST without `clientId` still works (Zod `.optional()`). The CI lint rule (1.6 sec-F3 pattern) catches a new POST handler that doesn't import the `clientIdSchema`. | A future POST handler that forgets the ratchet is caught by the lint rule + the integration test. |
| T-S43 | The new `sync_idempotency` migration runs out of order with the 1.5–1.9 route ratchets — production deploys the route changes before the table exists, idempotency middleware crashes on every request (ADR-0009 §3.13) | ADR-0009 §3.13 S1 + S2: the migration lands in S1 (Dexie schema + migration 0009 + the `version` column on every updatable entity table); S2 wires the middleware + the route ratchets AFTER the migration is in place. CLAUDE.md "migrations are append-only" honored. The deploy sequence is migrations → API binary → web bundle; the middleware gracefully no-ops on missing `Idempotency-Key` header (GET/HEAD too) so a stale client during the deploy window is fine. | Deploy sequencing is the bound; documented in the runbook. |
| T-S44 | A Dexie schema migration between app versions (1.10 → 1.11 / Excel imports) loses an in-flight queued operation because the migration drops or renames a column that the queued payload references (ADR-0009 §3.1 + CLAUDE.md "migrations are append-only") | ADR-0009 §3.1: Dexie schema follows the same append-only posture as the server migrations — `db.version(N).stores({...}).upgrade(tx => ...)` adds tables and columns; existing schemas remain valid. A queued operation's `payload_ct` is opaque ciphertext addressed by `payload_hash`; the queue worker doesn't introspect it. A schema bump that renames a Dexie table (which the ADR doesn't do) would migrate the queue's `table` column via the upgrade hook. The 1.10 → 1.11 path is a v2 schema add (Excel import tables), not a rename. | Append-only discipline is the bound; documented. |
| T-S45 | First-run cannot complete offline — the workplace KEK + signing key bootstrap is server-side; a rep installing the PWA on a fresh device with no network is stuck (ADR-0009 §3.6 + 1.2 T-A11) | ADR-0009 §3.6 + §"Require-online": all `/api/auth/*` routes (passkey verify, password verify, TOTP verify, recovery codes, first-run, session refresh — except `/session` which is cached for returning reps) are require-online. The first-run flow shows a clear "Network required to set up the app" banner. A returning rep with a valid cached session can boot to the app shell + Dexie cache offline; a fresh install cannot. The runbook covers the first-run requirement. | Documented; no security gap — the offline-first promise is for ongoing use, not bootstrap. |
| T-S46 | Three concurrent retry curves at play — per-mutation backoff (1s→24h), per-evidence-upload three-step retry, per-session-token JWT refresh — interact pathologically (e.g., a refresh failure during a drain leaves the queue stuck on 401 with no recovery) (ADR-0009 §3.2 + §3.8 + 1.2 §3) | ADR-0009 §3.2: a queue 401 is treated as session-expired; the queue worker pauses (no more drain attempts), the UI surfaces "Session expired — sign in to resume sync" in the chip, the rep re-authenticates (online), the access JWT refreshes, the queue resumes from the same backoff cursor (the `attempt_count` is NOT incremented by a 401 — only by 5xx / network). The session refresh path itself is require-online (§3.6); a failure there is a separate UX flow. Evidence-upload three-step retry interacts only with its own `step` counter — the per-mutation backoff curve covers the overall row. Integration test asserts a 401 mid-drain pauses cleanly + resumes after re-auth. | Documented; the three curves are decoupled by status code. |
| T-S47 | The chain anchor's timestamp diverges from the rep's reality across every queued operation, producing two timestamps in evidence (chain `ts_ms` + queue-typed-at on the device clock) — an arbitration adjudicator unfamiliar with the offline-first posture may attribute the divergence to tampering (CLAUDE.md #2 + ADR-0009 §3.2) | ADR-0009 §3.2 + §3.12 + Consequences: the runbook documents the chain-anchor latency contract explicitly — the chain proves "the server received this at time T," NOT "the rep typed this at time T'." The dead-letter UI and the sync-status view both surface the queue-typed-at hint from `sync_queue.created_at` (device clock) so the rep can produce it as a separate timeline if needed. The chain is the canonical evidentiary surface; the device clock is corroborating context. Arbitration adjudicators are guided by the runbook §"Chain-anchor latency framing." | Documented; the runbook is the arbitration-side resource. |
| T-S48 | A `recommendation.submit` conflict on two offline devices produces two chain anchors for what is evidentially the same recommendation; the resolution path emits a `recommendation.withdrawn` chain row for the duplicate, leaving TWO chain rows for one logical submission (ADR-0009 §3.7 + 1.9 T-R20) | ADR-0009 §3.7: the chain captures both — the duplicate submit AND the withdrawal of the duplicate. The runbook frames this as the correct evidentiary surface: the rep submitted twice (intentionally or not), and the chain records both events truthfully. The 1.9 T-R20 single-co-chair scope makes this near-zero in practice. The audit-log-verify cross-check (1.3 T-AC1) catches any tampering with either chain row. | Documented; near-zero in single-co-chair scope. |
| T-S49 | A conflict on encrypted text requires step-up to view both versions; a rep without recent step-up cannot resolve and the operation stays in `sync_conflicts` indefinitely (ADR-0009 §3.7 + §3.8) | ADR-0009 §3.7 + §3.8: the conflict UI for encrypted fields fires the existing reveal endpoints (`POST /api/sync-conflicts/:id/reveal` with `{which: 'local'|'server'|'base'}`); each reveal is step-up gated (same shape as 1.5 T-H4 / 1.8 T-I12 / 1.9 T-R26). The rep must be online + step-up-fresh to resolve. The amber chip surfaces the conflict count; an unresolved conflict has no impact on the rest of the app — the rep can keep working on other entities. The new `sync_conflict.revealed` chain kind anchors each reveal (CLAUDE.md #2). | Operational — a rep without step-up can't resolve, but the conflict doesn't decay or auto-merge. Documented. |
| T-S50 | The rep's device clock is set wrong — the `sync_queue.created_at` (device clock) is hours or days off; the dead-letter UI hint is misleading; an arbitration timeline derived from device clock is wrong (ADR-0009 §3.2 + Risks) | ADR-0009 Risks: the chain anchor `ts_ms` is server-side and unaffected by device clock skew — the canonical evidentiary timestamp is correct regardless. The device clock skew shows up only on the rep-facing UI hint (queue-typed-at) and is a known limitation. The runbook covers the framing: "the chain is canonical; the device clock is rep-facing only." | Server-side timestamps are the bound; documented. |
| T-S51 | Service worker NetworkFirst caches step-up-gated reveal responses indefinitely — a rep who once revealed evidence E1 under fresh step-up has E1's plaintext stored in CacheStorage. They lose network, re-navigate to the evidence view, the SW's NetworkFirst path times out + falls back to the cached response, returns plaintext binary WITHOUT a fresh step-up check AND WITHOUT a new `evidence.read` chain anchor (sec-F1, ADR-0009 §3.9 + CLAUDE.md #2 + #16) | **sec-F1 close-out (S5 fix bundle):** the SW's `REQUIRE_ONLINE_PATTERNS` check moved OUTSIDE the `if(isMutation)` branch — every reveal / export / download GET is now network-only with synthetic 503 `network_required` on offline. Workbox's `CacheableResponsePlugin` ignores `Cache-Control: no-store`; the require-online gate is the upstream defense that prevents reveal plaintext from ever entering the SW cache. The fix preserves CLAUDE.md #2 (chain-of-custody on every reveal) + CLAUDE.md #16 (step-up gating on every export) + the never-persist-decrypted contract from T-S3 / T-S22. | No residual — the require-online gate is structural; a future reveal endpoint added without an updated `REQUIRE_ONLINE_PATTERNS` line would route through the SW cache, but priv-F8 documents that brittleness + the 1.12 hardening backlog covers the smoke-test that walks every server route + asserts coverage. |
| T-S52 | Cache-INSERT error swallow + chain anchor double-emit window — a transient Postgres error on the idempotency cache INSERT was silently swallowed; a retry of the same Idempotency-Key re-ran the handler; if the chain anchor logic relied solely on the idempotency cache to prevent re-emit, the chain anchor double-fired (sec-F2 + sec-F8, ADR-0009 §3.4) | **sec-F2 + sec-F8 close-out (S5 fix bundle):** the cache-INSERT failure is now logged at warn level instead of swallowed. The chain-anchor double-emit concern is bounded by the entity-table UNIQUE on every chain-anchored route: `evidence_files` storage_key + plaintext_sha256 content-address, `action_item_moves` audit_idx UNIQUE, `recommendation_number` per-jurisdiction sequence under advisory lock, `inspection_signatures(inspection_id, role)` UNIQUE, `inspection_findings(inspection_id, item_key)` UNIQUE. A retry that re-runs the handler hits the entity-table UNIQUE first and the route maps the collision to its clientId-reuse 200 — same shape as the cache hit would have produced. The warn log is the operational signal that the dedupe window degraded. | The retry-window degradation is the rep-visible bound; the chain anchor invariant is preserved structurally. Documented in the runbook §3 + the middleware doc-comment. |
| T-S53 | Conflict resolution dialog Apply path is structurally broken — endpoint mapping was wrong (action_item_move POSTed /move vs server's /moves; finding_promotion POSTed /findings/:id vs /promote; evidence_finalize POSTed /finalize vs /; withdraw-duplicate didn't exist); raw `_sync_*` metadata leaked into PATCH bodies that hit `.strict()` Zod schemas; the encrypted-field Reveal dispatched step-up but never fetched plaintext (priv-F4 + sec-F3 + sec-F4 + sec-F6, ADR-0009 §3.7) | **priv-F4 + sec-F3 + sec-F4 + sec-F6 close-out (S5 fix bundle, per user authorization):** the Apply path is DISABLED in 1.10 and ships in 1.12. The 1.10 dialog ships VIEW-ONLY — three-way merge columns (Yours / Theirs / Base) render so the rep can compare plaintext metadata; encrypted-field rows render the honest "Apply pipeline ships in 1.12 — contact your operator" placeholder (no Reveal button, no step-up dispatch for a no-op); the Apply button is disabled with the label `Apply (1.12)`; an operator-script notice points the rep at `docs/runbooks/offline-sync.md §7`. The broken `defaultEndpointForKind` map + `chainWithdrawalKind` + the resolution-submission code (`applyResolution`) + the per-field manual-merge picker were removed entirely (the dead code invited a future PR to silently re-enable the broken pipeline; the file-comment documents the 1.12 implementer's checklist). | Conflicts in 1.10 require operator-side resolution per the runbook §7 (inspect Dexie row + UPDATE the server row + clear the client). The 1.12 Apply pipeline lands the in-app self-serve path. Single-co-chair single-tenant scope makes operator intervention frequency near-zero. Documented. |
| T-S54 | Inspection signature flow has no offline-clock notice — a signature captured offline at 10am that drains at 8pm has a chain anchor of 8pm; the rep believes the chain records 10am; in arbitration the signature's "when" diverges from the rep's reality (priv-F3, ADR-0009 §3.12 + T-S21) | **priv-F3 close-out (S5 fix bundle):** `OfflineSignatureTimestampNotice` (`apps/web/src/components/inspection-signature-sheet.tsx`) renders when the rep's `sync_queue` has a pending `inspection_signature` op for the current inspection. Copy: "This signature will be recorded on the server when you're back online. The chain of custody timestamp will be the SERVER's receive time, NOT the moment you signed. For arbitration, your device's clock-time is your record; the chain proves server-receipt." Mirrors the recommendation OfflineSubmitClockNotice for the signature flow (signatures are MORE evidentially weighty than recommendation submits — a recommendation can be re-submitted; a signature is a one-shot legal act tied to identity + role + immutable template version pin). Rights-protective tone per CLAUDE.md #7 (no shame, no anxiety-induce). | Rep informed-consent surface is the bound; runbook §10 + ADR §3.12 frame the arbitration record. |
| T-S55 | POST create responses omit `version` field; client's `_server_version=0`; first PATCH ships `If-Match: "0"` and the server returns 409 spuriously; every newly-created entity that the rep edits a second time produces a spurious conflict on the first PATCH (sec-F7, ADR-0009 §3.7) | **sec-F7 close-out (S5 fix bundle):** every POST create handler now includes `version` in the response body (fresh-create returns version=1; clientId-reuse path re-queries the current version so a two-device race doesn't trip). The typed-client's `extractVersion(body)` populates `_server_version` correctly; the next PATCH's `If-Match` matches without 409. Paired with the LOW close-out on `parseIfMatchVersion` that now rejects version=0 with 428 (surfacing the misconfiguration as a clean precondition error rather than letting it slip through to 409). Routes fixed: `POST /api/hazards`, `POST /api/action-items`, `POST /api/inspections`, `POST /api/inspections/:id/findings`, `POST /api/recommendations`. | The 1.12 Apply pipeline carries this forward; documented. |
| T-S56 | Session cache pollution across logout — a subsequent rep signing in on the same device inherits the prior session's queue rows, conflict rows, base-state cache, and refresh-on-online tables (corpus, templates) (sec-F9) | **sec-F9 close-out (S5 fix bundle):** `clearOnLogout()` helper (`apps/web/src/sync/db.ts`) is invoked from the auth context's logout path. Clears: `sync_queue`, `sync_conflicts`, `_base_state`, `legal_clauses`, `inspection_templates`. Preserves: entity caches (hazards / action_items / inspections / etc. — same rep signing back in expects their drafts to still be there) + `evidence_pending_uploads` (pre-capture state). The queue worker singleton is also reset (`setWorkerForTests(null)` in the logout path; the next `getWorker()` builds a fresh one). | Same-device cross-rep handoff is the bound; single-co-chair scope makes this near-zero in practice. Documented. |
| T-S57 | Optimistic-create clobbers a clean entity row — `enqueueMutation` spreads the new body over an existing CLEAN row + resets `_sync_state='dirty_create'`; the rep's NEW payload fields land in Dexie but the queued create hits the server's clientId-reuse 200 path which returns the EXISTING row, silently discarding the new payload (sec-F10, ADR-0009 §3.3) | **sec-F10 close-out (S5 fix bundle):** the typed-client's `enqueueMutation` checks Dexie for an existing row at the clientId BEFORE writing. If exists AND `_sync_state='clean'`, SKIP the optimistic write AND the queue enqueue; return the existing row to the caller to preserve the `Promise<T>` contract. A `console.warn` surfaces the bug in dev so the call site can be fixed to use the PATCH path. | A buggy call site that re-fires create handlers against synced rows now sees a warn log + the existing row — no silent data loss. Documented. |
| T-S58 | Hazards route inverted rate-limit / body-limit middleware order — `HAZARDS_BODY_LIMIT` was mounted BEFORE `rateLimit()` (inverted from the documented 1.5/1.6/1.7 pattern); an authenticated attacker spamming oversize POSTs at hazards routes consumed bandwidth without draining the rate-limit bucket (sec-F5) | **sec-F5 close-out (S5 fix bundle):** middleware order corrected to `rateLimit` BEFORE `bodyLimit`, mirroring `action-items/index.ts:62-67` + `evidence/index.ts:51-61` + `inspections/index.ts:107-114` + `recommendations/index.ts:104-111`. The 1.6 close-out's documented rationale (bodyLimit's `onError` short-circuits without calling next(); putting it first lets an attacker pin bandwidth at near-zero CPU cost without burning a token) applies symmetrically to hazards. | None material — the defense-in-depth ordering is now consistent across all five mutable routes. |

**Audit hooks for sync.** **No new chain-anchored audit kinds in 1.10.** The existing 1.5–1.9 kinds (`hazard.created`, `hazard.status_changed`, `action_item.created`, `action_item.moved`, `action_item.move_undone`, `action_item.updated`, `evidence.uploaded`, `evidence.read`, `evidence.list_accessed`, `inspection.created`, `inspection_finding.created`, `inspection_finding.promoted`, `inspection_finding.read`, `inspection.signed`, `inspection.exported`, `inspection.export.downloaded`, `audit.inspection_template.seeded`, `recommendation.drafted`, `recommendation.draft_patched`, `recommendation.submitted`, `recommendation.response_captured`, `recommendation.resolved`, `recommendation.withdrawn`, `recommendation.exported`, `recommendation.export.downloaded`, `audit.workplace_signing_key.seeded`) all fire at SERVER drain time — when the queue worker successfully ships the operation and the route handler runs inside its db.transaction. The chain anchor never fires at local-write time on the device; the local Dexie row is rep-trusted until the drain lands. Two operational kinds are added but are documented as separate non-chain-anchored streams: `sync_conflict.revealed` (the conflict-resolution reveal endpoint, mirrors the 1.5 reporter-identity reveal pattern from T-H4 — chain-anchored per CLAUDE.md #2 because it's a step-up-gated decrypt with audit value); and `sync.idempotency_replayed` (a debug-only operational stream, NOT chain-anchored — same shape as `auth_events` from the 1.2 → 1.3 backfill, and S5 reviewers may drop it without ceremony if the operational value doesn't justify the noise).

**The cross-cutting semantic shift** affects every prior kind: the chain row's `ts_ms` now represents "server received at" rather than "rep typed at." For online operations (which remain the overwhelming majority at single-co-chair scope) the two timestamps differ by milliseconds — the existing arbitration framing holds. For offline-then-drained operations the divergence can be hours or days; the runbook (`docs/runbooks/offline-sync.md` §"Chain-anchor latency framing") leads with this. Two specific kinds carry rep-facing legal weight that pivots on the new semantics:

- **`recommendation.submitted`** — the 21-day s.9(21) clock is measured from chain `ts_ms` (server `submitted_at`), NOT from device queue-typed-at, per §3.12. `computeRecommendationDeadline` (1.9 T-R10, pure function in `packages/shared-types`) consumes the server timestamp only. Rep-facing copy in the recommendation detail view makes this explicit ("21-day clock starts on sync").
- **`inspection.signed`** — the signature timestamp recorded in the chain is server-drain time. The runbook documents the arbitration framing: the device clock + the queue-typed-at hint on `sync_queue.created_at` are corroborating evidence the rep can produce, but the chain is canonical.

No payload-shape changes to any existing kind (the 1.5–1.9 typed-emit invariant holds — CLAUDE.md #2 + 1.3 priv-F2). Two new event-shape additions land in `packages/shared-types`: `SyncOpKind`, `SyncEntityTable`, `SyncOperationStatus`, `SyncConflictKind` (all enum/literal types — no PI surface). Verification: `audit-log-verify` does not change; the chain itself is unchanged in shape. The `sync_idempotency` ledger is operational-only and is NOT cross-checked by the verifier (the chain remains the canonical evidentiary record).

### 2.11 Excel-import threats (Milestone 1.11)

Excel import is the first surface where the app **parses untrusted user-supplied bytes** at arbitrary scale — a `.xlsx`/`.xlsm` workbook the rep dragged off email, off a USB stick, off a shared drive at the workplace, or out of a hostile counterparty's hands. The threat surface is the union of every prior milestone's encrypted-write discipline (1.5–1.9), the 1.7 sealed-box envelope shape (workplace public key, server-held private), the 1.6 `action_items` create + the `source_type='excel_import'` forward seam already wired in 1.6 line 113, the 1.10 idempotency ratchet on the commit POST, and four new surfaces: a third-party browser dependency (SheetJS) loaded into the rep's session and handed an attacker-controlled ZIP archive; a schema detector that classifies a workbook as `recognized` or `unrecognized` and gates whether parsing proceeds at all; a reconciliation engine that hashes parsed cell content into a deterministic dedup key and silently classifies rows as create / update / skip / conflict; and a single-shot server-side commit transaction that allocates per-row sequence numbers + emits O(N) chain anchors atomically — fail-closed if offline, 30-day reversible if the rep changes their mind. Non-negotiable #11 is the dominant constraint (raw bytes never leave the browser); #2 (chain-of-custody) and #4 (privacy-by-default) shape every mitigation below; #5 (corpus-only citations) governs the parser's refusal to auto-cite from cell content; #12 (action items first-class) governs the entity model (the import is plumbing onto the existing `action_items` shape, not a sub-concept); #16 (step-up + audit on every export) extends symmetrically to the commit + reverse paths even though they are intake not output. Every mitigation below cites the ADR-0010 subsection or the CLAUDE.md non-negotiable it implements.

| # | Threat | Mitigation | Residual |
|---|---|---|---|
| T-X1 | A supply-chain compromise of `xlsx` (SheetJS) on npm publishes a malicious version with a `beforeparse` hook that exfiltrates the cell stream to an attacker-controlled origin from inside the rep's browser, defeating non-negotiable #11's "raw bytes never leave the browser" guarantee at the dependency layer | ADR-0010 §3.1: `xlsx` is pinned to an exact version in `packages/excel-import/package.json` (no `^` / `~` range); the `pnpm-lock.yaml` integrity hash gates installs; the CI `pnpm audit --audit-level=high` job rejects any advisory against `xlsx`; `apps/web/vite.config.ts`'s CSP `connect-src` allow-list excludes any non-`self` origin so even a compromised dep cannot `fetch()` outward without a CSP violation report. The 1.10 §"Dependency & Supply Chain" controls (pinned versions, lockfile integrity, monthly `pnpm audit`) apply verbatim to the new workspace. Non-negotiable #11. | A zero-day advisory landing between `pnpm audit` runs is bounded by the CSP allow-list; a CSP-respecting exfil channel (e.g., DOM mutation timing oracle) is documented as a known unbounded surface and absorbed by the 1.12 SRI-on-bundle-output backlog. |
| T-X2 | A future PR adds a `fetch()` or `XMLHttpRequest` call inside `packages/excel-import` (e.g., "phone home for schema updates"), silently breaking the "no IO from this workspace" contract that non-negotiable #11 rests on | ADR-0010 §3.1: the workspace's contract is enforced by a Vitest assertion that greps the published bundle for `fetch(`, `XMLHttpRequest`, `navigator.sendBeacon`, `import('node:`, and `require('node:` — any match fails the test. The workspace's `package.json` declares no `node:*` dependencies. The CI bundle-analyzer step ensures `packages/excel-import/dist/index.js` contains no network primitives. Non-negotiable #11. | A determined PR author could rewrite the assertion; reviewer discipline is the bound. |
| T-X3 | A 50K-row workbook handed to `XLSX.read` on the main thread blocks UI for tens of seconds; the rep cannot cancel mid-parse and force-quits the tab, losing any in-progress reconciliation state from a prior import | ADR-0010 §3.2: parse runs in a dedicated Web Worker (`packages/excel-import/src/parser.worker.ts`); the main thread renders a progress UI and remains responsive. The worker contract is "one message in, one message out" — the rep can close the tab to abort (the worker is GC'd with the tab); there is no in-worker cooperative cancel signal in 1.11 (a 1.12 follow-up if telemetry shows it matters). The worker is `worker.terminate()`'d in `parseWorkbookInWorker`'s `finally` block so plaintext cell state never crosses imports. Non-negotiable #9 (mobile-primary; the worker keeps the 390px UI responsive). | Mid-parse cancellation is tab-close only in 1.11; documented in the runbook. |
| T-X4 | The Web Worker's message contract smuggles a session cookie or JWT into the postMessage payload — a future "for performance" PR caches auth into the worker so it can pre-fetch the existing action_items projection, putting auth credentials into a structured-clone path that a debugger or a malicious extension can read | ADR-0010 §3.2: the worker contract is `{kind: 'parse', arrayBuffer}` in, `{kind: 'result', result: DetectionResult}` out — typed in `packages/excel-import/src/parser-worker-protocol.ts`. The worker is same-origin but has no access to cookies / `document.cookie` / `localStorage` / `sessionStorage` (Web Worker scope explicitly excludes DOM + storage APIs). The `ExistingActionItemView` projection is fetched on the main thread via the typed API client and passed to `reconcile()` (NOT into the worker) per §3.1. Non-negotiable #4. | A future PR that violates the protocol typing would need to add a postMessage of a sensitive shape; the protocol union type is the structural backstop. |
| T-X5 | A workbook with formula-injection payloads (`=HYPERLINK("http://attacker/", "click me")`, `=cmd|'/C calc'!A0`, DDE-style payloads) parses in the rep's browser; even though SheetJS does not execute formulas, the formula text leaks into the action_item `description` and detonates later when the rep or a recipient opens the data in a real Excel client | ADR-0010 §3.2: SheetJS is configured with `cellFormula: false, cellHTML: false, cellText: true, raw: false` — `cellFormula: false` strips the formula text from the parsed cell object entirely so the formula representation never reaches the action_item field; `cellText: true` returns the formatted display string (what the rep actually saw, which is the rep's authoritative intent); `cellHTML: false` strips Microsoft-generated HTML. Fixture test (§3.13 S4) loads a workbook containing `=HYPERLINK(...)`, `=cmd|...!A0`, and `@SUM(...)` payloads and asserts the parsed action_item carries the display text only, never the leading `=` formula. The downstream Excel-WRITE round-trip risk is a Release 2 concern documented in the runbook. Non-negotiable #2 (rep's typed intent is authoritative, not the workbook's formula). | A workbook with a display string that LOOKS like a formula (a literal description that reads `=SUM(A1:A10)` typed by the rep) imports as that literal string — the rep is the authority on what their notes say, and the parser does not second-guess. The Release 2 Excel-WRITE path inherits this surface. |
| T-X6 | A 100MB zip-bomb `.xlsx` (an archive whose decompressed size is orders of magnitude larger than its on-disk size) is handed to SheetJS in the worker and consumes memory until the browser tab OOMs, denying the rep the import surface entirely | ADR-0010 §3.2: the worker enforces `arrayBuffer.byteLength <= 10*1024*1024` BEFORE `XLSX.read`; oversize files reject as `{kind: 'unrecognized', reason: 'payload_too_large'}` without invoking SheetJS. The decompressed-size bound is `100*1024*1024` enforced via SheetJS's hardened parser (per the `xlsx` security advisories) plus a post-parse total-row-count assertion (`rowCount <= 50000`). Fixture test loads an 11MB workbook and a synthetic zip-bomb fixture and asserts both reject before parse. Non-negotiable #4 (minimize collection; oversize is also a privacy bound). | A workbook crafted to fit under 10MB on-disk + 100MB decompressed + 50K rows but still trigger a SheetJS parser pathology is the residual surface; mitigated by SheetJS's own hardening + the worker's tab-isolation (an OOM crashes the tab, not the device). |
| T-X7 | The schema detector accepts a hostile workbook whose sheet names case-insensitively match the schema but whose content is intentionally mis-shaped (a `NEW BUSINESS` sheet containing inspection-review data), feeding the wrong parser and producing nonsense action_items | ADR-0010 §3.3: the detector matches sheet names AND first-row column headers (`Issue Description`, `Recommended Action`, `Start Date`, etc.) — both must match for `recognized`. The per-sheet parser additionally validates each row's cell types (date cells are date-shaped; status cells are in the enum). A mismatch within a recognized workbook lands in `excel_import_items.import_warnings` and surfaces in the preview UI as a per-row warning badge; the rep can skip or edit before commit. Non-negotiable #11 (audit chain integrity — the warning is provenance the rep can review). | A maliciously-crafted workbook that matches sheet AND column AND type shape but lies about the SEMANTICS (rows describing inspection findings filed under `NEW BUSINESS` headers) is indistinguishable from a legitimate workbook; the rep is the authority and the preview UI is the gate. |
| T-X8 | A workbook is missing one required sheet (e.g., `NOTICE OF RECOMMENDATION`); the detector returns `recognized` with a partial shape and the parser silently produces an empty recommendation list, dropping rows the rep intended to import | ADR-0010 §3.3: the detector is **fail-closed on missing-anything** — absence of ANY required sheet OR ANY required column on any required sheet returns `{kind: 'unrecognized', reason: "missing required sheet 'NOTICE OF RECOMMENDATION'"}`. No partial-recognized variant exists in the discriminated union; the typechecker rejects code that tries to construct one. Fixture test (§3.13 S4) loads a workbook missing each required sheet in turn and asserts each rejects with the specific reason string. CLAUDE.md Excel Import Rule 6 (clear "we don't recognize this format" error, never partial import). | None material — the discriminated-union shape is the structural backstop. |
| T-X9 | A `Start Date` cell containing `"2024-13-45"` (a malformed date string masquerading as ISO-8601) parses through the row mapper and lands as an action_item with a nonsense `start_date`, corrupting the content_hash and breaking reconciliation idempotency | ADR-0010 §3.4: per-sheet parsers Zod-validate every parsed cell against the field's typed shape — `start_date` is `z.string().date()` (ISO-8601 YYYY-MM-DD with calendar validation); malformed dates land in `import_warnings` and the row's reconciliation classification is forced to `conflict_pending` (the rep must edit the date before commit). The fixture suite covers nonsense-date, Excel-serial-date (the 1900 vs 1904 epoch trap), and timezone-suffixed strings. Non-negotiable #2 (chain-of-custody — the warning is provenance). | A rep who edits the date in the preview to a different valid-but-wrong date commits that date; the chain anchors what was committed, and the rep is the authority. |
| T-X10 | A `Status` cell containing a legacy string (`"Pending"`, `"In Progress (Owner)"`, free-text the rep typed years ago) maps to `'Not Started'` silently, losing the original intent | ADR-0010 §3.4: unknown status values map to `'Not Started'` with the original string captured in `excel_import_items.import_warnings: {originalStatus: '<legacy>'}`; the preview UI renders the warning per-row so the rep can edit before commit. Same shape for unknown `type` (maps to `'OTHER'` with `type_subtype` carrying the legacy string per the 1.6 taxonomy). Non-negotiable #2 — provenance is preserved in the import_warnings JSONB; the legacy value never silently disappears. | The rep is the authority; the preview's per-row warning is the gate. |
| T-X11 | A `description` cell carrying 100MB of text (paste-bomb or malicious workbook with an extreme single-cell payload) lands as an envelope-encrypted blob exceeding the action_items column's reasonable bound, breaking downstream rendering + the chain anchor's payload-size budget | ADR-0010 §3.4: per-cell length cap of 8KB on `description` / `recommended_action` / `raised_by` / `follow_up_owner` (matching the existing `action_items` column's documented bound from migration 0005); cells past the cap reject as `{kind: 'unrecognized', reason: "cell at row N exceeds 8KB"}` rather than truncate (truncation would silently rewrite evidence; rejection forces the rep to fix the workbook). Fixture test loads a workbook with a 9KB description and asserts the reject. Non-negotiable #2 (no silent rewrites). | None material — the cap is the bound; raising it is a deliberate code change. |
| T-X12 | An empty `description` cell on a `NEW BUSINESS` row produces a zero-content action_item with an empty `content_hash` input, colliding with every other empty-description row across all imports past and future | ADR-0010 §3.4: empty / whitespace-only `description` cells reject at the per-row parser with `import_warnings: {emptyRequired: 'description'}` and the row is forced to `excel_import_items.status='skipped'` (cannot be edited-into-existence at commit; the rep must add description content in the source workbook + re-upload). The content_hash function rejects empty canonical inputs. Non-negotiable #12 (action items are first-class — they cannot be content-empty). | None material. |
| T-X13 | The `Inspection Review` snapshot is stored on `excel_imports.inspection_review_snapshot_ct` as a JSONB blob containing supervisor names + witness names from the workbook's free-text notes, but the column is plaintext, leaking PI to a Postgres-side adversary | ADR-0010 §3.4: `inspection_review_snapshot_ct` is envelope-encrypted under the workplace public key alongside `inspection_review_dek_ct` (same sealed-box shape as 1.7 evidence). Same posture for `move_history_snapshot_ct` + `move_history_dek_ct` (the optional `_MoveHistory` sheet may carry actor names). The pair-NULL CHECK (§3.8) enforces both columns NULL or both populated. Non-negotiable #4. | The snapshot is read-only (per ADR §3.4 + ROADMAP scope; not promoted to native inspection records); decryption requires the reveal path with step-up — same scope as every other workplace-encrypted column. |
| T-X14 | The attendance list parses as a single newline-separated string and envelope-encrypts as one blob; a PIPEDA P9 request to redact one attendee requires decrypting + editing + re-encrypting the entire blob, an operation the 1.11 surface does not expose | ADR-0010 §3.4 + §"Out of scope": attendance is one ciphertext blob in 1.11 (under `meeting_metadata_ct` + `meeting_metadata_dek_ct`); per-attendee row-per-name encryption is deferred to 1.12 (§"Negative tradeoffs"). The 1.11 P9 stance is the same as 1.6 / 1.9 — default-refuse, with redaction deferred to the 1.12 ratchet that splits attendance into queryable rows. The runbook documents the bound + the operator-script escalation path. Non-negotiable #4 (privacy-by-default; the encrypt-at-rest discipline holds even if per-attendee granularity is deferred). | Per-attendee P9 redaction is a 1.12 deliverable; documented. |
| T-X15 | A `Closed Items History` row carries a `Closed Date` in the year 2099 or 1899 (rep typo, malicious workbook, or Excel serial-date confusion) and the action_item lands in `section='archived'` with a nonsense `closed_date`, confusing every downstream lifecycle projection | ADR-0010 §3.4: the per-row parser asserts `closed_date <= now()` AND `closed_date >= '2000-01-01'` (a workplace inception bound); out-of-range dates land in `import_warnings: {closedDateOutOfRange: '<value>'}` and the row's reconciliation classification is forced to `conflict_pending` until the rep edits. The 1900 vs 1904 Excel epoch trap is handled by SheetJS's date normalization with `raw: false`; the resulting ISO string is the canonical form. Non-negotiable #2 — provenance preserved. | None material — the bound is documented + tested. |
| T-X16 | The PII heuristic in `packages/excel-import/src/pii-scanner.ts` accidentally writes its findings to `console.log` (or a future analytics SDK), exfiltrating the rep's plaintext cell content to the browser console where dev-tools / a malicious extension can scrape it | ADR-0010 §3.5: the heuristic is a pure function returning `{row, fieldsWithPII, totalFlags}`; the function body has zero side effects (no `console.*`, no `fetch`, no `window.*` access). The same Vitest grep-the-bundle assertion that covers T-X2 covers `console.log` / `console.info` / `console.warn` / `console.debug` in the published `packages/excel-import` bundle. The 1.10 §"No third-party analytics SDK" rule applies. Non-negotiable #3 + #4. | A dev-mode `console.log` in `apps/web/src/excel-import/` (outside the published `excel-import` workspace) is not blocked by the bundle grep; reviewer discipline + the CLAUDE.md "no console.log in committed code" pre-merge check are the bound. |
| T-X17 | The PII heuristic produces false negatives (single-token names like `"Garcia"`, lowercase names `"john doe"`, obfuscated emails like `"name [at] domain [dot] com"`); the rep reads "0 emails flagged" in the preview and commits believing no email leaked into Postgres | ADR-0010 §3.5: the heuristic is **UX nudge, not data gate**. Every action_item sensitive column (`description_ct`, `recommended_action_ct`, `raised_by_ct`, `follow_up_owner_ct`) is envelope-encrypted **regardless of PII flag** — the encrypt-everything-sensitive default of 1.6 is binding. The preview UI copy reads "PII heuristic — review your data before commit; the heuristic catches common shapes but is not exhaustive" so the rep is correctly oriented to the bound. Non-negotiable #4 + #2. | Documented residual; the heuristic is best-effort and the rep is the authority. |
| T-X18 | The PII heuristic produces false positives (capitalized two-word phrases like `"Pallet Jack"`, `"Health Safety"`, `"Forklift Battery"`) and the rep develops banner-blindness, dismissing the warnings without reading and missing a real name flag in the next import | ADR-0010 §3.5 + Compliance #4: the preview groups flags by type with counts (`"12 rows flagged for name-shape; 3 for email; 0 for SIN"`) and shows per-row badges only on flagged rows so the visual density tracks the heuristic's actual signal. The runbook documents the false-positive rate and the rep's expected reading discipline. Non-negotiable #2 (the rep is the authority; the heuristic is documentation, not enforcement). | UX surface; documented. |
| T-X19 | The source filename (e.g., `"JHSC Minutes [Workplace Name] 2025-Q3.xlsx"`) is stored plaintext on `excel_imports.source_filename`, leaking the workplace name into Postgres (non-negotiable #1) | ADR-0010 §3.8 + §3.5: the column pair is `source_filename_ct` (envelope-encrypted under workplace public key) + `source_filename_dek_ct` (envelope-sealed DEK) — same sealed-box shape as 1.7 evidence + the other encrypted columns on this row. Pair-NULL CHECK enforced; both columns must be populated. The PII heuristic additionally surfaces a "filename contains name-shape data — encrypted at rest" badge in the preview so the rep sees the protection in action. Non-negotiable #1 + #4. | None material — the filename never lands plaintext anywhere in Postgres or in chain anchor payloads (the chain carries `sourceSha256`, not the filename). |
| T-X20 | A content_hash collision attack: an adversary crafts two action_item descriptions with the same `sha256(canonical(description || start_date))` to force the reconciler to merge unrelated rows | ADR-0010 §3.6: SHA-256's collision space (2^128 expected work for a collision) is structurally negligible; a deliberate collision is computationally infeasible at the resource bounds of an adversary realistically attacking a single workplace. The reconciler's behavior on the structurally-impossible collision case is "treat as same item, surface as `conflict_pending` if any field differs" — the rep is the gate. Non-negotiable #2 (the rep is the authority on what the rows mean). | Residual is theoretical; documented. |
| T-X21 | The content_hash canonicalization function (`s.normalize('NFC').trim().replace(/\s+/g, ' ').toLowerCase()`) is non-deterministic across runtime versions or platforms — NFC normalization drifts, the regex semantics change, and the same workbook re-imported produces different hashes on different devices, breaking idempotency | ADR-0010 §3.6: `canonical()` is a pure function pinned to a specific ICU normalization (NFC) + a specific regex (`/\s+/g`) + a specific Unicode lowercase mapping; unit tests in `packages/excel-import/test/content-hash.test.ts` cover the NFC-vs-NFD, whitespace-variant, case-variant, and ISO-vs-Excel-serial-date matrix per ADR §"Risks". A V8 / SpiderMonkey / WebKit normalization drift would surface immediately in the test matrix. Non-negotiable #2 — the hash is the integrity anchor for reconciliation. | Documented residual; the test matrix is the structural backstop. |
| T-X22 | A row imported into `NEW BUSINESS` in Q3 reconciles correctly. The same row appears in `OLD BUSINESS` in Q4 (carry-over). The Q4 import treats it as a new row because the section is different, double-creating the action_item | ADR-0010 §3.6: the content_hash is computed over `description || start_date` ONLY — section is NOT part of the hash. The Q4 import's row reconciles to the same action_item as Q3, classified as `update` (because `section` differs), and the preview surfaces a "section transition: new_business → old_business" badge. The rep accepts the transition; the commit emits a single `action_item.updated` chain anchor with the section change in payload. CLAUDE.md Excel Import Rule 5 ("same Description + Start Date = same item"). | None material — section is intentionally orthogonal to identity. |
| T-X23 | A row in the workbook matches an existing action_item by content_hash, but the existing action_item was created MANUALLY (not via prior import) — the reconciler creates an `excel_import_items` link, retroactively associating the rep's manual work with an import they did not consciously author, polluting the provenance | ADR-0010 §3.6: the `excel_import_items` row records the link as `status='updated'` (or `'skipped'` if no fields differ) — the link is a join, not a claim of authorship. The action_item's `source_type` stays at whatever it was (`'manual'`, `'hazard'`, etc.); the `source_excel_hash` column is populated only for `created` rows (where the action_item is fresh from this import). The preview UI surfaces the manual-vs-import distinction explicitly: "this row matches an existing manually-created action_item — your import will update its fields, not claim authorship." Non-negotiable #2 (provenance is preserved truthfully). | None material — the link is bi-directional but the authorship attribution is preserved. |
| T-X24 | The preview UI renders a cell containing `<script>alert(1)</script>` as actual HTML (a future PR slips `dangerouslySetInnerHTML` into the per-row component), executing attacker JS in the rep's session and exfiltrating the entire preview's plaintext via a `fetch()` from the rep's authenticated origin | ADR-0010 §3.7: the preview's per-row component renders cell content via React's default text rendering (JSX `{cellValue}` → text node, escape-by-default); `dangerouslySetInnerHTML` is grep-blacklisted in `apps/web/src/excel-import/**` via an ESLint rule (`react/no-danger`). The CSP `script-src` allow-list excludes `'unsafe-inline'` so even an escape-bypass would not execute. Fixture test (§3.13 S4) loads a workbook with `<script>`, `<img onerror>`, and `javascript:` payloads in cells and asserts they render as literal text. Non-negotiable #4 (the rep's session is the trust boundary). | A future violation of the ESLint rule + the CSP relaxation simultaneously is the residual; reviewer discipline + CSP are layered defenses. |
| T-X25 | The preview state lives in memory only; a rep who refreshes the page mid-review loses the reconciliation decisions + per-row edits and has to start over from a fresh parse, potentially editing the data inconsistently the second time | ADR-0010 §3.7: per-row edits and reconciliation decisions persist to Dexie under `_excel_import_drafts` so the preview survives a page refresh. The drafts are cleared when the import is committed or cancelled. The runbook documents the persistence behavior + the per-import draft lifecycle. Non-negotiable #9 (mobile-primary; phone tab-eviction is a real surface — the persistence covers it). | The drafts contain plaintext cell content in Dexie — same plaintext-on-device residual as 1.10 T-S1 (priv-F1); 1.12 at-rest encryption closes both. Documented. |
| T-X26 | A rep with a stale step-up token (granted at preview-open, 70 seconds before commit) taps the commit button, the client sends the stale token, the server's freshness check at 60s rejects with 401 mid-commit, and the rep loses the preview's reconciliation state | ADR-0010 §3.10: step-up modal is presented on commit-button-tap NOT on preview-open — the 60s freshness window starts when the rep grants step-up, immediately before the POST. A stale grant from a different action (`evidence.decrypt`, `inspection.export`) is rejected by the freshness check (per 1.9 T-R28 mirror). The preview's Dexie draft survives the 401 so the rep re-steps-up and retries without losing reconciliation state. The runbook §"Step-up expiry mid-commit" documents the recovery. Non-negotiable #16. | The 1.9 T-R29 honest stance carries forward: the action label `excel_import.commit` is cosmetic until 1.12 ships action-bound tokens; the 60s freshness check is the real defense. Documented. |
| T-X27 | A hand-crafted POST to `/api/excel-imports/:id/commit` lacks the `X-Requested-With: jhsc-web` CSRF guard header; a malicious cross-origin page tricks the rep's browser into firing the commit with attacker-supplied operations | ADR-0010 §3.10: `csrfHeaderGuard()` middleware (per `apps/api/src/index.ts`, 1.7 sec-F2 pattern) covers the commit + reverse routes; missing the header returns 403 `csrf_header_missing`. SameSite=Strict cookies (per 1.2) layer underneath. Integration test asserts a request without the header rejects. Non-negotiable #2 + #16. | None material — same shape as every prior mutation route. |
| T-X28 | A malicious actor with a compromised rep account scripts 1000 commits per hour from a botnet, draining the workplace public key's encryption window + flooding the chain with attacker-supplied action_items | ADR-0010 §3.10: per-actor rate limit of **5 commits per hour** for the commit route + **3 reverses per hour** for the reverse route, enforced by the existing `rateLimit()` middleware (per `apps/api/src/middleware/rate-limit.ts`). Excess requests return 429 `rate_limited`. The 5/hour bound is tuned to the realistic use case (batch import of historical files; a higher rate is structurally suspicious). The CSRF guard + step-up freshness + rate limit layer in defense. Non-negotiable #16. | A compromised account is bounded at 5 imports/hour but can still cause damage within that bound; the lost-device incident response (revoke-the-session) is the structural close-out. |
| T-X29 | A 1000-row commit transaction holds the section-scoped advisory lock (`pg_advisory_xact_lock(hashtext('action_items.seq.new_business'))`) for many seconds, blocking concurrent manual `action_items` create operations into the same section and creating a UX freeze for the rep | ADR-0010 §3.9: the per-section advisory lock is held for the duration of the commit transaction; at single-co-chair scale concurrent manual creates are vanishingly rare and the freeze surfaces as a brief loading indicator in the manual-create flow. The runbook documents the bound: commits of >500 rows complete in low hundreds of milliseconds at single-tenant scale; the lock duration scales linearly. A future 1.12 batch-allocation primitive (`allocateSequenceNumberBatch(N)`) would reduce the lock-hold to a single allocation; deferred. Non-negotiable #2 (atomicity matters more than concurrency for evidentiary writes). | Documented residual; the rep-facing UX is bounded by the 5/hour rate limit + the runbook. |
| T-X30 | The commit transaction fails mid-batch (e.g., a single `If-Match` mismatch on an `update` op); per-row Postgres state rolls back BUT the per-row `action_item.created` chain anchors that fired before the failure stay in the chain, producing orphan chain rows with no corresponding `action_items` row | ADR-0010 §3.9: ALL writes — `action_items` INSERT/UPDATE + `excel_import_items` UPDATE + per-row `action_item.created`/`action_item.updated` chain appends + batch-level `excel_import.committed` chain append + `excel_imports` status flip — run inside a SINGLE `db.transaction`. Any per-row failure aborts the whole transaction; Postgres rolls back the chain `audit_log` INSERTs alongside the entity INSERTs (the chain table participates in the transaction same as any other). The `excel_imports.status` stays at `preview`; the rep returns to the preview UI, re-reconciles, and re-commits. Integration test (§3.13 S2) simulates a mid-transaction `If-Match` mismatch and asserts zero chain rows landed. Non-negotiable #2 (chain integrity — no orphan anchors). | None material — the transaction discipline is the structural backstop. |
| T-X31 | An idempotent retry of a partially-failed commit (network blip on the response leg; the rep's client doesn't know if the commit landed) re-runs the entire batch, double-creating every `action_items` row and double-emitting every chain anchor | ADR-0010 §3.9 + 1.10 §3.4: the commit POST carries an `Idempotency-Key` per the 1.10 contract; the key is `sha256(canonical(operations))`. The `idempotencyKeyGuard()` middleware (1.10 T-S4) short-circuits a replay with the cached prior response, NOT re-running the handler. The per-row `clientId` values are stable across retries (the reconciler produces them deterministically from the parsed-row position + import id). Integration test simulates a retry and asserts the second POST returns the cached response without re-firing the handler. Non-negotiable #2 + 1.10 T-S4 idempotency invariant. | The 1.10 T-S4 / T-S6 idempotency residuals carry forward; documented. |
| T-X32 | The commit attempts to drain through the 1.10 sync queue (a future PR conflates "online mutation" with "queueable mutation"), partial-drains 100 of 200 rows on a network blip, leaves 100 in the queue with a `excel_import.committed` anchor that has wrong counts | ADR-0010 §3.9 + §3.12: the commit is **fail-closed offline**, not queued. The service worker's require-online allow-list explicitly includes `/api/excel-imports/:id/commit` and `/api/excel-imports/:id/reverse` (per 1.10 §3.9 SW allow-list ratchet). An offline tap renders "Network required to commit" in the preview UI; the reconciliation drafts persist in Dexie until the rep reaches a network. Three rationales (§3.12): atomicity (batch all-or-nothing), step-up freshness (60s window cannot span a queue drain hours later), sequence-number allocation (per-section advisory lock cannot serialize across queue drains). Non-negotiable #2 + #16. | Documented; the offline-first promise of 1.10 is intentionally not extended to commit. |
| T-X33 | The rep parses + previews a workbook offline; the workplace public key has rotated since the session bootstrap cached it; the browser-side envelope encryption uses the OLD key; the commit POST is rejected by the server's active-key id check (1.7 sec-F5), the rep loses the preview's reconciliation state | ADR-0010 §3.12: the commit handler returns 409 `workplace_key_rotated` with a body pointing the client at `/api/auth/session` to refresh the workplace public key. The client re-encrypts the operations payload under the new key and re-commits. The Dexie draft (per T-X25) survives the 409 so the per-row edits + reconciliation decisions don't have to be re-done. The runbook §"Workplace key rotation during preview" documents the recovery. Non-negotiable #4. | Rotation is rare at single-tenant scale; the recovery path adds a step but no data loss. |
| T-X34 | A rep imports a workbook with rows that mention OHSA s.25(2)(h) or CLC s.135(7) in the description text; a future PR adds a "convenience" auto-cite that writes `recommendation_citations` rows from cell-content regex matches, violating non-negotiable #5 (citations from corpus only) | ADR-0010 §3 + Compliance #5: the parser flags clause-shape strings (`s.25(2)(h)`, `s.43`, etc.) in the preview UI as a UX nudge but the commit transaction does NOT write `recommendation_citations` rows from cell content. The route handler's Zod body schema excludes any citation fields entirely. Fixture test (§3.13 S4) loads a workbook with clause-shape strings in descriptions and asserts no `recommendation_citations` rows land at commit. The preview copy reads "this row mentions s.25(2)(h); add the citation via the recommendations flow after import." Non-negotiable #5 + ADR-0003 lineage. | None material — the parser layer is the structural refusal; the corpus stays the single source of truth. |
| T-X35 | The 30-day reverse window expires by the server's clock while the rep's reverse request is in flight (day 30 boundary race) and a partial reverse stops mid-transaction, leaving the action_items half-deleted | ADR-0010 §3.11: the reverse route's window check is `committed_at > now() - interval '30 days'` evaluated INSIDE the reverse transaction, before any DELETE / UPDATE runs. If the check fails, return 410 BEFORE touching any entity row. If the check passes, the entire reverse runs in one transaction — atomic. The boundary race is bounded to "the check either accepts or rejects atomically; no half-reverse possible." Non-negotiable #2. | None material — the transactional check is the structural backstop. |
| T-X36 | A reverse attempts to DELETE an action_item that has been EDITED since the import (`version > 1`); silently deleting it would destroy the rep's subsequent manual work | ADR-0010 §3.11: the reverse handler asserts `version = 1` on each `created` row before DELETE; on `version > 1` it skips with `import_warnings: {refused: 'action_item_modified_since_import'}` and increments `refusedCount` in the chain payload. The rep sees a per-row outcome list in the reverse UI ("47 rows reverted; 3 rows refused — edited after import; reverse them manually if desired"). For `updated` rows, the chain payload of the original `action_item.updated` anchor carries the pre-import state; the reverse restores it; subsequent edits beyond that anchor are preserved. Non-negotiable #2 (the rep's subsequent work is evidence, not garbage). | The rep is the authority on subsequent edits; the partial-reverse + per-row outcome list is the gate. |
| T-X37 | The reverse path emits an `excel_import.reversed` anchor with `reversedAt` from the rep's client clock, allowing a rep to backdate the reverse and confuse the chain timeline | ADR-0010 §3.11: the chain row's `ts_ms` is set server-side from `now()` inside the reverse transaction; the payload's `reversedAt` is the same server time. The client's clock does not flow into the chain. Same shape as the 1.10 T-S21 server-clock invariant. Non-negotiable #2. | None material — server-side timestamping is the structural backstop. |
| T-X38 | A reverse fires `excel_import.reversed` before all per-row DELETEs commit; a network blip leaves the chain anchor recorded but the action_items half-deleted, producing a chain that claims a reverse that didn't fully happen | ADR-0010 §3.11: the `excel_import.reversed` chain anchor + `excel_imports.status='reversed'` flip + all per-row DELETEs / UPDATEs run in one db.transaction. Any failure rolls all of them back; the anchor does not land if any per-row write fails. The `refusedCount` in the payload captures legitimate per-row refusals (per T-X36); a transaction-level failure produces NO anchor at all. Non-negotiable #2. | None material — transaction discipline. |
| T-X39 | After 30 days, the reverse route returns 410, but a rep who genuinely needs to reverse must escalate to the operator script (`scripts/excel-import-reverse.ts --force`); the script bypasses the chain and produces an evidentiarily silent rollback | ADR-0010 §3.11 + §"Risks": the operator script emits the same `excel_import.reversed` chain anchor as the route, with an additional payload field `{viaOperatorScript: true, operatorUserId, justification}` so the chain still records the rollback. The script is documented in the runbook (`docs/runbooks/excel-import.md` §"Post-30-day reverse") and requires an operator + a justification text. Non-negotiable #2 — the chain remains the canonical record even for operator escalations. | Operator-only path is the bound; the chain still records, so the evidence trail is preserved. |
| T-X40 | The chain volume for a 1000-row import is 1001+ chain rows (1 `excel_import.uploaded` + 1 `excel_import.committed` + 1000 `action_item.created` + N `action_item.updated`), bloating `audit_log` and slowing `audit-log-verify.ts` linearly | ADR-0010 §3.9 + §"Risks": chain volume bound is documented — typical quarterly import is 20-50 action_items + 1 batch anchor; an outlier full-history import of 1000 rows produces ~1001 chain rows. At single-tenant scale the `audit_log` table grows by ~50 rows per quarter; an outlier import adds a one-shot bump that the verifier completes in seconds. The verifier is O(N) on chain length; a 1.12 `--check-excel` flag (per ADR §"Follow-ups") adds the cross-join between `excel_import_items.content_hash` and `action_items.source_excel_hash` for forward-defense. Non-negotiable #2 (the chain is append-only; volume is the documented cost of evidentiary discipline). | Documented residual; the 1.12 verifier flag closes the forward-defense gap. |
| T-X41 | The legal corpus is amended between preview and commit (a corpus migration retires a clause that one of the preview's rows mentions in its description); the commit transaction touches `legal_clauses` and races the corpus migration | ADR-0010 §3 (no legal-citation auto-import) + Compliance #5: the commit transaction does NOT touch `legal_clauses` — the parser does not write citation rows from cell content; the action_item's `description_ct` is opaque ciphertext to the server. The corpus is read-only during commit. A concurrent corpus migration does not affect the commit's correctness. Integration test asserts the commit transaction's table-touch set excludes `legal_clauses` and `recommendation_citations`. Non-negotiable #5. | None material — structural decoupling. |
| T-X42 | A lost-or-stolen-device threat post-1.10: the preview's reconciliation drafts in Dexie + the in-memory plaintext cell content are dumped by a forensic adversary, leaking the workbook's entire content before the commit's envelope encryption has fired | ADR-0010 §3.7 + 1.10 T-S1 priv-F1 lineage: the preview's plaintext cells in Dexie carry the same residual as 1.10 T-S1 — rep-typed sensitive content sits as plaintext in IndexedDB on the rep's device until 1.12 lands WebAuthn-PRF / session-derived at-rest encryption. The lost-device incident response is the same: revoke-the-session per the auth runbook + escalate to operator if the workbook contained high-sensitivity content. The runbook (`docs/runbooks/excel-import.md` §"Lost or stolen device during preview") documents the bound. Non-negotiable #4 (the bound is honest; the 1.12 fix is structural). | Same residual shape as 1.10 T-S1; 1.12 closes both surfaces with one ratchet. Documented. |
| T-X43 | A regulator subpoena demands "the original workbook" but the rep has deleted the file after import; the chain anchors only the SHA-256, not the bytes — the rep cannot produce the workbook in response | ADR-0010 §"Risks" + §3.2: the `source_sha256` is a one-way hash; reconstructing the bytes is computationally infeasible. The preview UI surfaces the truncated SHA-256 with a "copy" affordance + a runbook reference advising the rep to save the source workbook alongside their evidence backup. The chain proves what was committed FROM the workbook (the `excel_import.uploaded` + `excel_import.committed` anchors carry the hash); the workbook itself is the rep's archival responsibility. The runbook's "Source file archival posture" documents the recommended backup practice. Non-negotiable #2 (the chain is necessary but not sufficient evidence; the workbook is corroborating). | Operational; runbook is the bound. |
| T-X44 | A `.xls` (binary 97-2003) file or a `.csv` is uploaded; the detector rejects but the rep is unclear why, retries with the same wrong format, and loses trust in the import surface | ADR-0010 §"Out of scope" + §3.3: `.xls` is explicitly out of scope; the upload UI's file-input `accept` attribute is `.xlsx,.xlsm` so the OS file picker filters by extension. A `.xls` file uploaded via drag-drop fails the detector with `{kind: 'unrecognized', reason: "expected .xlsx or .xlsm; got .xls"}`. The preview's error copy reads "This app supports .xlsx and .xlsm (Excel 2007+). For .xls files, open in Excel and re-save as .xlsx, then re-upload." Non-negotiable #9 (mobile-primary; clear errors matter more on phone). | The 1.12 `.xls` fallback parser is a deferred follow-up if telemetry shows it matters; documented. |
| T-X45 | The source filename (`JHSC Minutes [Workplace] Q3.xlsx`) reaches the server in plaintext JSON because the route's Zod schema accepts `sourceFilename: z.string()`; envelope encryption fires server-side AFTER the plaintext has already crossed the trust boundary — observable in any Fly TLS-terminating intermediary, any request-logging middleware, any Postgres-side dump (S5 sec-F1 / priv-F1 close-out) | ADR-0010 §3 + S5 close-out: the wire format is now sealed-box-encrypted in the BROWSER. The route's createBody schema accepts `sourceFilenameCt` + `sourceFilenameSealedDek` (base64) only; the legacy plaintext field is .strict()-rejected with a 400. The browser uses libsodium's `crypto_box_seal` against the workplace public key (fetched at session boot from `/api/auth/session`); the server stores the raw bytes as-is into `excel_imports.source_filename_ct + source_filename_dek_ct` (NO server-side re-encryption). Decryption requires the workplace private key (held under the master KEK, opened one-shot for each reveal per the 1.7 evidence pattern). Per-actor step-up gate on the GET /:id detail handler (T-X50) prevents unaudited reveals. CLAUDE.md non-negotiable #11 — no plaintext sensitive field crosses the wire. | None material — the trust-boundary fix is structural; the runbook §3 documents the wire-format contract. |
| T-X46 | The Inspection Review snapshot's free-text cells (which may carry supervisor names + witness names per T-X13) reach the server in plaintext JSONB because the route accepts `inspectionReviewSnapshot: z.record(z.unknown())` plaintext; server-side envelope encryption is too late — the JSONB body already transited TLS + entered process memory + risks logger tee'ing (S5 sec-F2 / priv-F2 close-out) | Same posture as T-X45. The route's createBody schema now accepts `inspectionReviewSnapshotCt` + `inspectionReviewSnapshotSealedDek` (base64, optional) only. The browser canonical-JSON-stringifies the snapshot + sealed-box-encrypts under the workplace public key BEFORE the POST. Pair-NULL CHECK at the DB layer enforces both columns NULL or both populated. The reveal path is the same step-up-gated GET /:id detail handler — the snapshot decrypts only when the rep proves fresh step-up. CLAUDE.md non-negotiables #4 (privacy-by-default) + #11. | None material; same structural fix as T-X45. The runbook §3 + §6 document the supervisor / witness name posture. |
| T-X47 | The commit handler's conflict gate at lines 607-613 reads `excel_import_items.status` (client-supplied) as the canonical conflict classifier; a rep who fabricates `status: 'created'` on every row in the POST body bypasses the conflict-resolution UI entirely and overwrites action_items the JHSC has actively edited — the rep's "I never saw a conflict" arbitration defense is preserved (S5 sec-F3 close-out) | ADR-0010 §3.9 + §3.11 + the security review's sec-F3 finding: the commit handler now SERVER-RECONCILES every `created` row's content_hash against the live `action_items` pool (single-tenant scope: the cross-join is `excel_import_items` JOIN `action_items ON ai.id = eii.action_item_id AND ai.status != 'Cancelled'` against the candidate `created` hashes). Any collision returns 422 `conflicts_detected_server_side` with the offending hashes; the client's status field is ADVISORY ONLY. The server is the canonical reconciler. The browser-side reconciler stays as the preview surface; the server-side re-run is the load-bearing audit invariant. Non-negotiable #2 (chain-of-custody — the rep cannot bypass a conflict by relabeling). | The browser's reconciler may still classify rows differently from the server (e.g., when the action_items list projection lacks content_hash); the server is canonical. Documented in the runbook §5. |
| T-X48 | Meeting metadata (meeting_date, quorum, attendance, workbook_version) is parsed by the schema layer + briefly held in browser memory + then silently DROPPED — the route's Zod schema doesn't accept the field, the migration omits the columns, the rep believes they imported the meeting when they imported only the action_items (S5 priv-F6 close-out) | ADR-0010 §3.8 + S5 close-out: migration 0010 (in-place delta, the migration is unmerged) adds `meeting_metadata_ct` + `meeting_metadata_dek_ct` columns with a pair-NULL CHECK. The browser sealed-box-encrypts the metadata blob (same shape as T-X45 / T-X46) + uploads the ciphertext. The route stores the bytes; the GET /:id detail handler decrypts via the step-up-gated reveal path. The attendance field is the load-bearing PI surface (lists meeting attendees by name); per-attendee row-per-name encryption is still deferred to 1.12 (T-X14 carries forward) — the 1.11 grain is "the whole blob is one envelope". Non-negotiable #4. | Per-attendee P9 redaction is still a 1.12 deliverable (inherits T-X14). The runbook §11 documents the deferral. |
| T-X49 | The PII heuristic runs against the four per-row action_item fields only (description, recommendedAction, raisedBy, followUpOwner); the source filename + the Minutes attendance + the Inspection Review snapshot get NO heuristic flagging, so the rep reads "0 name-shape flagged" in the rollup and commits believing no surface leaked when in fact three sensitive surfaces escaped the scanner (S5 priv-F5 close-out) | ADR-0010 §3.5 + S5 close-out: the heuristic now runs against the filename, the attendance string, and the joined Inspection Review snapshot in addition to the four per-row action_item fields. The reconciliation summary's PII rollup surfaces three extra documentary nudges ("filename may carry name/email/phone shape", "attendance list contains name-shape entries", "inspection-review snapshot contains name/phone/SIN shape"). The fields are sealed-box-encrypted regardless of the flag; the flag is a documentary chance to scrub. Non-negotiable #4 (default to MORE surfaces, not fewer). | The heuristic remains best-effort; the rep is the authority. Documented in the runbook §6. |
| T-X50 | `GET /api/excel-imports/:id` decrypts the source filename server-side + returns it in the JSON response without any step-up gate; every detail read by the rep (pull-to-refresh, browser back/forward, deep-link from history) reveals the workplace name without a second factor — a hijacked-cookie attacker walks away with every import's filename (S5 sec-F7 / priv-F11 close-out) | ADR-0010 §3.10 + S5 close-out: the GET /:id handler is now step-up-gated (action='excel_import.read', maxAgeSeconds=60).
