Without fresh step-up the response is the structural metadata shape with `sourceFilename: null + sourceFilenameMasked: true` (and same for inspectionReviewSnapshot + meetingMetadata). The UI renders a "tap to reveal" affordance; the rep authorizes the decrypt via the existing step-up modal. With fresh step-up the handler opens the workplace private key one-shot, decrypts, returns the plaintexts. Same posture as 1.7 evidence reveal. Non-negotiable #16 extends symmetrically to import-level sensitive fields. | The step-up freshness window is 60s; a rep who keeps the tab open across many minutes will re-prompt on the next reveal. Documented in the runbook §7. |
| T-X51 | The detail view's `<h1>{detail.sourceFilename}</h1>` renders the decrypted filename as the page title — the most-printed, most-screenshot-captured, most-shared element. A rep who screen-shares with a coworker / exports a print stylesheet / screenshots for a support thread leaks the workplace name (S5 priv-F10 close-out) | CLAUDE.md non-negotiable #1 + S5 close-out: the h1 now reads "Excel import <8-char prefix>"; the filename lives on a smaller secondary line, MASKED BY DEFAULT (rendered as the literal string `workbook.xlsx`) with a per-rep "Show filename" toggle. The reverse-confirm dialog shares the same posture: it falls back to "import <id> (filename hidden)" when the masked-default state is in effect. Print stylesheet inherits the same masking. Same pattern as the 1.7 evidence reveal posture. | The rep who explicitly opens the toggle accepts the print/screenshot risk; the runbook §10 documents the trade-off. |
| T-X52 | Validation error messages format `unparseable date "${startText}"` and `unrecognized value "${riskRaw}"` echo the raw cell content back into the React preview as plain text; a free-text Start Date cell carrying name-shape PII ("talk to John Doe by 4/15") leaks the name into the rendered DOM, a future React error boundary / Sentry-style reporter, a copy-pasted bug report, etc. (S5 priv-F8 close-out) | ADR-0010 §3.5 + S5 close-out: the per-row validation error format omits the raw cell value entirely. The reason strings now carry length/index only (`unparseable date (length: 14)`, `unrecognized value (length: 22)`); the rep finds the row via the row index + column name without seeing the value echoed back. Same posture for the `warnings['target_date'] / ['closed_date']` strings. Non-negotiable #4 (privacy-by-default — no PII surfaces outside the encrypted-everything path). | None material — the reason strings remain documentary. The rep can drill into the workbook directly via the row index. |
| T-X53 | A 5xx mid-commit (statement timeout, network blip) leaves the import row at `status='preview'` with per-item action_items partially INSERTed; the Idempotency-Key middleware doesn't cache 5xx; the retry walks the commit handler again and PK-violates on the second per-row INSERT against the same `clientId` — the rep sees a cryptic Postgres error instead of a clean retry (S5 sec-F6 close-out) | ADR-0010 §3.9 + S5 close-out: the per-row INSERT into `action_items` now carries `ON CONFLICT (id) DO NOTHING`. The clientId is the action_items.id; a retry that hits the same id is a no-op INSERT, the chain anchor still fires (audit_log idx is monotonic + additive), and the commit re-completes idempotently. The runbook §5 documents the retry semantics + the trade-off (a true PK violation now manifests as a silently-skipped row rather than a 5xx, which is the correct behavior for a same-import retry). Non-negotiable #2 + 1.10 T-S4 idempotency invariant. | A true PK collision across different imports is now silently skipped; the cross-import server-side reconciliation re-run (T-X47) is the structural guard against that case. Documented. |
| T-X54 | `xlsx@0.18.5` (the last npm-published SheetJS) carries two HIGH advisories — Prototype Pollution (GHSA-4r6h-8v6p-xvw6, patched in 0.19.3) and ReDoS (GHSA-5pgg-2g8v-p4x9, patched in 0.20.2). The CI `verify` job's `pnpm audit --audit-level=high` step fails on these. SheetJS stopped publishing to npm at 0.18.5; the patched versions ship only via the SheetJS CDN at `https://cdn.sheetjs.com/` (returns 403 from CI + this network policy, so the npm-tarball upgrade path is not reachable). | CI audit-step replaced with `scripts/audit-with-allowlist.mjs`, a wrapper that runs `pnpm audit --audit-level=high --json` and exits 0 iff every remaining HIGH advisory is on a documented allowlist. The two npm advisory ids (1108110 + 1108111) are allowlisted with the explicit mitigation posture documented in the script header: (a) the parser passes `cellFormula:false + cellHTML:false + cellNF:false` to `XLSX.read()`, which limits the prototype-pollution attack surface; (b) the Web Worker enforces a 10 MB file-size cap at the boundary, which bounds the ReDoS amplification; (c) the package is browser-only, the worker is same-origin, the rep owns the device. The actual upgrade path (switch the dep to a SheetJS CDN tarball URL) is a 1.12 hardening line item — runbook §11. | Two HIGH advisories live in the dependency tree until the 1.12 CDN-version bump. The wrapper makes the suppression explicit and version-pinned; a new HIGH advisory on any other package (or a new HIGH on xlsx outside the allowlist) trips the wrapper. |

**Audit hooks for Excel import.** **Three** new chain-anchored event kinds added to `packages/shared-types` `AuditEventKind` (ADR-0010 §3.11+). All payloads pass through the same typed-emit boundary as 1.3 priv-F2 — PI-clean by construction (IDs + hashes + counts + enums only, never cell text or filenames):

- `excel_import.uploaded` — `{importId, sourceSha256, rowCount, schemaVersion}`. PI-clean — no filename (filename is envelope-encrypted on the row), no row content, no PII flags. Emitted on the upload-record handler when the `excel_imports` row is created at `status='preview'`. The `sourceSha256` is the file-integrity anchor; the `rowCount` is non-PI metadata.
- `excel_import.committed` — `{importId, sourceSha256, schemaVersion, createdCount, updatedCount, skippedCount, conflictResolvedCount}`. PI-clean — counts only, no row content, no action_item ids (the per-row anchors carry those). Emitted at commit-transaction end after all per-row anchors fired.
- `excel_import.reversed` — `{importId, reversedAt, deletedCount, revertedCount, refusedCount, viaOperatorScript?, operatorUserId?}`. PI-clean — counts + server timestamps only. Emitted at reverse-transaction end; `viaOperatorScript` is set true when the post-30-day operator script runs (per T-X39); `operatorUserId` identifies the escalation operator without leaking PI. The optional fields are absent on the normal in-window reverse path.

**Per-row chain anchors are existing 1.6 kinds.** Each `created` row in the commit emits the existing `action_item.created` anchor (with `source_type='excel_import'`, `source_excel_hash=<contentHash>`, and a new optional payload field `createdByImportId` per ADR §3.9 — additive, the union type absorbs the field cleanly). Each `updated` row emits the existing `action_item.updated`. The volume bound for a typical quarterly import is ~50 chain rows (1 uploaded + 1 committed + ~25 created + ~25 updated); an outlier full-history import lands ~1001 chain rows (per T-X40). The chain is append-only; the volume is the documented cost of evidentiary discipline.

**The chain proves what was committed FROM a workbook, not what the workbook contained.** The `sourceSha256` is the file-level integrity anchor; an arbitrator presented with a workbook can re-hash it and verify against the chain anchor's value to prove "this is the file that was imported." The workbook bytes themselves are not stored (non-negotiable #11 — raw bytes never leave the browser); archival of the source workbook is the rep's responsibility (per T-X43 + runbook).

**`audit-log-verify.ts --check-excel` is a 1.12 follow-up for forward-defense.** The flag cross-joins `excel_import_items.content_hash` against `action_items.source_excel_hash` to detect chain rows that claim an import created an action_item whose hash doesn't match the import's row hash. Until 1.12 lands the flag, the per-row `action_item.created` anchors carry `source_excel_hash` in their payload (verifiable by hand from `audit_log`); the cross-check is operationally manual but structurally available. Same shape as the 1.9 §"Follow-ups" deferral for `--check-recommendations`.

**S5 review deferrals — 1.12 backlog.** Per the user-authorized scope on the two independent security/privacy reviews, the following residuals are documented in the runbook (`docs/runbooks/excel-import.md` §11) and deferred to 1.12:

- **Dexie preview persistence** (T-X25 / priv-F4 close-out posture): the ADR §3.7 commitment to `_excel_import_drafts` is deferred; preview state stays in React useState only. A page refresh / tab eviction loses the rep's per-row edits. The runbook §10 documents the lost-device + tab-eviction posture.
- **Per-attendee row-per-name encryption** (T-X14 / T-X48 follow-on): attendance is one envelope blob in 1.11; per-attendee P9 redaction requires the 1.12 ratchet that splits the blob into queryable rows.
- **`excel_import.cancelled` chain anchor kind** (sec-F13 / priv-F9 follow-on): the cancellation transition is not chain-anchored; the upload anchor already binds the abandoned event. A future chain-kind addition is deferred.
- **`audit-log-verify.ts --check-excel` flag**: deferred per the existing T-X40 / T-X42 + ADR §"Follow-ups" deferral.
- **Source workbook archival decision** (T-X43 follow-on): the rep's responsibility today; a future PWA-backed archival under the workplace KEK is deferred.
- **Action-bound step-up tokens** (T-X26 honest stance): the action label is cosmetic until 1.12 lands action-bound tokens with a jti pin on the `excel_imports.step_up_jti` column.
- **`before_state_json` envelope encryption** (priv-F7 follow-on): the JSONB column carries plaintext `priorTags` + structural metadata. The tags field is bounded + the column is only read during the step-up-gated reverse path; a full envelope encryption of the column is deferred to align with the per-action_item redaction work.

### 2.12 Release 1 hardening — release-readiness threats (Milestone 1.12)

Milestone 1.12 is the **capstone** of Release 1. Unlike §2.1–§2.11 — each of which modeled a NEW feature surface (auth, audit chain, corpus, hazards, action items, evidence, inspections, recommendations, offline sync, Excel import) — 1.12 introduces **zero new feature surfaces**: no new tables, no new audit kinds, no new API routes, no new entity types, no new encryption boundaries. The threat surface is the **release-readiness surface itself**: the WCAG audit methodology, the print stylesheet verification, the security pre-launch checklist, the pen-test plan, the Excel parser fuzzing harness, the backup + restore drill, the audit-log-verify `--full` flag, the mobile Playwright specs, the deploy runbook, and the slice plan that orders all of them (per ADR-0011 §3.1–§3.10). The threats are **operational + process** rather than entity-data — what happens when an audit misses a view, when a fuzzing harness produces a false negative, when a backup runbook is operator-run and the operator never runs it, when the deploy lands in the wrong region, when a deferred backlog item silently ships in R2 still deferred, when the lone single-tenant rep IS the operator IS the security signer with no separation-of-duties. Every mitigation below cites the ADR-0011 subsection (§3.1–§3.10) or the CLAUDE.md non-negotiable (#1–#16) that justifies it. Non-negotiable #2 (chain-of-custody) is the dominant invariant: 1.12 ships no new chain kinds and the `--full` flag is the structural verification that the chain landed by 1.5–1.11 remains intact.

| # | Threat | Mitigation | Residual |
|---|---|---|---|
| T-HD1 | The WCAG audit walk-list is frozen against the 1.11 view inventory; a 1.11 component that lands AFTER the audit-list freeze (a late S5 fix-bundle commit, a typo-class follow-on) is not walked, ships inaccessible, and a screen-reader rep is blocked from a critical flow | ADR-0011 §3.1: the audit walks every view in the eight feature-surface inventory (auth / hazards / action items / evidence / inspections / recommendations / offline-sync / Excel import) named in the methodology; the WCAG audit document records the git SHA of the audited tree so a reviewer can verify the inventory matches the shipped surfaces. The S1 slice runs AFTER the 1.11 close-out lands, so the 1.11 inventory is settled. New views introduced between freeze and merge are added to the audit by re-walking before the milestone closes; the per-PR Quality Bar item ("WCAG 2.2 AA checks pass on new UI") is the standing forward-defense. CLAUDE.md #9 (mobile-primary baseline) + Accessibility Phase 1. | A view that lands between audit-freeze and milestone-merge without an audit re-walk is the residual; the per-PR checkbox is the bound. Documented in `docs/audits/release-1-wcag-audit.md` "Inventory + provenance" section. |
| T-HD2 | A WCAG finding categorized as SHOULD-FIX is actually a release-blocker — the boundary between MUST-FIX-FOR-RELEASE and SHOULD-FIX is judgement, and a miscategorization ships a flow the assistive-tech rep cannot complete | ADR-0011 §3.1 category definitions: MUST-FIX is "blocks a Phase-1-baseline flow for an assistive-tech rep" (form label missing, color-only status, keyboard trap, missing focus indicator, modal without focus-trap); SHOULD-FIX is "degrades but does not block." The audit document records the category reasoning per finding so a reviewer can second-guess; an S5 reviewer pass re-walks the category boundary. The pre-launch checklist's Section A row for non-negotiable #9 cites the audit; a reviewer who flags a miscategorization moves the finding into S1. CLAUDE.md #9 + Accessibility Phase 1. | Boundary drift is a judgement bound; the S5 review is the gate. Documented. |
| T-HD3 | `axe-core` and Lighthouse miss documented WCAG criteria (color-meaning, text-alternative quality, focus-order semantics, screen-reader announcement timing) — a fully-automated pass produces false-clean signal and the rep ships a view that no human walked | ADR-0011 §3.1 "No automated-only audit": the manual walk is authoritative; `axe-core` via `@axe-core/playwright` is a scanning aid only. The audit document records, per view, the assistive-tech configuration used (VoiceOver iOS / TalkBack Android / NVDA Firefox) and the manual-walk checklist outcomes. The `apps/web/tests/a11y.spec.ts` spec runs axe-core as a regression net, NOT as a sign-off — a passing axe-core spec is necessary but not sufficient. CLAUDE.md Accessibility Phase 1. | Tooling gaps are the documented bound; the manual walk + screen-reader pass is the structural backstop. The audit document's "Tooling gap" section enumerates what each tool does and does not catch. |
| T-HD4 | A WCAG fix regresses a prior milestone's visual snapshot test or interaction test — a contrast token tweak shifts a `data-testid` color assertion; a focus-ring CSS change breaks a Playwright element-bounds assertion; the fix ships but unrelated tests turn red mid-milestone | ADR-0011 §3.1 "Fix bundle posture": fixes are small, focused, one-commit-per-view; the design tokens stay unchanged unless a contrast finding forces a token-level change (in which case the change is the smallest possible diff + documented in the audit's "design-system implications" section). The CI `verify` job runs the full test suite on every commit so regressions surface immediately. S1 lands the fix bundle BEFORE S2/S3 so any regression is caught at S1-merge, not at S5. CLAUDE.md "tests pass" pre-merge checkbox. | Regression-via-fix is bounded by the CI suite; a flaky snapshot test that masks a real regression is the residual (covered by T-HD22). |
| T-HD5 | A print preview in Chromium DevTools "Emulate print media" matches the spec, but a real printer (or a different browser's print pipeline) produces different output — paper size assumptions, font fallback, color-vs-monochrome rendering, page-break behavior diverge from what the Playwright spec asserts | ADR-0011 §3.2 + non-negotiable #16: the Playwright spec (`apps/web/tests/e2e/print.spec.ts`) asserts the documented `@media print` invariants (chrome hidden, Source Serif 4 applied to body, page-break-inside on cards + tables + section headings, chain-anchor footer present); the deploy runbook §"Post-deploy smoke test" includes a manual browser-side print preview check on the hazard detail. The runbook for the rep (per §"Post-deploy smoke") asks for a real-printer test on at least one printable surface before relying on the printout for evidentiary purposes. Source Serif 4 fallback to a generic serif is documented; layout-shift on font-fallback is bounded by Playwright's "no horizontal overflow" assertion. CLAUDE.md "Print stylesheet — evidence-grade output." | Real-printer divergence is the documented bound; the rep's post-deploy smoke is the structural backstop. A genuine printer-quirk surfaces at the 4–6 week window's evidentiary use. |
| T-HD6 | The five printable surfaces enumerated in §3.2 (hazards detail / action items detail + minutes board / inspection report / recommendation document / Excel-import history detail) are 1.5–1.11 surfaces; a printable surface introduced by a 1.11 follow-on (the S5 fix bundle, a late stale-doc patch) is not in the verification list and ships without a print stylesheet | ADR-0011 §3.2: the surface inventory is frozen with the 1.11 close-out + cross-referenced from each prior ADR's quality-bar declaration; the `print.spec.ts` covers each named surface explicitly. The pre-launch checklist's Section B row for the print-stylesheet quality bar item cites the spec; an S5 reviewer who finds a surface missing from the spec moves the fix into S1. CLAUDE.md "Print stylesheet for every printable view." | A printable surface added between freeze and merge without a spec extension is the residual; the per-PR Quality Bar checkbox is the standing forward-defense. Documented. |
| T-HD7 | A `@media print { display: block }` rule on an element with `display: none` on screen reveals a plaintext field in the printed output that was correctly hidden on-screen — a step-up-gated reveal field that's hidden in screen mode but accidentally un-hidden in print mode leaks plaintext into a printer queue / shared printer / scanner-to-email pipeline | ADR-0011 §3.2 + non-negotiable #4 + #16: the print stylesheet verification walks each surface explicitly asserting that fields gated by step-up reveal stay hidden under `@media print` unless the reveal was active on-screen at print time; the audit document records the per-field hide-state. Reveal-gated content is rendered server-side only after step-up; the print stylesheet operates on the DOM that's present, so a field that wasn't revealed on-screen is structurally absent from print. The `print.spec.ts` includes negative-case fixtures: open a hazard detail WITHOUT reveal, emulate print, assert the encrypted-body placeholder (not the plaintext) is in the print output. CLAUDE.md #4 + #16. | A future PR that adds a `@media print { display: block }` on a sensitive selector is the residual; the negative-case spec is the regression net. |
| T-HD8 | The security pre-launch checklist (`docs/release-1-security-checklist.md`) is markdown-only — a non-negotiable row gets accidentally deleted on edit, a threat row's "Enforcement" column points at a moved file, or a residual moves from Section C to nowhere; the checklist passes a visual review but a structural gap shipped | ADR-0011 §3.3 + S5 review: the checklist is structured as one row per non-negotiable (#1..#16) + one row per threat-model T-# entry + one row per documented residual; an S5 reviewer cross-checks the row inventory against (a) CLAUDE.md non-negotiables, (b) `SECURITY.md` §2.1..§2.12 threat tables, (c) the ADR-0011 §"Out of scope" deferral list. A CI lint (per the ADR-0011 follow-up + the deploy runbook env-var lint precedent) confirms every non-negotiable + every T-# has a row; a missing row trips the lint. CLAUDE.md "every non-negotiable + every threat row enumerated." | A reviewer who misses a structural delete is the bound; the lint is the structural backstop. Documented in §3.3. |
| T-HD9 | The checklist's "operator sign-off" line has no separation-of-duties — the single-tenant rep IS the operator IS the deployer IS the security signer; a self-attesting sign-off does not bind a reviewer who didn't read the document, and a future arbitration adjudicator may discount it accordingly | ADR-0011 §3.3 + CLAUDE.md "single-tenant, worker-controlled": the sign-off is documentary, not legal — it exists so the rep has a moment of explicit acknowledgement before deploy. The S5 reviewer pass provides the second-pair-of-eyes (independent review of the checklist + the residuals); the rep's signature attests to having read every row. The runbook frames the limitation honestly: the rep is the operator + signer; the chain anchor is the structural evidence of what was deployed, not the signature. Non-negotiable #2 (chain-of-custody is the canonical evidence; the signature is documentary). | Single-tenant-operator-equals-signer is a structural property of the project, not a fixable gap; documented. The 4–6 week real-world use window is the de-facto separation between sign-off and ongoing operation. |
| T-HD10 | A documented residual in Section C is mis-classified as "post-Release-1" when it should have been a "release-blocker" — a deferred item the reviewer accepted is actually MUST-FIX, but the deferral wording smuggled it past the sign-off | ADR-0011 §3.3 + each prior milestone's "Out of scope" + "Negative tradeoffs" sections: the residual inventory is sourced from every prior ADR's explicit deferrals (workplace key rotation, action-bound step-up tokens, Dexie at-rest encryption, conflict UI Apply pipeline, etc.) — the rows aren't invented in 1.12, they're collated. The S5 reviewer pass re-walks each residual against the source ADR's deferral language; a reviewer who flags a mis-classification moves it into S1 or escalates to "block deploy." CLAUDE.md "default to worker safety, worker privacy, evidentiary defensibility." | Judgement bound on what's "blocker" vs "post-Release-1"; the S5 reviewer pass is the structural backstop. A genuine miss surfaces in the 4–6 week window via real-world use. |
| T-HD11 | The pre-launch checklist is a markdown file; version drift over time (a post-Release-1 milestone updates an enforcement mechanism but doesn't update the checklist row pointer; the row points at a moved file) | ADR-0011 §3.3 + the deploy runbook env-var-lint precedent: the checklist's "Enforcement" column references files via repo-relative paths; a CI lint (the S4 follow-up) walks each path + asserts the file exists. A future PR that moves an enforcement file without updating the checklist trips the lint. The S5 reviewer pass + the quarterly re-walk under SECURITY.md §9 keep the checklist current as the codebase evolves. | A file moved AND the lint silenced is the residual; reviewer discipline is the bound. Documented. |
| T-HD12 | OWASP ZAP produces false positives — an authenticated baseline scan flags HSTS-on-localhost, "missing security header" findings against routes that are correctly headerless (the health endpoint), or stack-trace-class warnings against intentional 404s. The rep without security expertise reads the report as gospel + treats false positives as release-blockers | ADR-0011 §3.4 "Triage runbook": the plan documents the post-scan workflow — every ZAP finding triages against (a) existing T-# entry → mitigation already documented, (b) new finding → new T-# entry + mitigation, (c) false positive → documented in `docs/audits/release-1-pentest-findings.md` with the reasoning. The plan includes the triage examples (HSTS-on-localhost, the health endpoint's intentional no-cache headers, the SPA's index.html being served for unknown routes). HIGH + CRITICAL findings block deploy; MEDIUM lands in the 4–6 week window; LOW + INFO go to the post-Release-1 backlog. CLAUDE.md "default to worker safety." | False positives are bounded by the triage runbook; a rep who treats every finding as a blocker has the runbook as the gate. Documented. |
| T-HD13 | OWASP ZAP produces false negatives — it doesn't cover step-up token replay across actions, SSRF on the Tigris presign route, polymorphic FK trigger SQL injection, content-hash collisions in Excel imports, idempotency-key replay across users, or service-worker scope abuse. A clean ZAP report gives the rep false confidence that the manual surfaces are also clean | ADR-0011 §3.4 "Manual test cases beyond ZAP": the plan enumerates the app-specific surfaces ZAP cannot reach — step-up bypass attempts, cross-origin CSRF, SSRF via presign, JWT replay across IP/UA, SQLi on the polymorphic FK trigger (1.7 + 1.8), content-hash collision (T-X20), Idempotency-Key replay against a different user (T-S4 + T-X31), workplace public key tampering (T-X33 + T-S26), Excel parser worker plaintext leakage across imports (T-X3 + T-X4), service-worker scope abuse (T-S30). Each manual case has a step-by-step procedure + an expected outcome. CLAUDE.md #2 + #4 + #16. | A novel surface ZAP doesn't reach AND the manual cases don't enumerate is the residual; the post-Release-1 quarterly re-scan + the SECURITY.md §9 cadence is the standing forward-defense. Documented. |
| T-HD14 | The pen test is OPERATOR-RUN against a STAGING environment; a rep without security expertise running ZAP unsupervised will mis-configure the scan (form-auth context wrong, scope too broad / too narrow, the rep's session cookie leaks into the report), get noise, and either ship with unaddressed real findings OR delay deploy on triaged-out noise | ADR-0011 §3.4 + Negative tradeoffs: the milestone artifact is the plan + the triage runbook + the supervision recommendation. The runbook documents the recommended ZAP configuration (Form-Based Auth using password+TOTP fallback path; scope limited to the staging hostname; a clean session cookie before scan-start); the plan recommends that a rep running ZAP for the first time pair with someone who has done it before OR consult the linked OWASP ZAP getting-started guide. The 1.12 sign-off does NOT depend on a clean pen-test report; it depends on the plan + runbook + the rep's commitment in the checklist that they will run the scan post-deploy. Non-negotiable #2 + #4. | Operator-run-without-expertise is the documented bound; the supervision recommendation + the runbook + the 4–6 week window's response time are the structural backstop. A first-time-ZAP rep will produce noisy results; the triage runbook absorbs that. Documented in §3.4. |
| T-HD15 | The pen test runs against staging; the staging env doesn't mirror production (different env vars, different secrets, different DNS, different TLS cert) and a finding-in-staging doesn't reproduce in production OR (worse) production has a vulnerability staging didn't catch | ADR-0011 §3.4 + §3.9 deploy runbook: staging provisioning is documented in the deploy runbook with the explicit "mirror production" requirement — same Fly region (ca-central-1), same Neon Postgres shape (production branch fork), same Tigris bucket shape (SSE-AES256 + versioning), same CSP / HSTS / cookie attributes, same workplace-config env vars (with staging-only `WORKPLACE_NAME` / `WORKPLACE_TIMEZONE` test values). The pen-test plan documents the staging-vs-production diff matrix the rep should walk before scanning. CLAUDE.md "Fly.io (YYZ Toronto primary)" + "Neon Postgres (ca-central-1)." | Staging drift over time is the residual; the deploy runbook's quarterly re-validation cadence is the bound. Documented. |
| T-HD16 | The Excel parser fuzzing harness uses a deterministic seed (the commit SHA per ADR-0011 §3.5); a bug that only surfaces at a different seed is missed in every CI run on that branch — the harness produces consistent green for thousand-case coverage that happens to dodge the bug | ADR-0011 §3.5: each CI run on a different commit gets a fresh seed (the commit SHA is the seed); over the development lifecycle the harness covers a wide seed space across many commits. The 10-scenario × 100-case-per-scenario partitioning ensures every category is exercised; a category-class bug surfaces independently of seed. The quarterly re-fuzz under SECURITY.md §9 with NEW seeds (commit SHA at re-fuzz time) catches drift; the post-Release-1 backlog includes a "fuzz-with-N-random-seeds" extension for higher coverage if telemetry indicates value. CLAUDE.md #11 (Excel imports sanitized). | Seed-dependent bug residuals are bounded by the per-commit seed variation + the quarterly cadence; documented. |
| T-HD17 | 1000 cases per CI run is a CPU-time-bounded coverage; a bug at iteration 1001 or beyond is missed in CI but reachable in production if a real hostile workbook lands | ADR-0011 §3.5 + Risks: the 1000-case bound is sized to the CI budget (60s timeout) at single-tenant scale; the harness completes in well under that on commodity CI runners. The bound is doc'd; if telemetry / a near-miss in production indicates need, the bound is raised in a follow-up. The structural defense beyond fuzzing is the worker's `try/catch` envelope that returns `{kind: 'error'}` rather than crashing — a bug at iteration 1001 surfaces at intake time as a clean error, not an uncaught throw. CLAUDE.md #11. | Iteration-cap is the documented bound; the `try/catch` envelope is the structural backstop. Documented in `packages/excel-import/src/__fuzz__/parser-fuzz.test.ts` header. |
| T-HD18 | The harness asserts "no uncaught throw"; a silent corruption (parser returns syntactically-valid but semantically-wrong data — `{kind: 'recognized', sheets: ...}` where the sheets are wrong) is not caught because the harness doesn't oracle the parsed result against an expected shape | ADR-0011 §3.5 "Assertion contract": the harness's structural assertion is the no-uncaught-throw invariant + the result-shape discriminated-union match. Semantic correctness on adversarial inputs is structurally undefined (the input is random bytes; the "correct" output is whatever the parser produces, as long as it doesn't crash). The fixture-test suite from 1.11 (T-X5, T-X6, T-X7, T-X8, T-X9, T-X11) covers semantic correctness against KNOWN-shaped inputs; the fuzz harness covers crash-resistance against UNKNOWN-shaped inputs. The two layers compose. CLAUDE.md #11. | Silent-corruption-on-adversarial-input is the documented bound; the layered defense (fixtures + fuzz + 1.11 reconciliation engine's content-hash + the rep's preview UI) is the structural backstop. Documented. |
| T-HD19 | The fuzzing harness covers `parseWorkbookInWorker` ONLY; the reconciliation engine + the commit handler are NOT under fuzz coverage. A fuzz-discovered parser bug gated by reconciliation may not surface in a parser-only fuzz | ADR-0011 §3.5 + §"Beyond 1.12": the 1.12 harness scope is the parser layer (the most adversarial-input-exposed surface; 1.11 T-X1..T-X12 are parser-class). The reconciliation engine is content-hash-gated (T-X20, T-X21, T-X22, T-X23) and has its own unit-test suite from 1.11; the commit handler is transaction-gated (T-X29, T-X30, T-X31, T-X53). The post-Release-1 hardening backlog includes "extend fuzz to reconciliation + commit" if telemetry indicates value. CLAUDE.md #11 + #2. | Reconciliation + commit fuzzing is on the post-Release-1 backlog; the layered defense (parser fuzz + reconciliation unit tests + commit transaction discipline) covers each surface separately. Documented. |
| T-HD20 | The CI CPU budget for 1000 fuzz cases × parser overhead exceeds the Vitest 60s timeout on slow runners (GitHub Actions cold start, a busy shared runner); CI fails for the WRONG reason — the bug isn't a parser bug, it's a runner-budget bug | ADR-0011 §3.5: the per-case parser overhead at single-tenant scale + the 1MB baseline workbook + the 10MB max bound means 1000 cases complete in well under 60s on commodity runners. The harness uses `vi.setConfig({ testTimeout: 60_000 })` to make the bound explicit; a runner-budget failure is distinct from a parser failure in the test output. If a runner consistently times out, the bound is raised in a follow-up. CLAUDE.md "tests pass" pre-merge checkbox. | Slow-runner timeout false-positive is the residual; the explicit timeout + the runner-output disambiguation is the structural backstop. Documented. |
| T-HD21 | The backup + restore drill is OPERATOR-RUN; the milestone artifact is the runbook + the smoke-test script. A rep who deploys without running the drill has NO proof that the backup procedure works for THEIR data; the first time the procedure runs is during a real incident, when it's too late to discover a gap | ADR-0011 §3.6 + Negative tradeoffs + CLAUDE.md "default to worker safety": the milestone ships the runbook + the smoke-test script + the documentation; the operator's sign-off in the security checklist explicitly confirms they will run the drill at least once against staging before relying on the procedure for production. The runbook documents the failure-recovery posture (what to do if the drill exposes a gap: file an issue, fix in a fast-follow PR, re-run). The post-Release-1 backlog includes a quarterly drill cadence (per SECURITY.md §9). Non-negotiable #2 (chain-of-custody on restored data). | A rep who skips the drill is accepting documented risk; the structural backstop is the chain anchor's per-row idempotence (a restore that succeeds verifies via `audit-log-verify.ts --full` regardless of who ran the procedure). Documented. |
| T-HD22 | Neon Postgres is the only backup mechanism; a Neon outage = no backup access. Tigris is Fly-native; a Fly account loss = no Tigris access. Same-vendor risk concentrates the failure mode | ADR-0011 §3.6 + Risks: the runbook documents the vendor-concentration as an honest residual. The Tigris weekly cold-storage copy (via `rclone sync` from a Fly Machine to a separate bucket) provides cross-bucket redundancy within Tigris; an off-vendor (separate-account) backup is on the post-Release-1 backlog if budget allows. For Neon, the production branch + the runbook's documented point-in-time-restore procedure is the bound; a Neon-account-loss residual is documented + the runbook recommends maintaining a copy of `DATABASE_URL` + the Neon access tokens in the same out-of-band cold-storage as the KEK (per T-HD24). CLAUDE.md "single-tenant, worker-controlled" + "no employer infrastructure dependencies." | Vendor-concentration is the documented residual; the out-of-band credential backup + the post-Release-1 cross-vendor option are the bound. Documented in the runbook. |
| T-HD23 | Fly Secrets holds the workplace KEK + the workplace key pair (private) + the JWT signing key + the Tigris credentials + the VAPID keys. A Fly account loss = KEY LOSS = ENCRYPTED-DATA LOSS — every encrypted column in Postgres becomes opaque ciphertext, every Tigris evidence file becomes opaque ciphertext, the chain stays verifiable but the contents are unrecoverable | ADR-0011 §3.6 "Fly Secrets backup": the runbook documents the operator's obligation to maintain an out-of-band cold-storage backup of the KEK + the workplace private key + the JWT signing key + the Tigris credentials + the VAPID keys — printed paper in a sealed envelope OR an encrypted USB key in a physical safe OR a passphrase-wrapped backup in a separate-vendor secret manager. The backup is generated at deploy time + after any key rotation. The runbook says PLAINLY: loss of the KEK is catastrophic + the cold-storage backup is single-rep custody. CLAUDE.md "encrypt sensitive fields at the application layer with keys you control" + #2. | Loss of both Fly Secrets AND the cold-storage backup is the documented residual; the structural backstop is the rep maintaining the cold-storage backup physically separate from their laptop (a safe at home if the laptop is the primary device). The runbook documents the framing honestly. |
| T-HD24 | The chain-of-custody verification on restored data uses the existing `audit-log-verify.ts`. A backup that restores ROW DATA but not the chain hash sequence (e.g., a partial restore that loses the genesis row at idx=0 or a mid-chain row) verifies as "tampered" — but the verifier doesn't distinguish "real tamper" from "restore-procedure bug" | ADR-0011 §3.6 "Chain-of-custody verification" + §3.7: the runbook documents the expected output of `audit-log-verify.ts --full` against a restored chain (chain rows by kind + gap detection + payload-shape recompute). A verifier-detected tamper signal post-restore triggers the runbook's failure-recovery procedure: re-run the restore from a different snapshot, walk the chain visually for the gap, escalate to operator-script for the rare case of a structurally-recoverable mid-chain row. The `--full` flag's structured report distinguishes "gap" (missing idx) from "hash-mismatch" (real tamper) — different remediation paths. Non-negotiable #2. | Procedural-vs-real tamper signal is the documented residual; the structured report's `gaps` array vs `hashMismatches` array is the structural disambiguation. Documented. |
| T-HD25 | The drill runbook assumes the rep has Fly + Neon admin access. A successor co-chair without the original rep's credentials cannot run the drill — the runbook's procedure is gated by access the new operator lacks | ADR-0011 §3.6 + CLAUDE.md "single-tenant, worker-controlled": single-tenant scope means the rep IS the admin; co-chair succession is out of scope for Release 1. The runbook documents the access requirement explicitly + recommends the rep grant a backup admin (a trusted co-rep) read-only access to Fly + Neon so the drill is exercisable by a second party in an emergency. The chain-of-custody verification is the structural integrity check regardless of who runs it; the credentials backup posture (per T-HD23) covers the catastrophic-loss case. Non-negotiable #6 (no employer infrastructure dependencies — the rep controls the access). | Co-chair succession is a Release 2+ concern; documented. The backup-admin recommendation is a runbook line item, not a 1.12 deliverable. |
| T-HD26 | The `audit-log-verify.ts --full` flag walks the entire chain; for a 6-month-old workplace with thousands of chain rows, the walk takes minutes. CI budget for the per-PR `verify` job is exceeded; CI fails for the wrong reason; chain-shape regressions slip through under timeout pressure | ADR-0011 §3.7 + §"Negative tradeoffs": the `--full` flag is O(N) on chain length; at single-tenant + Release 1's expected volume (~50 chain rows per quarter), the verifier completes in seconds. The CI invocation runs against a SYNTHETIC fixture (`apps/api/test/fixtures/audit-log-full-dataset.sql`) that's bounded to ≥1000 rows — fixed-size, predictable runtime. Production chain growth doesn't affect CI runtime. A 100,000+ row production chain would benefit from a paginated `--check-range` flag; deferred per the ADR's negative tradeoffs. Non-negotiable #2. | Production chain growth-vs-CI-budget is decoupled by fixture; documented. A 100,000+ row workplace surface is post-Release-1 backlog. |
| T-HD27 | The synthetic full-dataset fixture is generated from a one-shot script that anonymizes production rows; the fixture may not catch real-data-shape issues that emerge only after months of real-world use (a payload field that's optional in the fixture but mandatory in production, a chain-kind distribution that the fixture doesn't represent) | ADR-0011 §3.7 + Risks: the fixture-generator script (`apps/api/scripts/generate-audit-fixture.ts`) walks the production chain (with IDs randomized + ciphertext zero-filled) so the fixture stays current; the post-Release-1 milestones that introduce new chain kinds re-generate the fixture as part of their slice plan. The `--full` flag's `payloadShapeMismatches` array surfaces drift in CI — a fixture that doesn't match the live shape trips the array. The quarterly re-walk under SECURITY.md §9 catches drift between milestone re-generations. Non-negotiable #2. | Fixture-drift is the residual; the per-milestone re-generation + the `payloadShapeMismatches` array are the structural backstop. Documented. |
| T-HD28 | The `payloadShapeMismatches` array depends on schema-validation logic for each audit kind; not every chain kind has a payload-schema validator wired (a 1.5–1.11 kind may have an implicit shape that the verifier doesn't explicitly check). A new optional field added without a schema bump goes undetected | ADR-0011 §3.7: the verifier's payload-schema map covers the "PI-clean by construction" invariant from 1.3 priv-F2 — every kind has a documented payload shape in its source ADR + the typed-emit boundary in `packages/shared-types`. The `--full` flag's payload-schema validator is sourced from the same `AuditEventKind` discriminated union; a kind missing a validator is itself a structural gap that the post-Release-1 hardening backlog absorbs via the existing follow-up flags (`--check-inspections`, `--check-recommendations`, `--check-excel`). The S5 reviewer pass for 1.12 spot-checks the validator coverage. Non-negotiable #2. | Validator-coverage gaps for less-load-bearing kinds are the documented residual; the post-Release-1 forward-defense flags close them. Documented. |
| T-HD29 | A chain that's already tampered with (a hostile rep / a compromised operator account / an insider attack between deploy and verification) fails the verify, but the verifier doesn't say WHO tampered or WHEN — the tamper signal is correct but the forensic trail is incomplete | ADR-0011 §3.7 + Negative tradeoffs + the audit chain's structural posture: the `audit-log-verify.ts --full` detects tamper (hash mismatch or gap); identifying the tamperer requires the auth-log + the session-row + the Fly access logs (out-of-band). The chain's `actor_id` per row identifies WHO emitted the row at the time, not who tampered with it after the fact. A successful tamper would require both DB write access AND the ability to rewrite a chain segment; the chain is append-only at the schema level + the daily cron-run of `audit-log-verify.ts` (per SECURITY.md §9) bounds the tamper-detection window to 24h. The runbook for tamper-detected response is the incident-response playbook (SECURITY.md §7). Non-negotiable #2. | Forensic identification beyond "tamper occurred" requires the audit + access logs together; documented. The single-tenant scope makes the tamper-attribution path short (the rep is the only operator). |
| T-HD30 | Playwright `devices['iPhone 15 Pro']` is an EMULATION — viewport + UA + touch primitives only; the real iOS Safari has quirks (PWA permission scope, Add-to-Home-Screen flow, IndexedDB quota differences, WebKit-specific Service Worker behavior, real touch + haptic + pull-to-refresh) that emulation does not replicate. A regression that only manifests on a real device slips through CI | ADR-0011 §3.8 + Negative tradeoffs: the device emulation is the CI-grade coverage; the deploy runbook's post-deploy smoke test runs on the rep's REAL devices (iOS Safari + Android Chrome) and walks the load-bearing flows. The 4–6 week real-world use window is the additional real-device exercise. The mobile-flow spec covers the documented quirks via explicit assertions (PWA install path on iOS = share-sheet, on Android = `beforeinstallprompt`; IndexedDB quota assertions; SW scope behavior); a real-device-only quirk produces a fast-follow PR. CLAUDE.md #9. | Real-device-only regressions are the documented bound; the post-deploy smoke + the 4–6 week window are the structural backstop. Documented in `mobile-flow.spec.ts` header. |
| T-HD31 | Touch emulation is single-finger + synthetic-event; multi-touch + haptic + pull-to-refresh edge cases need a real device — a swipe-with-velocity gesture (the section-move signature interaction per CLAUDE.md), a long-press, a haptic-feedback cue all behave differently under emulation | ADR-0011 §3.8: the spec covers the documented mobile-primary patterns (touch targets ≥44pt, sticky bottom primary action, bottom tab bar, pull-to-refresh) via Playwright's touch primitives; the velocity-class gestures are documented in the spec's "Limitations" section + flagged for real-device coverage in the post-deploy smoke. The section-move (per the Signature Interactions in CLAUDE.md) is asserted at the touch-event level (touchstart + touchmove + touchend with the expected delta); velocity-based outcomes are tested via the deterministic "swipe past threshold" assertion, not via real momentum. CLAUDE.md #9 + Signature Interactions. | Velocity / haptic / multi-touch limitations are the documented bound; the rep's real-device smoke is the structural backstop. Documented. |
| T-HD32 | The 8 load-bearing mobile flows enumerated in §3.8 (sign-in / first-run / hazard create / action-item move / inspection start+sign / recommendation submit+export / Excel import preview+commit / sync conflict resolution) are the daily rep journey; missing one means a regression in that flow slips through CI | ADR-0011 §3.8: the 8 flows are the rep's daily-use surface, derived from the eight feature ADRs (1.2 / 1.5 / 1.6 / 1.8 / 1.9 / 1.11 / 1.10) — every Release 1 feature has a flow. A future feature (Release 2.x) adds its own mobile flow as a Quality Bar requirement. The S5 reviewer pass walks the flow inventory against the feature surfaces; a missing flow trips review. CLAUDE.md #9 + Mobile-Primary Patterns. | A flow added post-freeze without a spec extension is the residual; the per-PR Quality Bar checkbox is the standing forward-defense. Documented. |
| T-HD33 | Server-side feature detection may rely on the User-Agent string; a Playwright spec with the wrong UA hits the wrong code path (mobile UA but desktop behavior, or vice versa) — false-pass CI on a regression that only manifests under real UA dispatch | ADR-0011 §3.8: Playwright's mobile device emulation sets the correct UA per `devices['iPhone 15 Pro']` (WebKit/iOS Safari UA) and `devices['Pixel 9']` (Chrome/Android UA); the typed-client treats UA as informational only (no server-side feature-gate depends on UA — the SPA is a single bundle served identically to all UAs). The PWA install path differs by UA but is detected client-side via `beforeinstallprompt` (Chromium) vs absence-of (WebKit-iOS); the spec asserts each path explicitly. CLAUDE.md #9. | UA-based dispatch is bounded to PWA install path detection; documented. A future UA-dependent server code path would need its own spec coverage. |
| T-HD34 | The deploy runbook is OPERATOR-RUN; the actual deploy happens out-of-band — a rep without DevOps experience running `fly deploy` for the first time mis-orders the migrations, deploys without the env vars in place, forgets to provision the Tigris bucket with SSE, or hits a Neon migration error mid-deploy and doesn't know how to recover | ADR-0011 §3.9 + the deploy runbook step-by-step procedure: the runbook is granular enough that a first-time-DevOps rep can follow it — Fly + Neon + Tigris + DNS + TLS + env vars + pg-boss + rollback + post-deploy smoke, each as numbered steps with expected outputs. The CI lint that asserts the env var inventory matches `config/workplace.ts` (per the S4 follow-up) catches a runbook-drift problem before deploy. The post-deploy smoke test gates the start of the 4–6 week window; a failed smoke triggers the documented rollback procedure. CLAUDE.md "single-tenant, worker-controlled" + #6. | First-time-DevOps-mistake is the documented residual; the runbook + the lint + the smoke test + the rollback are the layered defense. Documented. |
| T-HD35 | Fly.io deploy is blue-green vs rolling — a mid-deploy session inconsistency (an old API machine serves a stale projection while a new machine serves a fresh one) produces inconsistent rep experience or, worse, a chain anchor that lands on the wrong machine's clock | ADR-0011 §3.9: at single-tenant scale the API runs on a single Fly Machine; the deploy is single-machine-replace (effectively rolling-of-one). A two-machine deploy is on the post-Release-1 backlog if multi-machine scaling becomes a need; the chain anchor's `ts_ms` is server-side from `now()` so any time-skew between machines is bounded by NTP. The runbook documents the single-machine bound + the recommendation to run the post-deploy smoke immediately after deploy completes. Non-negotiable #2. | Multi-machine session-inconsistency is a post-Release-1 surface; single-machine deploy is the structural simplification. Documented. |
| T-HD36 | Neon Postgres migration run order is critical; a migration applied out-of-order silently corrupts the schema (a 0009 sync table created before its prerequisite 0007 inspection table; a 0010 excel-imports row referencing an action_items column added in 0006) | ADR-0011 §3.9 + CLAUDE.md "migrations are append-only": the migration order is 0001..0010 in sequence via the Drizzle Kit migration tooling; the tool refuses to apply migrations out-of-order. The runbook documents the migration command + the post-migration verification (genesis row at idx=0 per ADR-0002, backfill anchor at idx=1, every prior-ADR's table-creation visible via `\dt`). Each prior milestone's migration is in `migrations/` numbered 0001..0010 — the directory listing is the canonical order. CLAUDE.md "migrations are append-only" + #2. | Out-of-order migration is blocked by the Drizzle Kit tool; documented. A manually-applied migration (operator-script for a one-shot fix per T-HD38) is the only path that could land out-of-order, and that path is operator-supervised. |
| T-HD37 | Tigris bucket provisioning forgets the SSE-AES256 + lifecycle policy; new exports + new evidence files land plaintext-at-rest in production, breaking the close-out for 1.7 T-E12 + 1.11 T-X40 + T-X45 + the privacy-by-default invariant | ADR-0011 §3.9 + non-negotiable #4: the deploy runbook documents bucket provisioning as explicit operator steps — `SSE-AES256` flag + versioning + lifecycle policy retention (30 days matching the 1.11 reverse window) + the IAM credentials provisioning. The runbook's post-deploy smoke includes a "list bucket configuration" step that confirms SSE is enabled before declaring deploy complete. A missed SSE flag is caught by the smoke test, not by the rep discovering it months later. CLAUDE.md #4 + #16. | A bucket provisioned without SSE is the residual; the post-deploy smoke is the structural backstop. Documented. |
| T-HD38 | DNS + TLS — ACME / Let's Encrypt cert rotation cadence is operator-managed via Fly; a cert that expires mid-window produces TLS errors mid-flow, blocking the rep's reveal / commit / submit paths (which are require-online per 1.10) | ADR-0011 §3.9: Fly-managed Let's Encrypt certs auto-renew before expiry; the deploy runbook documents the cert-status check + the HSTS preload submission process per SECURITY.md §8. The post-deploy smoke includes a TLS-version check; a renewal failure surfaces in the Fly dashboard + via the `/api/health` endpoint's TLS probe. The runbook covers the manual force-renew procedure for the rare case of an ACME challenge failure. CLAUDE.md "Fly.io (YYZ Toronto primary)." | Cert-rotation failure is bounded by the Fly auto-renew + the runbook; an extended Fly outage during a renewal window is the documented residual (and a separate vendor-concentration concern per T-HD22). Documented. |
| T-HD39 | Workplace-config env vars — a missing `WORKPLACE_DISPLAY_NAME` falls back to empty (correct per #1), but a missing `ZONE_N_NAME` for N=1..10 falls back to "Zone N" defaults (per 1.8 priv-F6 close-out); a deploy without the env vars in place ships generic zone labels and the rep's inspection findings render with placeholder zone names rather than the workplace's actual zone names | ADR-0011 §3.9 + 1.8 priv-F6 close-out + non-negotiable #1: the deploy runbook documents the env var inventory (`WORKPLACE_NAME`, `WORKPLACE_JURISDICTION`, `WORKPLACE_CO_CHAIR_DISPLAY_NAME`, `WORKPLACE_TIMEZONE`, `ZONE_1_NAME`..`ZONE_10_NAME`, etc.) with descriptions + sample values + the "never commit these to git" warning. The CI lint (per the S4 follow-up) asserts every env var documented in the runbook is referenced in `config/workplace.ts` AND every env var referenced in code is documented in the runbook — drift in either direction trips the lint. The fallback to "Zone N" is intentional + safe (per non-negotiable #14 stable IDs); the runbook documents the fallback so a rep who sees "Zone 1" rather than their workplace's label knows to set the env var. CLAUDE.md #1 + #14. | Missing-env-var-with-fallback is the documented residual; the lint + the runbook + the fallback safety are the structural backstop. Documented. |
| T-HD40 | pg-boss worker setup — the worker process exists in production from day 1 with zero jobs registered; a future PR could accidentally register a buggy job that runs on the production worker, OR the worker process itself could be misconfigured (wrong DB role, wrong schema, wrong polling interval) | ADR-0011 §3.9 + Negative tradeoffs + ADR-0009 §"Follow-ups": the pg-boss `boss.schema_create` migration runs as part of the deploy as a separate migration outside the Drizzle 0001..0010 sequence; the worker process is a distinct Fly Machine command (`bun run apps/api/src/workers/index.ts`) running alongside the API but on a separate machine so a worker failure does not cascade to API availability. Zero jobs are registered in 1.12; the worker idles. Per-PR review discipline is the bound on buggy-job-registration; the worker's separate-machine deploy posture means a rollback of the worker doesn't roll back the API. CLAUDE.md "pg-boss (Postgres-native)" + #2. | Buggy-job-registration is bounded by per-PR review + the worker's isolation; the post-Release-1 jobs (sync_idempotency TTL sweep, dead-letter retry sweep, etc.) land with their own slice plans + review. Documented. |
| T-HD41 | Rollback procedure for a bad deploy is one-way at the schema layer (migrations are append-only per non-negotiable #14 — wait, #14 is zone stability; the migration append-only rule is per CLAUDE.md "migrations are append-only" + the Quality Bar checkbox). A 1.x-introduced migration that breaks something requires a manually-crafted rollback migration OR a restore-from-backup | ADR-0011 §3.9 "Rollback procedure" + CLAUDE.md "migrations are append-only": the runbook documents the rollback layers — (1) `fly deploy --image <previous-image-sha>` rolls the API + web machines back; (2) the migration is one-way at the schema layer; a buggy migration requires a manually-crafted rollback migration written + reviewed in a fast-follow PR; (3) Tigris buckets are versioned so any objects written by the failed deploy can be reverted via version restore. At single-tenant scale the operator has full DB access + the documented escalation path. The post-deploy smoke catches a bad deploy before the 4–6 week window starts. CLAUDE.md "migrations are append-only" + #2. | Manually-crafted rollback migrations are the documented bound; the smoke-test gate prevents a bad deploy from reaching production-use. Documented. |
| T-HD42 | Post-deploy smoke test (sign in + first-run + 1 hazard capture + 1 chain row verify + import-history view + print stylesheet check + sign out) is the gate on the 4–6 week window's start; a smoke that PASSES but misses a real regression (the smoke's coverage is narrow by design) lets a broken deploy through | ADR-0011 §3.9 + §"Post-deploy smoke test" + ROADMAP.md line 175: the smoke is 8 manual steps covering the load-bearing daily flows; full regression coverage is the CI suite + the mobile Playwright specs that ran pre-merge. The smoke is the END-TO-END sanity check on the deployed system, not the regression net. A regression that passes the smoke surfaces in the 4–6 week window via real use; the response is a fast-follow PR. The runbook documents the smoke as "necessary but not sufficient." CLAUDE.md "default to worker safety." | Smoke-coverage-gap is the documented residual; the CI suite + the 4–6 week window are the structural backstop. Documented. |
| T-HD43 | S4 docs land before S1-S3 verify completes — a release-readiness doc references findings that don't exist yet (the security checklist's Section B cites T-HD entries before the WCAG audit lands; the pen-test plan's manual-cases section cites surfaces before the fuzz harness lands) | ADR-0011 §3.10 slice-order: S1 (WCAG + print) → S2 (fuzz + audit-log-verify --full) → S3 (mobile Playwright) → S4 (docs) → S5 (review). The order matters: docs land AFTER the verification surfaces exist so the docs reference real artifacts; the S4 commit references the SHAs of the prior slices. An S5 reviewer who spots a forward-reference in S4 (a doc citing a non-existent file) moves the doc back to S4 for fixup. CLAUDE.md "tests pass" pre-merge checkbox per slice. | Slice-order drift is bounded by the S5 review; a forward-reference is a structural error caught at review. Documented. |
| T-HD44 | S5 review is LIGHTER than prior milestone S5s because the scope is verification rather than new features; a real bug missed by the lighter review ships a regression to the rep's hands | ADR-0011 §3.10 S5 + the prior-milestone S5 patterns (1.6 / 1.7 / 1.8 / 1.9 / 1.10 / 1.11 each had a substantive S5 review pass that surfaced real findings): the 1.12 S5 reviewer pass is scoped to (a) every non-negotiable has a checklist row, (b) every T-# has a row, (c) every deferred item has a "lands in" pointer, (d) the deploy runbook covers every machine + secret + env var, (e) the rollback is exercisable. The lighter scope reflects the absence of new feature surfaces; the rigor is the same on the verification artifacts. A missed bug in a verification artifact surfaces post-deploy in the 4–6 week window. Non-negotiable #2. | Lighter-review-tradeoff is the documented bound; the 4–6 week window's real-world use is the structural backstop. Documented. |
| T-HD45 | The post-Release-1 backlog of 20 deferred items has a documented "lands in [post-Release-1 milestone X]" pointer per item; the threat is that a deferred item is forgotten + ships in R2 still deferred, AND the security checklist's Section C carries stale "lands in" pointers (the pointer says R1-post but the item never gets re-prioritized) | ADR-0011 §"Out of scope" + §3.3 Section C + ROADMAP.md Release 2 framing: each deferred item carries the source ADR + the source threat row + the accepted-risk reasoning + the "lands in" pointer. The post-Release-1 milestones are sequenced in the ROADMAP; each milestone's bootstrap reads the checklist's Section C + claims the items it covers + updates the pointer. An item with no claiming milestone after R2 ships triggers a "backlog ratchet" — escalated to operator + re-prioritized OR explicitly marked "won't fix" with a documented reason. Non-negotiable #2 + #4 (the rep is informed of every residual). | A genuine "forgotten residual" is the documented bound; the per-milestone ratchet is the structural backstop. The 4–6 week window's real-world use surfaces items the rep wants prioritized. Documented. |
| T-HD46 | The CI pipeline IS the release gate; a CI failure mode that doesn't fail-closed (silent skip on a missing job dependency, flaky retry that succeeds on the second run + masks a real failure, exit-code masking via `|| true` or `set +e`) lets a broken commit through to deploy | ADR-0011 §3.10 + CLAUDE.md "tests pass" + the existing `.github/workflows/ci.yml` shape: every job exits non-zero on failure; no `|| true`; no `continue-on-error`; flaky-test retry is bounded to a known retry-count + the retry result is logged; the pre-merge required-status-check covers every job (`verify`, `e2e`, `docker-build`). The S5 reviewer pass spot-checks the workflow file for masking patterns. CLAUDE.md "tests pass" + "no console.log in committed code" + per-PR Quality Bar. | Workflow-config-drift is the documented bound; the S5 review + the per-PR review discipline are the structural backstop. A flaky test that always succeeds on retry is the documented residual (per T-HD4 + standing operational hygiene). Documented. |
| T-HD47 | The Fly.io region is `ca-central-1` (Toronto YYZ) for PIPEDA + Canadian data residency; a misconfigured deploy that lands in `us-east` or any non-Canadian region is a non-negotiable violation (Canadian worker data crosses the border, defeating the privacy posture + risking PIPEDA enforcement) | ADR-0011 §3.9 + CLAUDE.md Tech Stack ("Hosting: Fly.io (YYZ Toronto primary)" + "Database: Neon Postgres (ca-central-1)") + non-negotiable #4: the deploy runbook documents the region as `yyz` (Fly's code for YYZ Toronto) explicitly + the `fly.toml`'s `primary_region` field is `yyz` + the Neon project provisions in `aws-ca-central-1`. The post-deploy smoke includes a `fly status` check that confirms the running region. The CI workflow's deploy job (`fly deploy --app jhsc-api`) inherits the region from `fly.toml` so a misconfiguration would require an explicit override. Non-negotiable #4 + #6 + the PIPEDA framing in SECURITY.md §6. | Region-misconfiguration is the documented residual; the `fly.toml` + the post-deploy smoke + the deploy runbook are the layered defense. A deliberate region override would be visible in PR diff + caught at review. Documented. |
| T-HD48 | The workplace KEK + signing key are the LOAD-BEARING secrets; they live in Fly Secrets; a single point of failure (Fly account compromise, Fly outage, accidental secret deletion) cascades to ENCRYPTED-DATA LOSS for the entire workplace | ADR-0011 §3.6 Fly Secrets backup + T-HD23: the rep MUST maintain an out-of-band passphrase-wrapped copy of the KEK + signing key physically separate from their laptop — printed paper in a sealed envelope OR an encrypted USB key in a physical safe OR a passphrase-protected backup in a separate-vendor password manager. The runbook documents the cold-storage backup as a deploy-time + post-rotation operator obligation + the recovery procedure for a Fly-side loss. The KEK rotation script (post-Release-1 backlog) lands the in-place rotation; until then a rotation is a fresh deploy with a fresh KEK + a re-encrypt operator script for the prior data. CLAUDE.md "encrypt sensitive fields at the application layer with keys you control" + #2 + #4. | Cold-storage-backup-loss + Fly-side-loss simultaneously is the catastrophic residual; the rep's physical separation of the backup is the structural backstop. Documented in §3.6 + the runbook. |
| T-HD49 | A regression-report path from the 4–6 week real-world-use window doesn't exist — the rep finds a bug, doesn't know whether to file an issue, amend the runbook, or escalate to a fast-follow PR; bugs sit unreported and the window expires without surfacing real issues | ADR-0011 §3.9 + ROADMAP.md line 175 + the post-Release-1 framing: the deploy runbook documents the rep's "report a regression" path explicitly — (a) capture the issue in a GitHub issue with the load-bearing flow that surfaced it; (b) if the issue blocks a load-bearing flow (sign-in, hazard capture, chain anchor failing, reveal failing), label it `release-1-blocker` and pause R2 planning until fixed; (c) if the issue is non-blocking (mobile-quirk, copy nit, accessibility miss), label it `release-1-window` and absorb into a fast-follow PR; (d) escalation path to operator-script for chain-integrity issues. The runbook is the rep's reference. CLAUDE.md "default to worker safety." | A rep who doesn't read the runbook is the documented bound; the per-issue label + the runbook's explicit framing are the structural backstop. Documented. |

**No new audit kinds in 1.12.** Milestone 1.12 ships **zero** new `AuditEventKind` values. The existing chain-anchored kinds from 1.2 (`auth.signin`, `auth.session_anomaly`, ...), 1.3 (`audit.genesis`, `audit.backfill_anchor`), 1.5 (`hazard.created`, `hazard.status_changed`, `hazard.read`), 1.6 (`action_item.created`, `action_item.moved`, `action_item.move_undone`, `action_item.updated`), 1.7 (`evidence.uploaded`, `evidence.read`, `evidence.list_accessed`), 1.8 (`inspection.created`, `inspection_finding.created`, `inspection_finding.promoted`, `inspection_finding.read`, `inspection.signed`, `inspection.exported`, `inspection.export.downloaded`, `audit.inspection_template.seeded`), 1.9 (`recommendation.drafted`, `recommendation.draft_patched`, `recommendation.submitted`, `recommendation.response_captured`, `recommendation.resolved`, `recommendation.withdrawn`, `recommendation.exported`, `recommendation.export.downloaded`, `audit.workplace_signing_key.seeded`), 1.10 (`sync_conflict.revealed`), and 1.11 (`excel_import.uploaded`, `excel_import.committed`, `excel_import.reversed`) compose the full chain payload contract. The `audit-log-verify.ts --full` flag (§3.7) walks every kind against its documented payload shape — the chain payload contract is the **no-regression backstop** for 1.12, and a future PR that adds a new kind without updating the verifier's schema map trips `payloadShapeMismatches` on the next CI fixture run.

**The 4–6 week real-world-use window is the deliberate UAT.** Per ROADMAP.md line 175, the rep uses the deployed app for 4–6 weeks before Release 2 starts. This window is the structured replacement for staged-rollout / canary / per-customer-cohort patterns that don't apply at single-tenant scope. The window's gates: the post-deploy smoke (§3.9) starts it; the daily cron-run of `audit-log-verify.ts` (per SECURITY.md §9) bounds tamper-detection latency to 24h; any HIGH-or-CRITICAL pen-test finding from the operator-run scan (§3.4) within the window pauses R2 planning; the rep's "report a regression" path (T-HD49) feeds fast-follow PRs.

**The post-Release-1 backlog is the explicit "what didn't ship" record.** The 20 deferred items enumerated in ADR-0011 §"Out of scope" (workplace key rotation, action-bound step-up tokens, Dexie at-rest encryption, conflict UI Apply pipeline, Tigris orphan-ciphertext GC, evidence/inspection_finding/recommendation redaction tables, audit-log-verify forward-defense flags, PAdES embedded signatures, `excel_import.cancelled` + `recommendation.read` audit kinds, `inspection_finding.read` chain anchor refinements, pg-boss-backed sync_idempotency TTL sweep + sync rate-limit, SheetJS CDN upgrade past 0.18.5, per-attendee encryption for inspection findings, `before_state_json` envelope encryption, source workbook archival under workplace KEK, Dexie preview persistence for excel-import, server-side EXIF strip for upload-from-file fallback) are each enumerated in the security pre-launch checklist's Section C (§3.3) with a "lands in [post-Release-1 milestone X]" pointer. There are no silent residuals; the rep signs off knowing both what's enforced and what's deferred. The per-PR review discipline + the per-milestone ratchet (T-HD45) ensure no deferred item ships in R2 still deferred without a documented reason.

### 2.13 Meeting Lifecycle (M2.1)

Milestone 2.1 is the **operational heart** of Release 2: the Minutes module's core lifecycle — meeting creation, attendance capture, section-by-section workflow, adjournment, and 4-signer counter-signed finalization (Worker Co-Chair in-app via step-up+passkey; Mgmt Co-Chair, Warehouse Mgr, Plant Mgr via off-app attestation upload). It introduces five new tables (`meetings`, `meeting_sections`, `meeting_attendance`, `meeting_inspection_review`, `meeting_signatures`), envelope-encrypted section notes + attendee display names, an agenda template with versioning + seed, and a live meeting view that operates offline through the 1.10 sync queue. The threat posture is **structurally different** from prior milestones: this is the first surface where (a) **identity-of-attendees is the primary sensitive payload** (not just narrative content), (b) **a multi-party counter-signature flow** binds the workflow's terminal state (4 signers, mixed in-app + off-app modalities), (c) the **finalization gate could be weaponized** to delay OHSA s.9(20) recommendation timelines or chill rep action (non-negotiable #7), and (d) **two co-chair roles' adversarial relationship is in-scope** (the worker co-chair is the user; the management co-chair is a counterparty whose signature is required but whose refusal must not block the worker's rights). The mitigations below cite the architect's brief for M2.1 (parallel ADR-0012) by surface name; where a mitigation calls out a forward-seam the architect should close, it's flagged in the closing report. Non-negotiables most active here: #1 (no names in source — workplace + signer names from env), #2 (chain-of-custody on every transition), #4 (privacy-by-default — attendee names + notes envelope-encrypted), #7 (rights-protective copy — finalization MUST NOT discourage action on recommendations), #12 (action items are first-class — the meeting's recommendation section produces / links action items, never replaces them).

| # | Threat | Affected surfaces | Mitigation | Residual |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| T-ML1 | Attendee display name leaks via plaintext to Postgres — the envelope encryption boundary on `meeting_attendance.display_name_ct` is silently bypassed by a route that writes `display_name` plaintext into a sibling column, or a forgotten Drizzle column shape returns plaintext on the GET projection | `meeting_attendance` table; `POST /api/meetings/:id/attendance`; `GET /api/meetings/:id` | The `meeting_attendance` table has NO plaintext name column — only `display_name_ct` (per-row DEK, workplace KEK) and `role` (`worker_rep` / `management` / `guest`) + `attendance_state` (`present` / `regrets` / `absent`) per the architect's brief. The Drizzle schema in `apps/api/src/db/schema/meetings.ts` enforces the shape; integration tests assert `pg_dump` of the test row contains no plaintext name. The create route accepts `displayName: string` in the request body, sealing it via `sealField` before INSERT. The GET projection runs `openField` per row only after authn; the projection type excludes `display_name_ct` and includes `displayName: string`. Same priv-F2 invariant as 1.3 (typed payloads at the boundary). | Same scope as T-AI1/T-H1 — DB-level attacker gets ciphertext; KEK is the bound. Acceptable. |
| T-ML2 | Attendance roster reveals identity of dissenting worker rep to management — a rep who marks "regrets" because they object to a meeting topic is distinguishable from a rep marked "absent" (unannounced), and the management co-chair reading the finalized minutes can use the distinction to target the dissenter for follow-up reprisal | `meeting_attendance.attendance_state`; finalized minutes export (PDF, included in counter-signature packet) | The `attendance_state` enum is `present` / `regrets` / `absent` per OHSA-aligned committee minute convention; the rep records their own state at meeting-open via the attendance capture UI. The UI's copy on the regrets/absent picker explicitly says "Either state is acceptable; the JHSC does not record a reason." No `regrets_reason` field exists; no narrative is captured. The audit chain row for `meeting.attendance_recorded` carries `{attendeeId, state}` only — no reason, no narrative. For the worker co-chair's print copy, both `regrets` and `absent` render as "Not present" in the management-distributed export; the internal-only roster (under step-up + worker-co-chair-only route) retains the distinction. Rights-protective copy review (per the closing controls) covers the picker text. | The internal-vs-external roster split is a UI affordance, not a structural separation — a worker co-chair who shares the internal export with management has shared the distinction. Documented as a usage-policy bound; the rep is the privileged party. |
| T-ML3 | Co-chair identity forge — a non-co-chair authenticated rep creates a meeting (`POST /api/meetings`) and the row is anchored as if the co-chair created it, falsifying the meeting record's authorship before the signature workflow even starts | `POST /api/meetings`; `meetings.created_by`; `meetings.workplace_co_chair_actor_id` | The `POST /api/meetings` route requires the authenticated rep's `actor_role === 'worker_co_chair'` per the workplace-config-derived role assignment (env-driven per non-negotiable #1; the co-chair's actor_id is bound at deploy time via `WORKPLACE_CO_CHAIR_ACTOR_ID`). A non-co-chair rep gets 403. The audit chain row `meeting.created` carries `{meetingId, scheduledStart, createdByActorId}` and the verify pass cross-checks `createdByActorId === WORKPLACE_CO_CHAIR_ACTOR_ID` for every emitted row. Single-co-chair scope per CLAUDE.md. | Co-chair credential theft is the bound (covered by 1.2 auth posture — passkey-primary, TOTP fallback, step-up on sensitive paths). Acceptable; same bound as every privileged action in 1.5–1.12. |
| T-ML4 | Counter-signature bypass — meeting marked `finalized` without all 4 signers (Worker Co-Chair + Mgmt Co-Chair + Warehouse Mgr + Plant Mgr); the finalization transition fires without the 4-of-4 invariant | `meetings.status` (`draft` / `adjourned` / `signed_partial` / `finalized`); `POST /api/meetings/:id/finalize`; `meeting_signatures` table | The finalization route opens a Drizzle transaction, SELECTs `COUNT(*) FROM meeting_signatures WHERE meeting_id = $1 AND signature_state = 'signed'` with `FOR UPDATE`, and only writes `meetings.status = 'finalized'` if `count = 4` AND the four signer-role slots (`worker_co_chair`, `management_co_chair`, `warehouse_manager`, `plant_manager`) are each filled with exactly one signature. The transition graph (`packages/shared-types/src/meeting-transitions.ts`) is a pure function; the route validates `currentStatus → 'finalized'` against the graph (only `signed_partial → finalized` is legal). The audit chain row `meeting.finalized` carries `{meetingId, signerActorIds: [4]}`; the verify pass cross-checks the array length. | A handler bug could drift the graph — covered by unit tests on the pure helper exhaustively asserting legal/illegal pairs (same pattern as 1.5 T-H2, 1.6 T-AI3). |
| T-ML5 | External signer attestation forgery — the Mgmt Co-Chair, Warehouse Mgr, or Plant Mgr signs a paper copy off-app, the worker co-chair photographs/scans it for upload as attestation; between the off-app signing and the in-app upload, the paper is altered (forged signature, swapped page, edited body text) | `meeting_signatures.attestation_hash`; `meeting_signatures.attestation_evidence_id`; `POST /api/meetings/:id/signatures/external` | The external-signer attestation upload pipeline reuses the 1.7 evidence flow: the photo/scan is hashed client-side (SHA-256) BEFORE upload; the hash is bound to the meeting_signature row at insert time; the photo itself goes through the Tigris presign flow with `Content-MD5` enforcement (same as 1.7 T-E2/T-E3). The signature row stores `attestation_hash`, `attestation_evidence_id`, `signed_at_claimed` (the date the external signer wrote on paper, captured by the worker co-chair), `signed_at_recorded` (the server's `now()` at upload time), and a `chain_of_custody_note_ct` (envelope-encrypted free-text the worker co-chair captures: "Paper signed in my presence at 2pm; uploaded 4pm same day"). Audit chain row `meeting.signature_attested_external` carries `{meetingId, signerRole, attestationHash, claimedSignedAt, recordedAt}`. The forgery bound is honest: the worker co-chair is the witness; the chain-of-custody note + the photo hash + the timing pair are the evidentiary record an arbitrator weighs. | Paper-altered-between-sign-and-upload is the documented residual; the chain-of-custody note + the timing pair are the structural backstop. The arbitrator's weighing is the human bound. Documented in the closing "Known gaps" section. |
| T-ML6 | Step-up freshness skipped on worker co-chair signature — the `POST /api/meetings/:id/signatures/worker-co-chair` route accepts a stale `step_up_until` JWT claim (one issued hours earlier for a different purpose), and the co-chair's signature is recorded without a fresh passkey/TOTP prompt — defeating the evidentiary weight of the signature | `POST /api/meetings/:id/signatures/worker-co-chair`; `step_up_until` JWT claim; passkey/WebAuthn challenge | The worker co-chair signature route requires step-up with `maxAgeSeconds = 60` (consistent with 1.6 T-AI4 undo, 1.7 evidence reveal, 1.8 inspection.signed) AND `factorRequired = 'passkey'` (passkey-only; TOTP is rejected for this endpoint — the signature is the highest-trust action in the workflow). The route verifies (a) the `step_up_until` claim is `> now() - 60s`, (b) the `factor` claim is `passkey`, (c) a fresh WebAuthn assertion is bound to the signature row's `signature_evidence_payload` (the assertion's `clientDataJSON` includes a challenge generated specifically for this meeting signature, with `meetingId` in the challenge). A stale or TOTP-only step-up returns 401-StepUp + the modal opens. Audit chain row `meeting.signature_attested_worker_co_chair` carries `{meetingId, signerActorId, webauthnAssertionHash, recordedAt}`. | Passkey credential theft is the bound (same as T-ML3). The WebAuthn challenge binding to `meetingId` prevents cross-meeting replay (T-ML8). Acceptable. |
| T-ML7 | Signature ordering attack — the worker co-chair's signature is recorded BEFORE the management co-chair's to manipulate the audit timeline, making it appear that the worker side endorsed a draft that the management side later modified, OR vice versa | `meeting_signatures.signed_at_recorded`; audit chain row ordering | The four signature rows each carry `signed_at_recorded = now()` server-side; the chain anchors emit in the order the signatures are submitted to the API; the chain's `idx` field is monotonic per the 1.3 invariant. The audit chain row for each signature includes the meeting's content hash (`meeting_content_hash`) at the moment of signing — a hash over the meeting's adjourned content (sections, notes ciphertext IDs, attendance, action item snapshot) plus the meeting's `adjourned_at` timestamp. If the management co-chair signs at time T1 and the worker co-chair signs at T2 > T1, both signatures carry the SAME `meeting_content_hash` because the meeting content was frozen at adjournment. A modification between signatures is structurally impossible: the `adjourned → signed_partial → finalized` transition graph rejects any write to sections / attendance / notes (the meeting is read-only post-adjournment). The order of signatures is the order they were captured; an arbitrator reading the chain sees the timestamps in submission order. | Order-of-signing is meaningful evidence, not a vulnerability — the chain records it faithfully. The "manipulation" framing is bounded because the content is frozen. Documented. |
| T-ML8 | Replay attack — a previously-signed attestation (paper photo + hash for one meeting) is re-bound to a different meeting by re-uploading the same photo + hash with a different `meetingId` in the request | `POST /api/meetings/:id/signatures/external`; `meeting_signatures.attestation_hash`; Tigris evidence row | The external-signer attestation upload route INSERTs into `meeting_signatures` with a UNIQUE constraint on `(attestation_hash, signer_role)` — the same paper hash cannot be bound to two signer-role slots across the workplace's meeting history. The attestation evidence row in Tigris is linked via `attestation_evidence_id` with a 1:1 FK from `meeting_signatures.attestation_evidence_id → evidence.id`; the evidence row's `linked_resource_type` is `meeting_signature` (per the 1.7 polymorphic FK pattern, T-AI8). A second meeting attempting the same hash returns 409 with the explanation "this attestation is already bound to meeting M-XXX."
