For the worker co-chair WebAuthn signature, the challenge is per-meeting (T-ML6 mitigation) so replay across meetings fails the assertion verify. | A genuine duplicate paper (the same signer signed the same statement for two meetings) would trip the UNIQUE constraint — the worker co-chair re-photographs or the signer re-signs. Documented as an operational friction, not a bypass. |
| T-ML9 | Sensitive notes envelope leaks via API response — the `GET /api/meetings/:id` route returns ALL section notes plaintext including notes from sections the requesting rep doesn't need (a guest viewer route, a public-share-link route, an export route that should redact in-camera sections) | `GET /api/meetings/:id`; `meeting_sections.notes_ct`; export PDF generation route | The `meeting_sections.notes_ct` column is envelope-encrypted (per-row DEK, workplace KEK); the GET projection runs `openField` per section row only after authn. There is NO guest viewer route in M2.1 (single-tenant scope; every authenticated rep sees the same data, same scope as 1.5–1.11). There is NO public-share-link route. The export PDF generation route (per non-negotiable #16) runs server-side with step-up, decrypts each section, and writes the PDF with the output document hash audit-logged. For sections marked `in_camera` (a section-level flag the chair can set during the meeting), the export PDF redacts the notes body with a "[in-camera deliberation — not in published minutes]" placeholder; the internal export retains the body. Same priv-F2 invariant as 1.3 — the projection type excludes `notes_ct` and includes `notes: string`. | The `in_camera` redaction is a UI affordance; a worker co-chair who exports the internal version and shares it has shared the in-camera body. Documented as a usage-policy bound. |
| T-ML10 | Section notes survive after meeting deletion (orphan rows) — a `DELETE /api/meetings/:id` (for an erroneously-created meeting that was never adjourned) removes the `meetings` row but leaves `meeting_sections`, `meeting_attendance`, `meeting_signatures`, and `meeting_inspection_review` rows orphaned in the DB with encrypted notes still readable via direct table query | `DELETE /api/meetings/:id`; FK cascade behavior on child tables | All child tables (`meeting_sections`, `meeting_attendance`, `meeting_signatures`, `meeting_inspection_review`) have `ON DELETE CASCADE` from `meetings.id`; the Drizzle migration includes integration tests that assert child rows are deleted when the parent is. The `DELETE /api/meetings/:id` route is restricted to `meetings.status = 'draft'` (a meeting that has been adjourned or partially-signed cannot be deleted; the only path is to finalize-with-zero-content or to leave it in the audit trail). Step-up required. Audit chain row `meeting.deleted` carries `{meetingId, deletedByActorId, sectionsDeletedCount, attendanceDeletedCount}`. The 1.3 KEK rotation runbook bounds in-flight encrypted rows; a deleted row's ciphertext is unrecoverable once the row is dropped (Postgres tombstone + Neon vacuum is the bound). | A row that was returned to a client cache (Dexie) before deletion may persist client-side. The 1.10 sync queue's tombstone-emit pattern propagates the delete; a Dexie cache that hasn't synced will hold a stale copy. Documented forward-seam — covered by the offline section below (T-ML15+). |
| T-ML11 | Meeting notes reveal incident-investigation deliberation pre-publication — a section discussing an active incident-investigation (witness analysis, employer-side-conduct concerns) is readable by every authenticated rep including a rep whose role doesn't need it, leaking deliberation that should stay co-chair-only | `meeting_sections.section_type`; `meeting_sections.notes_ct`; `GET /api/meetings/:id` projection | Single-tenant scope per CLAUDE.md: every authenticated rep sees the same data; multi-tier visibility (co-chair-only sections) is OUT of scope for M2.1 — the forward-seam aligns with the multi-rep role-separation pattern flagged in 1.5 T-H10 + 1.6 T-AI9. Until role-separation lands, the `in_camera` flag (T-ML9) is the structural affordance; a section marked `in_camera` is redacted in the published-export but visible to authenticated reps. The architect's brief should consider whether a `co_chair_only` section type is in-scope for M2.1; if not, document the forward-seam. | Co-chair-only visibility is a forward-seam to a later release (likely R2 role-separation or R3 multi-co-chair); documented. The architect should flag whether the M2.1 schema includes a `visibility` column to seed the forward-seam without exercising it. |
| T-ML12 | Action item snapshot diverges from live state in a way that misrepresents the meeting record — the meeting's frozen-at-adjournment snapshot of the action item board ("what items were open at the time of this meeting") drifts from the live action_items table if a post-meeting move updates the live state, and an arbitrator reading the snapshot months later sees state that doesn't match the chain | `meetings.action_items_snapshot_hash`; `meeting_sections.notes_ct` (for items discussed); snapshot generation in `POST /api/meetings/:id/adjourn` | The adjournment route generates a content-hash over `(action_items.id, action_items.section, action_items.status, action_items.flag_state)` for every open action item at the moment of adjournment; the hash is stored in `meetings.action_items_snapshot_hash` AND a per-meeting denormalized snapshot table (`meeting_action_item_snapshot`) records the per-item state with the meeting_id. Post-meeting changes to `action_items.section` write to `action_item_moves` (per 1.6) and never modify the snapshot table. The export PDF includes the snapshot view; an arbitrator reading the meeting record sees the frozen state. Audit chain row `meeting.adjourned` carries `{meetingId, snapshotHash, openActionItemCount}`. The verify pass cross-checks the snapshot hash against the snapshot table's content. | Snapshot table grows linearly with meetings × open items; at single-tenant scale (24 meetings/year × ~40 open items) the row count is bounded. Documented. |
| T-ML13 | Adjournment metrics manipulated by editing audit-chain rows (chain tamper) — the meeting's "auto-generated key metrics" (open items count, items closed this meeting, recommendations raised, attendance percentage) are stored in `meetings.adjournment_metrics_json` and could be edited post-adjournment to misrepresent the meeting's productivity | `meetings.adjournment_metrics_json`; `POST /api/meetings/:id/adjourn` | The `adjournment_metrics_json` is computed server-side at the moment of adjournment from the live tables; it's stored in the meetings row AND the same metrics are embedded in the `meeting.adjourned` chain anchor payload (`{meetingId, openItemsCount, closedThisMeetingCount, recommendationsRaisedCount, attendancePercent}`). The `meetings` row's adjournment_metrics_json field is read-only post-adjournment (the transition graph rejects updates to adjourned meetings, T-ML4 pattern). A direct SQL UPDATE that bypasses the route would diverge from the chain; the `audit-log-verify.ts --full` flag's payload-shape map (1.12 T-HD28) cross-checks the row's metrics against the chain row's payload. | Same bound as 1.6 T-AI2 (manual SQL UPDATE detection-only at the DB level; documented). The verify-pass detection is the structural backstop. |
| T-ML14 | Quorum compliance falsified — the worker co-chair convenes a meeting without the OHSA-required quorum (≥1 worker rep + ≥1 management rep per s.9(18)) but records attendance with a phantom present worker rep to make the meeting record appear compliant; the quorum-check is purely client-side and could be bypassed | `meeting_attendance.attendance_state`; quorum-check helper; `POST /api/meetings/:id/adjourn` | Quorum is computed server-side at adjournment time: a pure function in `packages/shared-types/src/meeting-quorum.ts` takes the attendance roster + role distribution + jurisdiction (Ontario OHSA s.9(18) requires ≥half of members AND ≥1 worker rep + ≥1 management rep; federal CLC Part II s.135.1 has a similar requirement). The adjournment route runs the function; non-quorum meetings can adjourn but the meeting record is flagged `quorum_state = 'not_met'` (a meeting can still be valid as an informational session; the JHSC convention is to record non-quorum meetings as such, not to hide them). The chain anchor `meeting.adjourned` carries `quorumState` in the payload; an arbitrator reading the chain sees the truth. The phantom-attendee threat reduces to T-ML2 (attendance forgery) — the attendance roster is the rep's input; the rep is the privileged party; the chain records who recorded what. The quorum rules themselves come from the legal corpus (M1.4 forward-seam — the citation is rendered in the UI; the helper is pure). | Phantom attendance is bounded by the rep's discipline; the chain records the roster the rep entered. Documented; same bound as T-H5 (rep types a real name into a free-text field). |
| T-ML15 | Two co-chairs (single-tenant invariant violated by attacker) write conflicting meeting states from offline devices — a session-hijacker on a second device records a different meeting in parallel, and both devices push to the sync queue with the same `meetingId`, producing two divergent finalized meetings | 1.10 sync queue; `meetings.id` uniqueness; `POST /api/sync/queue` | The `meetings.id` is a UUID generated client-side at meeting creation; the sync queue's idempotency layer (1.10 T-S4, T-S5) UNIQUEs the `(idempotency_key, actor_id)` pair. Two devices sharing the same `actor_id` (a session-hijacker on a second device IS the same actor from the chain's perspective) writing different `meetingId` UUIDs produce two distinct meeting rows — neither is "conflicting" per se; the chain records both. The single-co-chair invariant per CLAUDE.md means there's no legitimate second-device-writing-different-meeting scenario; a session-hijacker writing on a second device is covered by 1.2 auth (session anomaly detection, refresh-token rotation, `webauthn_challenges` single-use). The Lucia session row `last_ip` + `last_user_agent` columns surface anomalies. | Session hijack is bounded by 1.2 auth; multi-device legitimate use is documented (the rep using their phone + laptop). Two-meeting divergence is recorded by the chain; the rep reconciles via the standard UI. Documented. |
| T-ML16 | Sync queue replays a meeting creation, producing duplicate records — the 1.10 sync queue retries a POST after a network error, the second POST lands AFTER the first succeeded, and two `meetings` rows are created with the same client-side intent but different server-side IDs | 1.10 sync queue retry path; `POST /api/meetings`; `meetings_idempotency_key_unique` constraint | The 1.10 sync queue carries an `Idempotency-Key` header (per 1.10 T-S4/T-S5); the `POST /api/meetings` route uses the key as the dedupe primitive — the server-side INSERT is gated by `INSERT ... ON CONFLICT (idempotency_key, actor_id) DO NOTHING RETURNING *`. A retry hits the same key, gets the same row back (or the existing-row response per 1.10's idempotency contract). The `meetings.id` is the client-side UUID, NOT a server-generated sequence — the retry can't produce a different ID because the client-side UUID is bound at first-attempt. Audit chain row `meeting.created` is emitted once per idempotency key; the chain's `idx` is monotonic. | Same bound as 1.10 idempotency posture; documented. |
| T-ML17 | An attacker re-uploads an offline-queued mutation with a different actor_id — a worker rep's laptop is stolen; the attacker extracts the queued sync payload from IndexedDB and re-submits it under their own session, hoping to commit the rep's queued work under the attacker's identity | 1.10 sync queue; IndexedDB Dexie store; `POST /api/sync/queue` | The 1.10 sync queue payload contract requires the `Idempotency-Key` AND the `actor_id` to match between the queue row and the submitting session; the server-side route rejects payloads where the request session's `actor_id` differs from the queue row's `actor_id` (the queue row carries the actor_id at enqueue time). The attacker re-submitting under their own session would either (a) be rejected because the actor_id mismatch (if the queue row's actor_id is honored), or (b) commit the work under the attacker's actor_id (if the route uses the request session's actor_id) — the chain records the COMMITTING actor, not the QUEUE-ENQUEUING actor; the chain row's `actor_id` is the truth. Dexie at-rest encryption is a documented forward-seam (1.12 ADR-0011 §"Out of scope" — Dexie at-rest encryption is post-Release-1 backlog). Until Dexie at-rest encryption lands, the residual is real: a stolen unlocked laptop with an unsynced queue is a risk. | Dexie at-rest encryption is the forward-seam; documented in 1.12 ADR-0011 backlog. The structural backstop is the OS-level full-disk encryption the rep is responsible for. Documented. |
| T-ML18 | External signer (employer-side role) gains read access to encrypted notes via signing flow — the Mgmt Co-Chair, Warehouse Mgr, or Plant Mgr submits a paper attestation for upload, and the upload pathway accidentally returns the meeting's decrypted notes in the API response, leaking deliberation content to a counter-party who shouldn't read it | `POST /api/meetings/:id/signatures/external` route response; meeting notes envelope | The external-signer attestation upload is run by the worker co-chair (the authenticated rep), not the external signer themselves. The external signer never authenticates to the app; they sign paper off-app. The route accepts the photo + claimed signed-at + chain-of-custody note from the worker co-chair's session and returns ONLY the inserted `meeting_signatures` row (signer_role, attestation_hash, recorded_at) — NEVER the meeting's notes. The route's response Zod schema explicitly excludes meeting_sections. The published-export PDF (which the external signer reads off-app) goes through the §3 export step-up + audit-log + output document hash flow; the in_camera-redacted version is what the worker co-chair shares with the external signer. CLAUDE.md non-negotiable #6 (no employer infrastructure dependencies) — the external signer has NO app access. | The worker co-chair is the gatekeeper; a co-chair who shares the internal export with the external signer has shared the in-camera body. Documented as a usage-policy bound. |
| T-ML19 | Workplace name / signer name from workplace config exposed in client bundle (non-negotiable #1 violation) — the `WORKPLACE_DISPLAY_NAME`, `WORKPLACE_CO_CHAIR_DISPLAY_NAME`, `WORKPLACE_MGMT_CO_CHAIR_DISPLAY_NAME`, `WORKPLACE_WAREHOUSE_MGR_DISPLAY_NAME`, `WORKPLACE_PLANT_MGR_DISPLAY_NAME` env vars are inlined into the Vite client bundle at build time, exposing four real human names + workplace identity in any source-map or bundle-inspection | `config/workplace.ts`; Vite client bundle; `apps/web/dist/*.js` | Per non-negotiable #1, workplace + signer identities live in `config/workplace.ts` loaded from env at runtime — for the SERVER. The client bundle does NOT inline the env vars; the client fetches `/api/workplace/config` after authn and the route returns the display names ONLY to authenticated reps. The route emits the names in the JSON response; the names live in HTML the rep's browser renders + in the React component tree but NEVER in the static bundle. Build-time replacement of `import.meta.env.*` for these specific keys is forbidden by the build config; the CI lint (per 1.12 T-HD39) asserts no `VITE_WORKPLACE_*` env var is referenced in client code. | A future PR that adds a `VITE_WORKPLACE_CO_CHAIR_DISPLAY_NAME` env var would trip the lint; documented. The runtime-fetch posture is the structural pattern. |
| T-ML20 | Rights-protective copy regression — workflow copy discourages co-chair from acting on items before all signatures land, e.g., "Wait for all 4 signatures before submitting recommendations to MLITSD" — chilling exercise of OHSA s.9(20), s.43, s.50 (non-negotiable #7 violation) | Meeting view UI; finalization gate UI; recommendation submission UI; `apps/web/src/views/meeting-*-view.tsx` copy strings | The rights-protective copy review checklist (per the closing controls) covers every workflow string in M2.1. Specific patterns to AVOID and REPLACE: "Finalize the meeting before submitting your recommendation" → REPLACE with "Recommendations under s.9(20) can be submitted independently of meeting finalization." "Wait for management co-chair signature" → REPLACE with "Your recommendation under s.9(20) is independent of the management co-chair's signature." The S5 reviewer pass walks every copy string against the checklist. The pre-launch checklist for M2.1 cites non-negotiable #7. CLAUDE.md "Copy must never discourage exercise of OHSA s.43 (refusal), s.50 (reprisal), or CLC s.128/s.147." | Copy review is judgment-bound; the S5 reviewer + the explicit checklist are the structural backstop. A miss surfaces in the rep's daily use and is fast-followed. Documented. |
| T-ML21 | Finalization gate misused as a censoring affordance — the management co-chair refuses to sign, holding the meeting in `signed_partial` indefinitely to delay action items being "officially" published; the worker co-chair feels constrained from acting on items until finalization | `meetings.status = 'signed_partial'`; action item availability post-adjournment | Action items are FIRST-CLASS per non-negotiable #12 and have their own lifecycle (1.6); they are NOT gated by meeting finalization. The action item view shows items regardless of the source meeting's signature state; the section moves (1.6's signature interaction) operate on items independently of meeting finalization. The UI's meeting-detail view shows the meeting's signature state honestly ("3 of 4 signatures captured; awaiting Mgmt Co-Chair") with copy that explicitly says "Action items raised at this meeting are tracked in the action items view independent of signature state." The recommendation flow (1.9) is similarly independent — a draft recommendation can be submitted to MLITSD before, during, or after meeting finalization. The chain anchor `meeting.signed_partial` records the partial state honestly; an arbitrator sees the management co-chair's refusal as the management co-chair's choice, not a worker-side blocker. CLAUDE.md non-negotiables #7 + #12. | Same bound as T-ML20 — copy discipline is the structural defense. Documented. |
| T-ML22 | Audit chain anchor missing on `meeting.finalized` — finalization is a state transition that doesn't emit a chain row, breaking the "every state transition is audit-anchored" invariant | `POST /api/meetings/:id/finalize`; audit chain `meeting.finalized` kind | The finalization route opens a transaction that (a) verifies 4-of-4 signatures (T-ML4), (b) writes `meetings.status = 'finalized'` + `finalized_at = now()`, (c) emits `meeting.finalized` chain row with `{meetingId, signerActorIds: [4], finalContentHash}`, (d) emits the output document hash for the finalized-export PDF per non-negotiable #16. All four steps are in one `db.transaction`; a failure on any rolls back all. The chain row's `idx` is monotonic. The `audit-log-verify.ts --full` flag's chain-kind inventory includes `meeting.finalized` with its payload schema. A missing chain row would trip the verify pass (1.12 T-HD28 forward-defense). | Same bound as 1.5 T-H9 (transaction discipline); documented. |
| T-ML23 | Signature evidence hash collision attack — an attacker crafts two different paper attestations that hash to the same SHA-256 value, allowing one paper to be replaced with another without changing the hash bound to `meeting_signatures.attestation_hash` | `meeting_signatures.attestation_hash`; Tigris evidence storage | SHA-256 collision resistance is the cryptographic assumption — no practical second-preimage attack is known; the residual aligns with 1.7 evidence T-E5. The attestation evidence row in Tigris carries its own `Content-MD5` enforcement (per Tigris presign flow) + the workplace's signing-key signature over the hash (per 1.9 workplace_signing_key seed); a successful collision attack would require breaking SHA-256 AND forging the workplace signing-key signature. The chain anchor row's payload includes the hash; a future hash-algorithm upgrade lands in the standard crypto-rewrap pattern (1.3 §3a runbook). | SHA-256 break is the documented bound; same as 1.7 + 1.9 + 1.11 evidence flows. Acceptable. |
| T-ML24 | Audit row redaction (a previously-emitted row gets soft-deleted because it contains PII) — a meeting attendance chain row inadvertently captured a real name in its payload; an operator tries to "redact" the row to comply with PIPEDA privacy obligations, breaking the chain | `audit_log` chain rows; PIPEDA personal-information-access response | The chain row payload contract for M2.1 follows the priv-F2 invariant from 1.3: typed payloads emit ONLY non-sensitive metadata. `meeting.attendance_recorded` carries `{attendeeId, state}` — no name; the `attendeeId` is a UUID, not a name. `meeting.signature_attested_*` carries `{signerRole, attestationHash}` — no signer name (the role is the structural fact). `meeting.adjourned` carries metrics, no narrative. The redaction need does not arise because the rows carry no PII. If a future bug emitted PII into a payload, the response is the 1.12 T-HD29 documented forensic procedure: the chain is append-only; redaction is structurally forbidden; the response is to fix the emitter + document the row in the incident-response log + (if the row's PII must be revoked) rotate the workplace KEK so the ciphertext-referenced fields become opaque. The audit-row-redaction table (per the 1.12 backlog) is the forward-seam for legitimate redaction needs. | Forward-seam — the redaction table is post-Release-1 backlog; the priv-F2 invariant is the structural defense. Documented. |
| T-ML25 | Reprisal narrative inadvertently captured in section notes (incidental capture of #4 privacy) — a rep records "John Smith reported reprisal after raising the safety concern" in a meeting section note; the narrative lands in encrypted `notes_ct` but is still accessible to every authenticated rep, breaking the principle that reprisal narratives have heightened protection | `meeting_sections.notes_ct`; rep input discipline; M2.2 forward-seam | Single-tenant scope per CLAUDE.md: every authenticated rep sees the same data; multi-tier visibility (reprisal-narrative-only-co-chair) is OUT of scope for M2.1. The architect's brief should consider an `in_camera` section-type for reprisal/accommodation deliberation; until then, the rights-protective copy in the meeting view's note-entry UI includes a helper text: "For reprisal, accommodation, or critical injury content, consider creating a separate confidential thread in Release 2.2 rather than capturing in meeting notes." The chain row carries no narrative (T-ML24); the encrypted notes are the bound. The 2.2 Reprisal Tracker (per ROADMAP.md) is the canonical home for reprisal narratives; the M2.1 copy directs reps there. CLAUDE.md non-negotiable #4 + #7. | Forward-seam to M2.2; documented. The helper text is the structural cue. |
| T-ML26 | Finalization UI suggests waiting on all 4 signatures before publishing action items (slows OHSA s.9(20) recommendation timelines) — a future copy edit lands "Publish action items: requires 4 signatures" in the action item view, gating action item visibility on meeting finalization | Action item view UI; meeting view UI; copy strings | This threat is the inverse of T-ML20 — same mitigation. Action items are FIRST-CLASS (non-negotiable #12) and their visibility/availability is independent of meeting finalization. The S5 reviewer pass walks every copy string in the action item view AND the meeting view for this regression. The rights-protective copy review checklist explicitly includes "no copy that gates action item availability on meeting signature state" as a line item. CLAUDE.md non-negotiable #7 + #12. | Same bound as T-ML20; documented. |
| T-ML27 | Mgmt co-chair's refusal to sign weaponized to block formal recommendation — the management co-chair refuses to sign the meeting, the worker co-chair believes the recommendation under s.9(20) is blocked from submission to MLITSD until the meeting is finalized, and the recommendation languishes | Recommendation submission flow (1.9); meeting finalization gate; rep copy | Recommendations under OHSA s.9(20) / CLC s.135 are independent of meeting finalization per Canadian JHSC law (the recommendation is a JHSC action that the worker side can advance; the management co-chair's signature on the meeting minutes does not gate the recommendation's regulatory clock). The 1.9 recommendation flow operates on its own state machine (`drafted → submitted → response_captured → resolved`); a recommendation can be `submitted` at any time after `drafted`, regardless of the source meeting's signature state. The UI in the meeting view's recommendation section includes a "submit this recommendation now" affordance even when the meeting is in `adjourned` or `signed_partial`. The legal-corpus citation (per non-negotiable #5) renders the s.9(20) clock language verbatim; no app text suggests waiting on the mgmt co-chair's signature. CLAUDE.md non-negotiables #5 + #7. | Same bound as T-ML20/T-ML21/T-ML26; documented in the rights-protective copy checklist. |
| T-ML28 | Worker co-chair coerced into adding a signer who isn't legally required — a manager pressures the worker co-chair to add a 5th signature slot for "the General Counsel" or "the HR Director" who isn't a JHSC committee member; the app's signature workflow accommodates the addition, normalizing the over-collection | `meeting_signatures` table; signature role enum; UI for adding signers | The `meeting_signatures.signer_role` column is a FIXED ENUM in `packages/shared-types/src/meeting-signer-role.ts` with EXACTLY four values: `worker_co_chair` / `management_co_chair` / `warehouse_manager` / `plant_manager` — sourced from the workplace's JHSC charter (env-driven per non-negotiable #1; the specific Warehouse Mgr / Plant Mgr roles reflect this workplace's structure and are configurable per workplace via env). A 5th signer slot is structurally impossible; the API rejects any insert with a `signer_role` not in the enum. The UI has no "add signer" affordance — the four slots are pre-populated at meeting creation. A workplace whose charter requires a different role set (e.g., a federal workplace with a single VP signer) configures via env at deploy time; the M2.1 deploy runbook documents the env var inventory. Coercion to add an extra signer is structurally rejected, and the worker co-chair has the chain row as the bind ("the app does not permit a 5th signer per the JHSC charter"). | A charter that legitimately changes (e.g., a workplace acquires a second plant manager) lands in a follow-up deploy with the env var change; documented. The structural rejection is the immediate defense. |
| T-ML29 | Imported Excel minutes' attendance overrides current-meeting attendance — a 1.11 Excel import contains a meeting record with attendance; if M2.1 reuses the same `meeting_attendance` table, the import could overwrite live-meeting attendance for the current period | 1.11 Excel import reconciliation; `meeting_attendance` table; meeting-level conflict resolution | The 1.11 Excel import schema (per `docs/excel-import-format.md`) imports action items + recommendations + move history; it does NOT import meeting attendance (the Excel file's "Attendance" sheet is informational only in the imported preview). The architect's brief should confirm M2.1 does NOT extend the Excel importer to consume the attendance sheet; if it does in a future milestone, the reconciliation pattern (1.11 T-X20/T-X21 content-hash-keyed dedupe) applies with meeting-id + attendee-id as the dedupe key. For M2.1, the `meeting_attendance` table only accepts inserts via the live-meeting capture route; the Excel import path does not write to it. | Forward-seam — Excel attendance import is out of M2.1 scope; documented. The architect should flag if the M2.1 importer extension is planned. |
| T-ML30 | Excel-imported recommendation gets duplicated when also drafted in the live meeting — the worker co-chair imports a historical Excel file containing a recommendation, then drafts the same recommendation in a live M2.1 meeting; the live-meeting recommendation links to a new action item while the Excel-imported one already created one, producing two duplicate items | 1.11 Excel import; 1.9 recommendation flow; M2.1 meeting recommendation section | The 1.11 reconciliation engine uses content-hash keyed by (Description + Start Date) per the Excel import rules; a duplicate hash matches and merges (1.11 T-X20/T-X21/T-X22/T-X23). For the live-meeting-drafted recommendation, the M2.1 meeting recommendation section creates the recommendation via the 1.9 flow; if the description + date matches an Excel-imported recommendation, the M2.1 UI surfaces the existing recommendation and offers "link to existing" rather than "create new" (the same UI affordance pattern as the hazard → action item conversion in 1.6). The audit chain rows for the two creation paths are independent; the link is captured as a `recommendation.linked_to_excel_import` (forward-seam — confirm in M2.1 schema) or via the source_type/source_id polymorphic FK pattern from 1.6. | The link affordance is a UI policy; a rep who creates a new recommendation without checking the dupe is the bound. The duplicate detection in 1.11 reconciliation is the structural backstop. Documented. |
| T-ML31 | Live meeting view offline sync queue grows unboundedly during a long meeting — the rep is on the floor (poor connectivity), the meeting runs 90 minutes, the sync queue accumulates 200+ section-note edits / 50+ attendance state toggles / 30+ action item moves; the queue can't drain when the rep walks into a connected zone | 1.10 sync queue; Dexie storage quota; `POST /api/sync/queue` batch path | The 1.10 sync queue's batch path supports bulk drain; the M2.1 meeting view edits debounce at 2s per section note (a typing burst writes one queue row, not 50). Attendance state is bounded by the roster size × 3 states (a 10-person committee × 3 states max = 30 entries; in practice each attendee has one entry that's updated in place — the queue row coalesces). Action item moves are bounded by the number of items discussed × 1 move per item. Queue growth at meeting scale (90 min × debounced inputs) is well under the 1.10 Dexie quota assertions. The post-deploy smoke includes a "long meeting offline simulation" Playwright spec that asserts queue drain under load. CLAUDE.md #9 + 1.10 + #2. | Queue-growth bound is the 1.10 quota; documented. |
| T-ML32 | Adjournment-time race — two reps simultaneously click "Adjourn meeting" from different devices, producing two adjournment events with two different content hashes for the same meeting | `POST /api/meetings/:id/adjourn`; transition graph; chain anchor ordering | The adjournment route opens a Drizzle transaction with `SELECT ... FROM meetings WHERE id = $1 FOR UPDATE`, checks the transition (`draft → adjourned` is the only legal pair), writes the new status + adjourned_at + content hash, emits the chain anchor — all in one transaction. The second concurrent click serializes; if the first commits, the second sees `status = 'adjourned'` and gets 409 with "meeting already adjourned at T". The chain has exactly one `meeting.adjourned` row per meeting. Single-co-chair scope means same-rep-multi-device is the realistic scenario; the 409 surfaces cleanly. | Same bound as 1.5 T-H8 (status transition race); documented. |
| T-ML33 | Agenda template versioning silently drifts — the seed agenda template (10 standing items, time allocations) is updated in a future release; meetings created under the OLD template render with the NEW template's items, breaking the historical record (parallel to non-negotiable #13's inspection template immutability) | `agenda_template` table; `meetings.agenda_template_version`; template seed migration | Per non-negotiable #13's pattern extended to meetings: an `agenda_template_version` column on `meetings` pins the template version at meeting creation time; future template updates create a new version row in `agenda_template` (versioned, append-only) and never modify the version pinned to historical meetings. The meeting view loads the agenda items from the version pinned to the meeting, not the current version. The template seed migration emits a chain row `audit.agenda_template.seeded` (parallel to 1.8's `audit.inspection_template.seeded`). | Same bound as 1.8 template immutability; documented. The architect's brief should confirm M2.1 schema includes `agenda_template_version` (FK to `agenda_template.version`). |
| T-ML34 | Attendance `present` state forged by a non-co-chair rep on behalf of another attendee — a rep marks an attendee's state via the live-meeting capture UI, but the captured state is not bound to who actually captured it; an arbitrator can't tell whether the rep recording attendance was the attendee themselves or a third party | `meeting_attendance.attendance_state`; `meeting_attendance.captured_by_actor_id`; audit chain | The `meeting_attendance` table includes `captured_by_actor_id` (the actor_id of the rep who recorded the state) AND `captured_at` (the server timestamp); the chain row `meeting.attendance_recorded` carries `{meetingId, attendeeId, state, capturedByActorId, capturedAt}`. The UI's attendance capture pattern is "the worker co-chair (or their delegate) captures the roster at meeting open" — by convention, the captures are co-chair-led. A non-co-chair rep CAN capture (subject to the same rate-limit and audit row); the chain records the truth. The audit trail discloses both who-was-present and who-recorded-it. | Roster forgery (a third party records a wrong state) is bounded by the chain's attribution; documented. |
| T-ML35 | Meeting-deletion-via-finalization-rejection — a worker co-chair refuses to sign their own meeting to hold it in `signed_partial` indefinitely, effectively "deleting" the meeting from the operational record (it never reaches `finalized`); the meeting's chain rows still exist but the UI hides the unfinalized meeting from the standard list view | `meetings.status = 'signed_partial'`; UI list filtering; chain row visibility | The meetings list view defaults to "show all meetings" with a status filter; an unfinalized meeting is visible. The chain row `meeting.created` is permanent and the meeting's existence is auditable regardless of the UI filter. The worker co-chair refusing to sign is a legitimate workflow state — the meeting was held, the worker co-chair has a documented reason not to finalize. The UI surfaces the partial state honestly. A pattern of repeated unfinalized meetings surfaces in the audit-log-verify run + the rep's own dashboards. | Worker-co-chair-refusal-to-sign-own-meeting is a legitimate state, not a vulnerability; documented. |
| T-ML36 | Inspection review section drift — the `meeting_inspection_review` table links reviewed inspections to meetings; if an inspection is updated after the meeting's review section is finalized, the review record points to a different inspection state than what was actually discussed | `meeting_inspection_review` table; 1.8 inspections; content hash bind | The `meeting_inspection_review` row binds the inspection at review time with `inspection_id` + `inspection_content_hash_at_review` (a hash over the inspection's findings at the moment of review); the chain anchor `meeting.inspection_reviewed` carries the hash. Per non-negotiable #13, inspections are immutable post-conduct; the content hash should not change. If a follow-up edit somehow modified an inspection (forward-seam — 1.8's immutability is the structural defense), the review row's hash diverges from the live inspection's hash and the audit-log-verify flags the divergence. | Same bound as non-negotiable #13 + 1.8 inspection immutability; documented. |
| T-ML37 | Meeting view loads slowly on first visit (cold cache) on mobile — a 90-minute meeting's section notes + attendance + action item snapshot fetches sequentially, blocking the rep's ability to capture live notes during the meeting | `GET /api/meetings/:id` projection; client cache priming; offline-first pattern | The 1.10 offline-first pattern primes the meeting view from Dexie on cold load; the live API fetch hydrates in the background. The projection bundles meeting + sections + attendance + signature state + action item snapshot in one round-trip (server-side join + a single decryption pass over `notes_ct` and `display_name_ct`). The meeting view's "start meeting" affordance pre-warms the cache the night before. CLAUDE.md mobile-primary pattern (skeleton screens, optimistic UI). | Cold-load latency on a fresh device is the documented bound; the pre-warm + skeleton screens are the structural backstop. |
| T-ML38 | External signer's claimed signed-at date is in the future or impossibly past — the worker co-chair fat-fingers the date the external signer wrote on paper ("2027-06-03" instead of "2026-06-03"); the signature row carries the wrong timestamp evidence | `meeting_signatures.signed_at_claimed`; route input validation | The `signed_at_claimed` is validated by Zod to be (a) not in the future (must be `≤ now()`), (b) not earlier than the meeting's `adjourned_at` (an external signer can't sign before the meeting concluded), (c) not earlier than 30 days before `now()` (a reasonable upper-bound on the off-app-signing-to-upload latency; configurable per workplace). A fat-finger outside these bounds gets a 422 with the rejected value. The chain row carries both `signed_at_claimed` AND `signed_at_recorded` (the server's `now()`); an arbitrator sees both and weighs accordingly. | Genuine fat-finger within bounds is bounded by the UI's date picker + the worker co-chair's review; documented. |
| T-ML39 | Encrypted notes envelope's per-row DEK leaks via repeated re-encryption — a section note is edited many times during a 90-minute meeting; each edit re-seals the field with a fresh DEK; the workplace KEK is used N times in 90 minutes, potentially exposing the KEK to side-channel observation in the API process | `meeting_sections.notes_ct`; envelope encryption; KEK usage frequency | The libsodium-wrappers XChaCha20-Poly1305 envelope encryption per CLAUDE.md is side-channel-resistant at the algorithm level; the KEK lives in Fly Secrets memory and is loaded once per process. Repeated `sealField` calls do not re-load the KEK; they invoke the AEAD operation. The DEK is per-row and per-write (fresh nonce each time); the ciphertext does not reveal prior versions. The 1.10 sync queue's debounce (T-ML31 mitigation) bounds re-encryption frequency to ~one per 2s of typing, not per keystroke. KEK rotation cadence (per 1.12 backlog) is the further-defense. | Side-channel-on-KEK is the same bound as every encrypted-field surface (1.5–1.11); documented. |
| T-ML40 | Action item snapshot at adjournment uses a stale section-state — an action item moved a millisecond before adjournment isn't reflected in the snapshot because the snapshot read raced with the move write | `POST /api/meetings/:id/adjourn`; `action_items` table; snapshot generation transaction | The adjournment transaction opens a serializable isolation read of `action_items` (SELECT ... FOR SHARE on the section + flag_state columns) before computing the snapshot hash; concurrent action item moves block until the snapshot read completes. The 1.6 action item move route's `pg_advisory_xact_lock` (T-AI4 pattern) serializes against the adjournment transaction. The snapshot reflects a consistent view. | Lock contention at adjournment is bounded by the transaction duration (sub-second); documented. |
| T-ML41 | Meeting creation race with workplace config rotation — a workplace's signer-role config changes (e.g., a new Warehouse Mgr is appointed) mid-meeting-creation, and the meeting is created with the OLD signer-role binding while the new config is what the workplace charter requires | `WORKPLACE_*` env vars; `meetings.signer_roles_snapshot`; meeting creation transaction | Workplace config changes land via a fresh deploy (per 1.12 T-HD39 + the deploy runbook); the API restarts with the new env vars. A meeting created during the deploy window would use whichever env was loaded at the time. To bind the signer-role config to the meeting evidentially, the `meetings` row includes a `signer_roles_snapshot_json` column captured at creation time (the four role labels at meeting-creation moment); the chain row carries the snapshot. A future meeting with a different snapshot would reflect the new config; both are valid records of their respective time. | Deploy-window race is rare (single-tenant scope, deploys are intentional); documented. |
| T-ML42 | Recommendation drafted in meeting carries wrong meeting_id binding on the chain — the meeting's recommendation section drafts a recommendation via the 1.9 flow, but the resulting `recommendation.drafted` chain row's payload doesn't include the source `meetingId`, breaking the meeting → recommendation linkage | 1.9 recommendation flow; `meeting.recommendation_drafted` chain anchor | The architect's brief should confirm M2.1 adds a `meeting.recommendation_drafted` chain anchor that wraps the 1.9 `recommendation.drafted` emission, carrying `{meetingId, recommendationId, sectionType}`. The `recommendation_id` FK points to the live recommendation row; the chain row's payload-shape map (1.12 T-HD28) includes `meetingId`. The verify pass cross-checks the meeting → recommendation linkage. | Forward-seam — confirm in M2.1 ADR-0012; documented. |
| T-ML43 | Step-up modal opens during a live meeting and interrupts attendance capture / note typing — a step-up-required action (recommendation submission, action item promotion, finalization) opens the modal mid-meeting and the rep loses focus on the live capture flow | Step-up modal; meeting view; UX disruption | The step-up modal pattern from 1.2 (`stepUpEmitter` + 401-StepUp handshake) preserves the underlying view state; the rep returns to the meeting view with their in-flight typing intact (the React Hook Form state is not lost). The meeting view's "session log" panel records the step-up event so the rep can re-walk what they were doing. Step-up frequency is bounded by the JWT's `step_up_until` claim (passkey-fresh for ~10 min after a successful step-up). CLAUDE.md mobile-primary pattern. | UX-disruption is bounded by the freshness window; documented. |
| T-ML44 | A meeting's `created_at` timestamp is set client-side and could be back-dated by a malicious rep to falsify when the meeting was convened | `meetings.created_at`; client-side timestamp; chain anchor | The `meetings.created_at` is set SERVER-SIDE via `now()` at INSERT time; the client-side timestamp is rejected by Zod (the route's input schema does not accept `created_at`). The chain anchor `meeting.created` carries the server's `now()` as `ts_ms`. A back-dating attempt fails at the schema layer. The meeting's `scheduled_start` is a separate column (the planned date, captured at meeting creation) that the rep can set freely; the chain row carries both fields. | None material; documented. |

#### Cross-cutting controls

- **Step-up freshness on all signature endpoints.** The worker co-chair signature route (`POST /api/meetings/:id/signatures/worker-co-chair`) requires `factorRequired = 'passkey'` (TOTP rejected) + `maxAgeSeconds = 60` + a fresh WebAuthn assertion whose `clientDataJSON` challenge includes the `meetingId`. The external-signer attestation upload route (`POST /api/meetings/:id/signatures/external`) requires step-up `maxAgeSeconds = 60` on the worker co-chair's session (the uploader). The finalization route (`POST /api/meetings/:id/finalize`) requires step-up `maxAgeSeconds = 60`. The adjournment route requires step-up `maxAgeSeconds = 60`. The chain row for each signature event carries the step-up factor used + the assertion hash (for passkey) or the TOTP-bound timestamp.
- **Envelope encryption on names + notes + evidence.** `meeting_attendance.display_name_ct`, `meeting_sections.notes_ct`, `meeting_signatures.chain_of_custody_note_ct`, and any free-text rep input that may contain PII are envelope-encrypted at the application layer with per-row DEKs under the workplace KEK. The Drizzle schema enforces the `_ct` suffix convention (1.5 priv-F1 pattern carried forward); integration tests assert `pg_dump` of test rows contains no plaintext PII. The KEK lives in Fly Secrets, never logged, never returned by API.
- **Audit chain on every state transition.** Every M2.1 state transition emits a chain row in the same transaction as the state write. The chain kinds added by M2.1: `meeting.created`, `meeting.attendance_recorded`, `meeting.section_note_updated`, `meeting.inspection_reviewed`, `meeting.adjourned`, `meeting.signature_attested_worker_co_chair`, `meeting.signature_attested_external`, `meeting.finalized`, `meeting.deleted` (draft-only per T-ML10), `meeting.recommendation_drafted` (wraps the 1.9 emission per T-ML42), `audit.agenda_template.seeded` (template seed per T-ML33). Each kind has a documented payload shape in `packages/shared-types/src/audit-event-kind.ts`; the verifier's schema map (1.12 T-HD28) covers each.
- **Rights-protective copy review checklist.** Every copy string in the meeting view, finalization gate, recommendation section, and action item view is reviewed against non-negotiable #7. The checklist (`docs/m2.1-rights-protective-copy.md` — forward-seam doc; the architect should land it) covers: (a) no copy that gates action item availability on meeting signature state (T-ML20, T-ML26); (b) no copy that suggests recommendations require meeting finalization (T-ML20, T-ML27); (c) no copy that frames the management co-chair's signature as a worker-side dependency (T-ML21, T-ML27); (d) no copy that records a reason for "regrets" attendance (T-ML2); (e) reprisal/accommodation/critical-injury content directed to dedicated tracker modules (T-ML25). The S5 reviewer pass walks every string against the checklist.

#### Known gaps

1. **Paper-attestation chain-of-custody is hash + camera-timestamp + chain-of-custody note — not cryptographically perfect.** The external-signer paper-sign + photo-upload flow can't structurally prevent paper alteration between off-app signing and the camera capture (T-ML5). The mitigations layer documentary defense (the worker co-chair's witness narrative, the per-photo SHA-256 hash bound at upload, the claimed-vs-recorded timing pair, the workplace's signing-key signature over the hash). An arbitrator's weighing of this evidence is the structural backstop, not a cryptographic guarantee. PAdES-embedded-signatures (per 1.12 ADR-0011 backlog) is the eventual close-out for in-app signing; off-app signing always carries this residual. Documented honestly.
2. **Co-chair-only / in-camera section visibility tiers don't structurally exist in M2.1.** Per single-tenant scope, every authenticated rep reads every meeting section. The `in_camera` flag (T-ML9) is an export-redaction affordance, not a read-time access control. The forward-seam is the multi-tier role-separation pattern flagged in 1.5 T-H10 + 1.6 T-AI9 + reprisal-narrative T-ML25 + reprisal-deliberation T-ML11. The architect should consider whether a `visibility` column on `meeting_sections` is in-scope for M2.1 to seed the forward-seam without exercising it.
3. **Dexie at-rest encryption is not in M2.1.** Per 1.12 ADR-0011 backlog, Dexie at-rest encryption is post-Release-1. The M2.1 live meeting view writes encrypted notes (`notes_ct` ciphertext is what the sync queue carries) AND plaintext-encryption-key-material (the worker co-chair's DEK derivation) into Dexie. A stolen unlocked laptop with an unsynced queue is the residual (T-ML17). OS-level full-disk encryption is the operator-controlled defense.
4. **Quorum citation is forward-seamed to M1.4 corpus.** The quorum helper (T-ML14) reads the OHSA s.9(18) + CLC s.135.1 quorum rules; the citation in the UI must come from the legal corpus per non-negotiable #5. If M1.4 hasn't shipped the relevant corpus entry by M2.1's start, the citation is a forward-seam — the helper itself is pure-function (correctness-bounded) and the UI's citation render-spot can be a placeholder that wires up when the corpus entry lands.
5. **Agenda template seed depends on jurisdiction.** The 10 standing agenda items are Ontario-OHSA-aligned by default; a federal-CLC workplace has a slightly different standing-item list. The seed migration emits BOTH templates and pins per workplace via `WORKPLACE_JURISDICTION` env; the rep cannot mix-and-match items across jurisdictions in a single template version (T-ML33 immutability).
6. **The architect should flag back from the M2.1 ADR**: (a) confirm the `agenda_template_version` column shape (T-ML33); (b) confirm whether `meeting_sections.visibility` is seeded for the forward-seam (gap #2 + T-ML11); (c) confirm whether `meeting.recommendation_drafted` chain anchor is emitted (T-ML42); (d) confirm whether `meeting_signatures` includes `chain_of_custody_note_ct` and the workplace-signing-key signature over the attestation hash (T-ML5, T-ML23); (e) confirm whether the Excel importer's M2.1 extension consumes the attendance sheet (T-ML29).

**M2.1 adds 11 new audit event kinds: `meeting.created`, `meeting.attendance_recorded`, `meeting.section_note_updated`, `meeting.inspection_reviewed`, `meeting.adjourned`, `meeting.signature_attested_worker_co_chair`, `meeting.signature_attested_external`, `meeting.finalized`, `meeting.deleted`, `meeting.recommendation_drafted`, `audit.agenda_template.seeded`.** The deploy runbook's `audit-log-verify --full` continues to verify all kinds end-to-end. Each kind has a documented payload shape in `packages/shared-types/src/audit-event-kind.ts`; the verifier's schema map (1.12 T-HD28) is extended with the M2.1 kinds in the same S2 slice that lands the migration. The `payloadShapeMismatches` array surfaces any drift between the chain row's actual payload and the documented shape; the fixture-generator script (1.12 T-HD27) re-generates the synthetic full-dataset to include the M2.1 kinds before close-out.

### 2.14 In-Meeting Action Item Management (M2.2)

Milestone 2.2 is the **operational consummation** of the Minutes module: M2.1 stood up the meeting lifecycle (create → in_progress → adjourn → pending_finalization → finalized), and M2.2 is what the worker co-chair actually DOES inside that lifecycle. Five new surfaces extend the M2.1 substrate: (a) **add-action-item-during-meeting** (already wired in M2.1 via `POST /api/action-items` with `firstRaisedMeetingId`+`meetingId`, but M2.2 surfaces it inside the in-meeting section nav and introduces an in-meeting create-form variant), (b) **in-meeting section moves** (the 1.6 `POST /api/action-items/:id/moves` route called from inside the meeting view, with the new in-meeting-move-history surface), (c) **in-meeting status updates** (PATCH on action items, with the live `meeting_action_item_state` snapshot writer firing per change — this is the path the M2.1 reviewer F-L8 deferred), (d) **JHSC closure counter-sign** (a new step-up-gated route that records a JHSC verification on an action item's `Closed` transition, distinct from the meeting's 4-signer counter-sign), (e) **live-updating key metrics dashboard** (the M2.1 adjournment metrics — itemsRaised / itemsClosed / recommendationsDrafted / inspectionsReviewed / quorum — recomputed on-demand during the live meeting, not only at adjournment). The threat posture is **incremental** vs M2.1 — encryption boundary, audit chain, step-up gate, attestation crypto all reuse the M2.1 substrate. What's NEW: (i) a second step-up-gated counter-sign workflow (the per-action-item closure verification, distinct from the meeting-finalization 4-signature workflow), (ii) live-snapshot accumulation under high write frequency during a 90-minute meeting (T-ML31-class amplification), (iii) the move-history-as-printable surface that re-exposes section-name vocabulary and audit-row indices in a UI that gets exported, (iv) the metrics dashboard that aggregates per-rep activity (T-IM27 surveillance framing risk), and (v) cross-chain composition (meeting + action_item + closure-verification three-way anchor) that demands the same priv-F2 + T-AC9-class payload discipline. Non-negotiables most active here: #2 (chain-of-custody on closure verifications), #4 (closure-reason PI encryption), #7 (rights-protective copy on the counter-sign gate — must not chill the rep's authority to act on items), #12 (action items remain first-class — the counter-sign is a verification step on the action item's own lifecycle, NOT a meeting state transition).

| # | Threat | Affected surfaces | Mitigation | Residual |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| T-IM1 | JHSC counter-sign forgery via session-hijack post-step-up — a session-stealer on a second device with a valid step-up grant submits `POST /api/action-items/:id/closure-verifications` impersonating the worker co-chair; the closure verification row is written under the legitimate actor_id and the chain anchor records the impersonator's claim as the co-chair's | new `POST /api/action-items/:id/closure-verifications` route (M2.2 S2); `action_item_closure_verifications` table (M2.2 S1); `step_up_jti` claim on the row | The closure-verification route requires step-up with `factorRequired = 'passkey'` (TOTP rejected for this endpoint, parity with T-ML6 worker-co-chair signature) AND `maxAgeSeconds = 60`. The route binds a fresh WebAuthn assertion whose `clientDataJSON` challenge includes `actionItemId` + the action item's pre-closure content hash (parity with T-ML6 + M2.1 review F-S4's deepening fold). The closure-verification row carries an Ed25519 attestation over the canonical row JSON (parity with M2.1 TM-fold-4 / `meeting_signatures.attestation_signed_ct`) signed by the workplace signing key; a second-device attacker without the passkey credential cannot produce the assertion. The chain row `action_item.closure_verified` carries `{actionItemId, verifierActorId, webauthnAssertionHash, attestationSigHash, stepUpJti, verifiedAt}`. | Passkey credential theft is the bound (same posture as T-ML3 + T-ML6); covered by 1.2 auth posture. Documented. |
| T-IM2 | Counter-sign accepted without step-up freshness check — the route trusts a `step_up_until` JWT claim issued 8 hours earlier for a different purpose (recommendation submission, evidence reveal); the closure verification is recorded without a fresh prompt and the evidentiary weight collapses | new `POST /api/action-items/:id/closure-verifications` route; `step_up_until` JWT claim; `stepUpGate` middleware | The route calls `stepUpGate(c, action='action_item.closure_verify', maxAgeSeconds=60)` (mirroring the M2.1 signature route's `meeting.sign.<role>` action labels per M2.1 review §F). The `action` label is endpoint-specific so a step-up grant issued for `recommendation.submit` is structurally rejected — the `stepUpGate` middleware verifies the JWT's `action` claim matches the called endpoint's required action AND the freshness window AND (per T-IM1 deepening) the WebAuthn assertion's `clientDataJSON` is bound to the target actionItemId. Integration test asserts a grant for `meeting.sign.worker_co_chair` returns 401-StepUp at this endpoint even if within the 60s window. | Same bound as T-ML6 — the WebAuthn challenge binding to `actionItemId` prevents cross-resource replay. Acceptable. |
| T-IM3 | Action item closed without the counter-sign — a rep PATCHes `status='Closed'` directly via `PATCH /api/action-items/:id` (the existing 1.6 route) without going through the M2.2 closure-verification flow; the item moves to `Closed` with no `action_item.closure_verified` chain row and the JHSC counter-sign discipline is bypassed | `PATCH /api/action-items/:id` route (`apps/api/src/routes/action-items/index.ts:644+`); `action_items.status` column | Two-layered defense: (a) the action item PATCH route's status-transition graph (extended in M2.2 S1, parallel to M2.1's meeting transition graph in `packages/shared-types/src/meeting-transitions.ts`) REJECTS any PATCH that sets `status='Closed'` directly — the only legal `→ Closed` path is via the new `POST /api/action-items/:id/closure-verifications` route, which writes the verification row AND flips the status inside one transaction. Direct PATCH to `Closed` returns 422 `closed_requires_verification` with the endpoint pointer in the error body; (b) a DB CHECK constraint on `action_items` enforces `status='Closed' ⇒ closure_verification_id IS NOT NULL` (the `closure_verification_id` FK column added by M2.2 S1, FK to the `action_item_closure_verifications` table, NOT NULL when status='Closed'); a hand-crafted SQL UPDATE that bypasses the route still trips the DB CHECK. The `audit-log-verify --check-action-items` extension (M2.2 S2) cross-checks every `action_item.status_changed` chain row with `to_status='Closed'` against a `action_item.closure_verified` row referencing the same actionItemId. | A coordinated bypass (route + DB CHECK disabled + verifier disabled) is the same posture as 1.6 T-AI2 direct-SQL bound; documented. |
| T-IM4 | Re-opening a closed item silently invalidates the prior counter-sign — a rep moves an item from `Closed → In Progress` via the existing move/PATCH path; the prior `action_item.closure_verified` row stays in the chain but the item's current status no longer matches the verification, and an arbitrator reading just the current row sees mismatched state | `PATCH /api/action-items/:id` (status transition `Closed → *`); existing `POST /api/action-items/:id/moves` for `archived → *` (already step-up-gated per `action-items/index.ts` header line 11); new closure-verification table | The status-transition graph extension (T-IM3 mitigation) treats `Closed → In Progress` (and any `Closed → *`) as a STEP-UP-GATED re-open transition (parity with the existing 1.6 `archived → *` and `→ archived` step-up posture per the action-items route header). The PATCH route requires `stepUpGate(c, action='action_item.reopen', maxAgeSeconds=60)` for any `Closed → *` transition AND emits a new `action_item.reopened` chain row carrying `{actionItemId, fromVerificationId, reopenReasonHash, reopenedByActorId, reopenedAt}`. The prior `action_item_closure_verifications` row is NOT deleted (per #2 chain-of-custody append-only invariant); it gains a `superseded_at` + `superseded_by_reopen_event_idx` denormalization that points at the reopen chain row. The verifier `--check-action-items` cross-checks `closure_verified` rows whose actionItemId has a later `reopened` row to ensure the supersession denormalization matches the chain order. | Re-open is a legitimate workflow (work resumed after JHSC verification); the chain records the truth. Documented. |
| T-IM5 | Closure-reason PI leak via audit-log payload — the closure-verification flow accepts a free-text "verification narrative" (the rep records why the JHSC accepts the item as closed, possibly naming the employee whose accommodation request was resolved); the narrative lands in the `action_item.closure_verified` chain payload as plaintext and the priv-F2 / T-AC9-class invariant is broken | `POST /api/action-items/:id/closure-verifications` route; `action_item_closure_verifications.narrative_ct`; chain payload shape | Per T-ML24/T-ML25 + T-AC9-class — the narrative is stored ONLY in `action_item_closure_verifications.narrative_ct` (envelope-encrypted, per-row DEK under workplace KEK, parity with `meeting_sections.notes_envelope_ct`). The chain payload `action_item.closure_verified` carries `{actionItemId, verifierActorId, verificationId, narrativeHash, attestationSigHash, verifiedAt}` — narrative is HASH only, not plaintext. The `AuditPayload` discriminated union in `packages/shared-types/src/index.ts` makes any future drift a compile-time error (the kind's payload type does not include `narrative: string`). Integration test asserts `pg_dump` of `audit_log` rows for the new kind contains no plaintext markers. | DB-level attacker gets ciphertext; KEK is the bound. Same posture as M2.1 §E verified-clean. |
| T-IM6 | Closure-verification evidence orphan-ciphertext in Tigris — the rep optionally uploads a photo of the resolved hazard (the freezer door is now closing properly) as evidence the JHSC counter-sign rests on; the Tigris upload succeeds but the route fails between the upload and the row INSERT, leaving the encrypted blob orphaned | new `POST /api/action-items/:id/closure-verifications` route; Tigris bucket; `action_item_closure_verifications.evidence_storage_key` | The closure-verification route reuses the 1.7 evidence flow + the M2.1 §3.9 off-app-signer evidence pattern: the photo is uploaded via the 1.7 presigned PUT to a `pending:<uuid>` key, then the closure-verification route accepts the FINALIZED `evidence_storage_key` (not the pending one — per M2.1 review F-L1 fix). A Zod regex on the route rejects keys starting with `pending:`. If the route fails after the upload, the orphan blob is swept by the same deferred GC job that handles 1.7 + M2.1 off-app signature evidence (same forward-seam — Tigris orphan-ciphertext GC is the documented Release 2.x hardening item per M2.1 ADR-0012 §"Risks" and 1.7 deferral). The bound at single-tenant scale: ~50 closure verifications per quarter × 10% with evidence × 1% failure rate = ~0.2 orphans/year. | Same forward-seam as 1.7 + M2.1; Tigris orphan-ciphertext GC lands in Release 2.x hardening. Bounded. |
| T-IM7 | Status-change replay via idempotency-key reuse for distinct semantic changes — the rep PATCHes status `Not Started → In Progress` with key K1, the request times out at the proxy layer; the client retries with the SAME K1 but in the meantime the rep also queued a different PATCH (`In Progress → Blocked`) with the same key from another offline session; the idempotency cache returns the cached first-response and the second semantic change silently drops | `PATCH /api/action-items/:id` (existing 1.6 route); `Idempotency-Key` header; 1.10 sync queue idempotency cache | The 1.10 idempotency middleware (per ADR-0009 §3.4 + 1.10 T-S4/T-S5) caches the (idempotency_key, actor_id) pair → first-response mapping. The client-side sync queue (M2.2 S3 extension to the Dexie queue) generates a FRESH `Idempotency-Key` per semantic-change row (per ADR-0009 §3.3 — the client UUID v7 is the dedupe primitive and is regenerated per intent). A queued PATCH from a long-offline second device with a duplicate key would hit the cache and the response would reflect the FIRST intent; the second device's local Dexie marks the queue row as "completed" with the cached payload, which on next sync surfaces as a divergence the rep reconciles via the standard 1.10 conflict UI. Integration test asserts two PATCHes with the same idempotency key produce one row write + one chain row + the cached response on the second call (not a silent overwrite). | Two-device same-key collision is the operator's discipline (a rep does not generate identical idempotency keys); the 1.10 client-side UUID v7 makes the collision astronomically improbable. Documented. |
| T-IM8 | Section-move-replay gaming the 21-day s.9(21) clock — a rep moves an action item `new_business → old_business → new_business` to reset the "first raised" timestamp the Action Flag computes against (CLAUDE.md: 🟠 <21 days vs 🟠 >21 days); the move history shows the round-trip but the flag computation reads only the current section state | `POST /api/action-items/:id/moves` (existing 1.6 route); `action_items.start_date` column; Action Flag computation in `@jhsc/shared-types/action-item-flag` | The 21-day s.9(21) clock is anchored to `action_items.start_date` (the date the item was first raised — IMMUTABLE post-create, parity with M2.1 `first_raised_meeting_id` immutability), NOT to the current section's move-in timestamp. Per 1.6 T-AI5 (already documented in §2.6), the move history is append-only via `action_item_moves` rows and the Action Flag pure function reads `start_date` + `current_section` + `status`; a round-trip move does NOT reset the clock because `start_date` is unchanged. The PATCH Zod (`apps/api/src/routes/action-items/index.ts:172-192` `.strict()`) does not include `startDate` so no PATCH can move it; the M2.1 reviewer verified the parallel `firstRaisedMeetingId` immutability (linkage review "verified clean" §). Integration test asserts a `new_business → old_business → new_business` sequence preserves `start_date` and the Action Flag's "days since raised" math reads the original date. | Start-date forgery would require direct SQL UPDATE — same bound as 1.6 T-AI2. Documented. |
| T-IM9 | Section-move audit-payload PI leak via section-name vocabulary — the chain payload for `action_item.moved` (1.6 kind, reused in-meeting per ADR-0012 §3.7) carries `{fromSection, toSection}` as string enum values; if a future M2.2 fold adds a "custom section" with a display-name that the rep types in (parallel to the M2.1 deferred custom-section forward seam), the chain payload would leak the rep's typed name | existing `action_item.moved` chain payload; M2.2 S1 must NOT add a free-text section-display-name column | M2.2 explicitly preserves the closed-section-enum invariant from M2.1 ADR-0012 §"Negative tradeoffs" and S0 user-decision §3 ("12-value section_type enum is CLOSED for all of Release 2"). The five-value `action_item.section` enum (`new_business` / `old_business` / `recommendation` / `completed_this_period` / `archived`) per CLAUDE.md is similarly CLOSED — no M2.2 S1 migration adds a custom-section column. The chain payload's `fromSection` / `toSection` are bounded enum values, never free text; the discriminated union in `shared-types` is the typechecker-level gate. The M2.2 closure-verification flow may emit `action_item.closure_verified` with `{prevSection}` — also bounded by the closed enum. | Custom sections are deferred to Release 3 per M2.1 S0 user-decision; the chain payload stays enum-only. Documented. |
| T-IM10 | Two-rep concurrent section move with same If-Match version produces lost-update — Rep A and Rep B both load the action item at version V; Rep A swipes `new_business → old_business`; Rep B swipes `new_business → completed_this_period`; both submit `If-Match: V`; the route's `version` ratchet bumps V → V+1 on Rep A's commit; Rep B's request fails with 409 BUT a race in the route between the SELECT-version and the UPDATE-version could let both succeed | `POST /api/action-items/:id/moves` (existing 1.6 route); `action_items.version` column; If-Match middleware | The 1.6 move route uses `pg_advisory_xact_lock` keyed on the action item id (per `apps/api/src/routes/action-items/index.ts:1185` `allocateSequenceNumber` pattern + the move handler's lock at ~line 950) — concurrent moves on the same action item serialize. Inside the locked transaction, the route SELECTs `version FOR UPDATE`, compares against the If-Match value, and UPDATEs `version = version + 1` atomically. The second concurrent submission sees the bumped version and returns 409 with `version_conflict` + the current version (parity with M2.1 PATCH routes using `readIfMatchOr428` middleware at `apps/api/src/routes/meetings/index.ts:79`). Integration test asserts two simultaneous moves with the same If-Match value produce exactly one success + one 409 + exactly one `action_item.moved` chain row (NOT two). Single-co-chair scope (per ADR-0001) makes the "two reps simultaneously" scenario realistic only on multi-device same-rep usage; the version conflict surfaces cleanly. | Same bound as 1.5 T-H8 + M2.1 T-ML32 (transition race); documented. |
| T-IM11 | Status-change retry-loop spams the live snapshot table — a network-flaky retry of a PATCH status change re-enters the route N times (the 1.10 retry policy with exponential backoff caps at 5 retries per ADR-0009 §3.5); each entry calls `writeLiveActionItemSnapshot` (per `apps/api/src/routes/meetings/index.ts:2116`) and INSERTs a fresh `meeting_action_item_state` row, accumulating N duplicate snapshot rows for the same logical change | `writeLiveActionItemSnapshot` helper (`apps/api/src/routes/meetings/index.ts:2116-2166`); `meeting_action_item_state` table | The PATCH route is wrapped by `idempotencyKey` middleware (per ADR-0009 §3.4 + the action-items route header line 62); a retry with the same key returns the cached response without re-entering the handler body — so the snapshot writer fires at most once per logical PATCH. If a CLIENT-BUG produces fresh idempotency keys per retry (defeating the middleware), the snapshot writer would fire N times; mitigation: a partial UNIQUE on `(meeting_id, action_item_id, snapshot_status, snapshot_section, snapshot_at::date)` is NOT added (would over-constrain legitimate same-day status flips); instead, the writer dedupes against the most-recent live snapshot — if `(snapshot_status, snapshot_section, assignee_hash)` matches the row at `MAX(snapshot_at)` for this `(meeting_id, action_item_id, snapshot_kind='live')` tuple, the writer no-ops and emits no chain row. M2.2 S1 adds this dedupe check to the helper (S1 architectural fold below). The 1.10 sync queue Dexie cap (per 1.10 T-S6 storage-quota assertions) caps the queue at meeting scale. | Honest client + idempotency middleware = at-most-once; the dedupe check is the structural backstop against client-side bugs. Documented. |
| T-IM12 | `first_raised_meeting_id` retroactively re-pointed via a hand-crafted PATCH — the M2.1 chain anchor `action_item.created` records `firstRaisedMeetingId` in the chain payload, but the column is on `action_items` and a hand-crafted SQL UPDATE could re-point it without a corresponding chain row, breaking the meeting → action item provenance | `action_items.first_raised_meeting_id`; M2.2 S2 must not add a PATCH path that exposes this column | M2.1 linkage reviewer verified "`firstRaisedMeetingId` immutability: PATCH Zod is `.strict()` and does NOT include `firstRaisedMeetingId`; an attempt to PATCH it returns 400 `invalid_body`" (linkage review "verified clean" §). M2.2 S2 does NOT relax this — the M2.2 closure-verification PATCH (T-IM3) and the in-meeting status PATCH path both reuse the existing 1.6 PATCH Zod with the same `.strict()` posture. The `audit-log-verify --check-action-items` extension (M2.2 S2) cross-checks `action_items.first_raised_meeting_id` against the `action_item.created` chain row's payload; a divergence surfaces in the verifier report. Direct SQL UPDATE is the bound (parity with 1.6 T-AI2). | Same posture as 1.6 T-AI2 + M2.1 verified-clean §; documented. |
| T-IM13 | Cross-chain anchor `meeting.action_item_status_changed` hash spoof — M2.2 introduces a cross-chain anchor (parallel to M2.1 TM-fold-3's `meeting.recommendation_drafted`) that wraps each in-meeting `action_item.status_changed` event with `{meetingId, actionItemId, statusChangedEventHash}`; an attacker could attempt to construct two distinct status-change events with the same SHA-256 hash to bind the wrong status-change to a meeting | new `meeting.action_item_status_changed` chain kind (M2.2 S1); `computeChainEntryHash` helper at `apps/api/src/routes/meetings/index.ts:2179` | The cross-chain anchor reuses the SAME `computeChainEntryHash` helper M2.1 uses for `meeting.recommendation_drafted` (per `apps/api/src/routes/meetings/index.ts:2179`); the hash is SHA-256 over the canonical-JSON chain entry. SHA-256 collision resistance is the cryptographic assumption (parity with T-ML23 + 1.7 T-E5). Both the upstream `action_item.status_changed` row and the cross-chain `meeting.action_item_status_changed` row are emitted in the SAME transaction (parity with M2.1 review §C Gate 3 "both emissions are inside the same transaction — if the recommendation INSERT fails the chain rolls back together"). An attacker crafting a colliding event would also need to bypass the per-row hash chain's prev-hash linkage. | SHA-256 break is the documented bound (T-ML23 parity); acceptable. |
| T-IM14 | `meeting.metrics_recomputed` chain payload tampering on read — M2.2's live-metrics dashboard recomputes metrics on every GET; if the recompute is anchored to the chain on each read, the chain grows unboundedly AND the read-anchor's payload could be mass-tampered via a payload-shape regression | new `GET /api/meetings/:id/metrics/live` route (M2.2 S2); audit chain row emission decision | The live-metrics endpoint is **read-only and NOT chain-anchored** (parity with ADR-0012 §3.8 — adjournment metrics ARE chain-anchored because they capture the evidentiary moment; live mid-meeting metrics are recomputed-on-read for the dashboard UX and are NOT evidentiary). The dashboard endpoint returns the metrics dict for the live UI to render; the metrics are recomputed from the live `action_items` + `recommendations` + `meeting_inspection_review` + `meeting_attendance` rows on each call — no chain row per read. The ONLY chain anchor for metrics is the existing M2.1 `meeting.adjourned` event at adjournment time, which freezes the evidentiary snapshot. The dashboard is the operator's situational awareness; the chain is the evidence. M2.2 S1 documents this in the route header (parity with M2.1 route header conventions). | Live metrics are NOT evidence; only the adjourned snapshot is. Documented in the route header + the M2.2 runbook. |
| T-IM15 | Live-metrics endpoint enumerated by a low-priv rep across meetings — `GET /api/meetings/:id/metrics/live` accepts any meeting id; a rep walks `/metrics/live` for every meeting in the workplace's history, harvesting per-meeting productivity data | new `GET /api/meetings/:id/metrics/live` route; meeting id parameter | Single-tenant scope per CLAUDE.md: every authenticated rep sees the same data; there is no multi-rep enumeration concern. The route requires `authMiddleware` (same as every other M2.1 route per `apps/api/src/routes/meetings/index.ts:69-70`). The route returns ONLY non-PI aggregate counts (the same shape as M2.1 `meeting.adjourned` metrics payload — itemsRaised / itemsClosed / recommendationsDrafted / inspectionsReviewed / quorumCompliance). No per-rep breakdown is in the response (T-IM27 mitigation). A rate-limit (M2.2 S2 — parity with the action-items route's rate-limit at `apps/api/src/routes/action-items/index.ts:64-68`) caps polling at 60 requests/minute per actor. | Single-tenant + rate-limit are the bounds; documented. |
| T-IM16 | Quorum-delta inferred attendance leak via metrics endpoint — the live-metrics endpoint returns `quorumCompliance: { metAtCallToOrder, lostIntervals: [...] }`; an attacker correlating multiple polled responses over the meeting's duration could infer late arrivals or early departures of specific attendees by watching the quorum chip change | `GET /api/meetings/:id/metrics/live` quorum payload | The `quorumCompliance` payload returns ONLY `{metAtCallToOrder: boolean, ruleCitation: string}` per M2.1 §3.8 metrics shape (per `apps/api/src/routes/meetings/index.ts:1690-1693`). The M2.1 ADR §3.8 mentions `quorum_lost_intervals` as a payload field for the adjournment metrics — M2.2 S2 explicitly OMITS this field from the live-metrics endpoint (the intervals are evidentiary, computed once at adjournment, not exposed live). The live endpoint returns the current `metAtCallToOrder` boolean only. An attacker correlating responses sees a binary at-this-instant compliance signal, not interval data; the inference from "quorum went from met to not-met between poll N and N+1" reveals "someone left" but not WHO — and at single-tenant scale the rep IS the polling actor, so the inference is moot. | Live-metrics omit interval data; only the adjourned snapshot carries intervals (M2.1 chain-anchored per T-ML12 family). Documented. |
| T-IM17 | Metrics-recompute DoS via polling — a malicious in-browser script polls `/metrics/live` at 100 req/sec from the live meeting view; each call runs four COUNT queries + a quorum compute over `meeting_attendance`; the Postgres connection pool saturates | new `GET /api/meetings/:id/metrics/live` route; Postgres pool | Route-level rate-limit caps at 60 req/min per actor (T-IM15 mitigation). The dashboard UI uses Server-Sent Events or a 10-second polling interval (M2.2 S3 — parity with mobile-primary pattern; the dashboard does not need 100 req/sec). The four COUNT queries are bounded by single-tenant scale (~30-50 action items per meeting + ~10 attendance rows + 5 inspection reviews); each query is O(rows) with the existing `meetings_status_idx` + `action_items_first_raised_meeting_idx` + `meeting_attendance_meeting_idx` indexes per `apps/api/src/db/schema.ts:1307-1380`. The Postgres pool is sized per ADR-0011 deploy runbook for the per-Fly-machine connection cap. | Rate-limit + index discipline + single-tenant scale = bounded. Documented. |
| T-IM18 | Metrics cache leaks across meetings via shared cache key — if M2.2 S2 introduces a Redis/pg-boss cache for the live-metrics endpoint (perf optimization), a cache-key collision between meetings could serve Meeting A's metrics to a query for Meeting B | M2.2 S2 metrics cache (if introduced); cache-key construction | M2.2 S2 does NOT introduce a cache layer for the live-metrics endpoint (T-IM17's rate-limit + index discipline removes the perf need). The metrics are recomputed on every GET. If a future hardening adds a cache, the cache key MUST include the meeting id + the meeting's `version` column (so a state change invalidates the cache); a Redis namespace per workplace_singleton prevents cross-workplace bleed (single-tenant scope means this is theoretical). M2.2 S1 architectural fold: the route header documents "no cache layer; metrics are recomputed on each GET" so a future PR doesn't add one without the per-meeting-version key. | No cache in M2.2; documented forward-seam. |
| T-IM19 | In-meeting move history surfaces actor display names in the printable view — the M2.2 S3 move-history surface (under each section in the meeting nav) renders `action_item_moves` rows with the actor's display name; the print stylesheet exposes the name in the printed PDF, violating non-negotiable #1 by surfacing workplace identity in an exportable document | new in-meeting move-history surface (M2.2 S3); `action_item_moves.moved_by_actor_id`; print stylesheet | Per non-negotiable #1, no name lives in source. Per M2.1 ADR-0012 §"Negative tradeoffs" the signer display names are encrypted at rest AND only decrypted inside the PDF generator under the workplace private key. The M2.2 move-history surface follows the same pattern: the row's `moved_by_actor_id` is a UUID; the UI looks up the actor's display name via the SAME workplace public-key encrypted display-name surface that M2.1 uses for `meeting_signatures.signer_display_name_ct`. The print stylesheet for the move-history surface uses the canonical `data-print="hide"` for screen-only chrome and `data-print="evidentiary"` for the chain-anchor metadata (per the CLAUDE.md print convention + `apps/web/src/index.css`).
