The actor's display name renders as a role label ("Worker Co-Chair recorded this move") rather than a specific name in the print output — the rep can opt to include the display name in the formal minutes PDF (M2.3 deliverable), but the M2.2 in-meeting print preview is role-only. | Role-label-only in print preview; the formal PDF is M2.3's surface where the display-name decryption goes through the step-up + audit + document-hash flow per non-negotiable #16. Documented. |
| T-IM20 | Move-history read bypasses the role gate — a future M2.2 fold exposes `GET /api/action-items/:id/moves` to non-co-chair reps (the in-meeting move-history surface needs the data); a rep who shouldn't see the move actor could read it | existing 1.6 `action_item_moves` table; new `GET /api/action-items/:id/moves` route (if added in M2.2 S2) | Single-tenant scope: every authenticated rep sees the same data (parity with M2.1 T-ML9, T-ML11 — multi-tier visibility is a forward-seam to Release 2.x role-separation). The M2.2 move-history GET route requires `authMiddleware` only; no role check beyond "authenticated rep" per ADR-0001. The chain payload for `action_item.moved` already excludes name fields (per 1.6 T-AI9 + M2.1 §E verified-clean); the move row's `moved_by_actor_id` is a UUID. The role-separation forward-seam (M2.1 T-ML11 + T-ML25) is the structural answer when multi-tier visibility lands. | Same forward-seam as M2.1 §2.13 gap #2; documented. |
| T-IM21 | Move history's chain-anchor explanation in print exposes audit-row indices that could reveal action-item velocity to a hostile arbitrator — the print stylesheet's `data-print="evidentiary"` block (per CLAUDE.md print convention) surfaces the chain row `idx` for each move; an arbitrator counting indices could infer the rep's activity cadence | M2.2 S3 in-meeting move-history print stylesheet; `data-print="evidentiary"` block | The chain row `idx` is a global monotonic counter across ALL audit events (auth, meetings, hazards, action items, recommendations, inspections, evidence, excel imports). A row at idx=15234 reveals nothing about action-item velocity specifically — the idx aggregates every actor's every action across all milestones. The print stylesheet's `data-print="evidentiary"` block surfaces idx + document hash (per the CLAUDE.md canonical pattern + `docs/release-1-wcag-audit.md §"Print stylesheet verification"`); this is the EVIDENTIARY purpose — an arbitrator needs the chain anchor to verify tamper-evidence (non-negotiable #2). A rep who wishes to redact the idx for a particular print audience uses the export step-up flow (M2.3 PDF generator) which produces the formal distribution version; the in-meeting print preview is the rep's working surface. | Idx aggregation across all milestones makes per-actor velocity inference impractical; the evidentiary anchor is non-negotiable #2's structural requirement. Documented. |
| T-IM22 | Offline status-change re-orders relative to the live snapshot accumulation — a rep on the floor (poor connectivity) makes status changes that queue locally; a different in-flight live-snapshot from a connected device interleaves; on drain, the snapshot table receives rows in wall-clock-server-receipt order, NOT in the rep's intent order; the metrics dashboard reflects an inconsistent state mid-drain | 1.10 sync queue (per ADR-0009 §3.5); `meeting_action_item_state` row ordering; `writeLiveActionItemSnapshot` | The 1.10 sync queue per-actor + per-resource ordering is preserved on drain (per ADR-0009 §3.5 + 1.10 T-S7 "queue drain preserves intent order"). The `meeting_action_item_state.snapshot_at` is set SERVER-SIDE at row INSERT time (per `apps/api/src/routes/meetings/index.ts:2137-2149`), so the row's `snapshot_at` reflects server-receipt time, NOT client-intent time. The `meeting.adjourned` finalized-snapshot promotion reads `DISTINCT ON (action_item_id) ORDER BY snapshot_at DESC` (per `apps/api/src/routes/meetings/index.ts:1612-1616`) — the MOST RECENT live snapshot wins per action item. Offline-then-drain ordering is a documented residual: a status change made at T1 (offline) that drains at T2 wins over a change made at T1.5 (connected, immediate); the rep's local Dexie row shows the post-drain truth; the 1.10 chain-anchor latency stance (per ADR-0009 §3.12) is the legal posture — the chain proves server-receipt time, not meeting-time. | Offline reorder is the documented 1.10 residual per ADR-0009 §3.12; the rep is aware via the 1.10 sync-status chip; the adjournment captures the post-drain truth. Acceptable. |
| T-IM23 | Offline counter-sign attempt — the JHSC closure-verification route is step-up-gated AND online-only (parity with M2.1 `POST /api/meetings/:id/finalize`); a rep offline taps "verify closure" on the in-meeting action-item card and the request queues locally, then drains hours later when the meeting's state may have changed | new `POST /api/action-items/:id/closure-verifications` route; 1.10 sync queue offline behavior | The closure-verification route is REQUIRE-ONLINE per the M2.1 §3.10 step-up posture (per `apps/api/src/routes/meetings/index.ts` step-up gate matrix); the client-side UI (M2.2 S3) surfaces a "Network required for closure verification" banner when the rep taps the affordance while offline, parity with the M2.1 finalization-view's offline banner. The step-up JWT cannot be issued offline (the WebAuthn challenge is server-issued per ADR-0001 §3.2); the request CANNOT queue for later drain because the step-up freshness window is 60s and the queue drain latency is typically minutes-to-hours. The Dexie sync queue's `requires_online` flag (M2.2 S3 extension to the queue) marks the closure-verification mutation as non-queueable; the UI rejects the tap with the banner instead of queueing. | Same posture as M2.1 finalization + adjournment require-online; documented. |
| T-IM24 | Dexie live snapshot diverges from server-side adjournment finalization — during a meeting, the Dexie cache holds `live` snapshot rows; on adjournment the server promotes them to `finalized` rows in a transaction; if the rep's Dexie sync runs MID-promotion, the cache could hold a mixed live+partial-finalized view that confuses the live-metrics dashboard | Dexie cache; `meeting_action_item_state` table; adjournment transaction at `apps/api/src/routes/meetings/index.ts:1608-1667` | The adjournment transaction is server-side and atomic (per `apps/api/src/routes/meetings/index.ts:1608-1667` — the promotion loop is inside the same `db.transaction` as the meeting status flip); a sync that runs MID-transaction sees the pre-transaction state (live rows only, no finalized rows yet). On the next sync after commit, the cache receives BOTH the live rows AND the finalized rows + the `meeting.adjourned` chain anchor + the meeting's new `pending_finalization` status. The Dexie reconciliation per ADR-0009 §3.7 (server `version` ratchet on `meetings` row) invalidates the cached meeting envelope, triggering a re-fetch that surfaces the consistent finalized state. The live-metrics dashboard reads from the in-memory React state hydrated from the GET response; on the post-adjournment GET, the dashboard re-renders with the finalized snapshot data (or surfaces "Meeting adjourned — viewing finalized state"). | Transactional atomicity on the server + version-ratchet invalidation on the client = consistent view post-drain. Documented. |
| T-IM25 | Counter-sign UX framed as a gatekeeping requirement chills the rep — the closure-verification copy reads "You cannot close this action item until the JHSC verifies it" rather than "The JHSC counter-sign is your evidentiary attestation of closure; record it when ready"; the framing implies external permission rather than rep authority | M2.2 S3 closure-verification UI copy; rights-protective copy review | Per non-negotiable #7, copy must never discourage exercise of OHSA s.43/s.50 (or the equivalent worker-rep authority to close an action item). The M2.2 rights-protective copy review checklist (parallel to M2.1 §2.13 cross-cutting controls) explicitly bans gatekeeping framings AND requires the closure-verification copy to read as REP AUTHORITY: "Record JHSC counter-sign for this closure" (not "Wait for JHSC approval to close"); "This is your evidentiary attestation under s.9(20)/s.50" (not "The JHSC must approve before closing"). The S5 reviewer pass walks every copy string in the closure-verification view against the checklist. CLAUDE.md non-negotiable #7. | Copy review is judgment-bound; the S5 reviewer + the checklist are the structural backstop (parity with M2.1 T-ML20 / T-ML21 / T-ML26 / T-ML27). Documented. |
| T-IM26 | Closure-reason narrative field framing pressures the rep to justify rather than document — the field label reads "Why is the JHSC accepting this as closed?" implying the rep must justify their decision to a hostile auditor; a worker-side label reads "Record the basis for JHSC counter-sign (evidence reviewed, conditions met)" framing the rep as the records custodian | M2.2 S3 closure-verification narrative field UI; rights-protective copy review | The narrative-field label + helper text follow the rep-as-records-custodian framing per M2.1 ADR-0012 §"Negative tradeoffs" (the rep is the worker-side records custodian; the chain anchors what the rep recorded). The label reads "Basis for closure verification (optional)" and the helper text reads "What evidence did the JHSC review? E.g., 'inspection re-conducted', 'engineering control verified', 'training completion confirmed'." NO label asks "why" — the framing is documentary, not justificatory. The M2.2 rights-protective copy checklist explicitly lists "no 'why' framing in closure-verification copy" as a line item. | Documentary framing per M2.1 + CLAUDE.md non-negotiable #7; the S5 reviewer enforces. Documented. |
| T-IM27 | Metrics dashboard surfaces "items raised by rep X" implying productivity surveillance — the live-metrics dashboard's "items raised" count could be displayed per-rep (the data exists in `action_items.created_by_actor_id`), enabling a co-chair's view of who-raised-what that doubles as a productivity ranking | M2.2 S3 live-metrics dashboard UI; metrics payload shape | The live-metrics payload is AGGREGATE-ONLY (T-IM15 mitigation): `{itemsRaised: number, itemsClosed: number, recommendationsDrafted: number, inspectionsReviewed: number}` — NO per-actor breakdown. The dashboard UI mirrors this shape; there is NO per-rep filter, NO per-rep chart, NO leaderboard. M2.2 S1 architectural fold: the live-metrics payload Zod schema explicitly excludes per-actor fields; a future PR that adds a per-rep count would fail typecheck against the schema. The M2.2 rights-protective copy checklist includes "no per-actor counts in dashboards" as a line item. Single-tenant + single-co-chair scope makes per-rep productivity tracking moot (the rep is the only operator); the structural defense prevents drift if multi-rep scope ever lands. | Single-tenant + aggregate-only payload + schema-level enforcement = surveillance-resistant. Documented. |
| T-IM28 | `closer_actor_id` / `counter_signer_actor_id` is a stable employer-org reference that could leak via the metrics endpoint payload — even though metrics are aggregate counts, the underlying `action_item_closure_verifications` row carries `verifier_actor_id` which is a stable identifier across meetings; an export of the table would tie back to a specific human | new `action_item_closure_verifications` table (M2.2 S1); `verifier_actor_id` column | The `verifier_actor_id` FK references `users.id` — single-tenant scope means there is one worker co-chair; the actor_id is a UUID that does not leak the rep's name (the rep's name is in `user_profiles.display_name_ct` which is envelope-encrypted, parity with the M2.1 attendee-name posture). The chain payload for `action_item.closure_verified` carries `verifierActorId` (UUID) but never the rep's name. Exports of the table (via the M2.3 PDF generator + future Release 2.x analytics) decrypt the display name under the workplace private key inside the export's step-up + audit-log + document-hash flow (non-negotiable #16). A direct SQL dump of `action_item_closure_verifications` reveals UUIDs only; the actor_id → name mapping requires the workplace KEK. | Same bound as M2.1 attendee display name (T-ML1); UUID-only at rest, encrypted name on export, KEK is the bound. Documented. |
| T-IM29 | Closure-verification narrative envelope KEK rotation across meeting boundaries — a closure verification is recorded under KEK version K1; the workplace KEK rotates to K2 before the meeting is finalized; the M2.3 PDF generator queries the narrative and finds the row was sealed under K1 which is no longer the active KEK | `action_item_closure_verifications.narrative_ct`; workplace KEK rotation runbook (1.3 §3a); M2.3 PDF generator | The 1.3 §3a KEK rotation runbook (per `apps/api/scripts/workplace-key-rotate.ts`) rewrites every encrypted row through the old-key-decrypt + new-key-encrypt path BEFORE retiring the old KEK; a closure verification sealed under K1 is re-wrapped to K2 during rotation. The M2.3 PDF generator opens narratives under the current active KEK; post-rotation rows are all under the new KEK. M2.2 S1 architectural fold: the `action_item_closure_verifications` table is added to the rotation runbook's table inventory (parity with `meeting_sections.notes_envelope_ct` + `meeting_attendance.display_name_ct` + `meeting_signatures.signer_display_name_ct` + `meeting_signatures.chain_of_custody_note_ct`). The KEK rotation runbook test fixture (per 1.12 T-HD27) is regenerated to include closure-verification rows. | Rotation runbook covers the table; documented in the runbook + the 1.12 fixture-gen. |
| T-IM30 | Adjournment compute reads the live snapshots; a malicious live-snapshot insert between adjournment compute and chain emit could falsify metrics — a hand-crafted SQL INSERT into `meeting_action_item_state` between the metrics COUNT and the chain `append` emit could add a phantom snapshot that distorts the recorded metrics | `POST /api/meetings/:id/adjourn` route at `apps/api/src/routes/meetings/index.ts:1581-1706`; transactional isolation | The adjournment route runs the entire compute + promote + chain-emit inside ONE `db.transaction` block (per `apps/api/src/routes/meetings/index.ts:1559-1709`); the transaction holds a `FOR UPDATE` lock on the `meetings` row from line 1560 onwards. A concurrent SQL INSERT into `meeting_action_item_state` for the same meeting_id would either block (if the writer respects table-level locking) or commit between the SELECT and the chain emit; the COUNT queries on lines 1581-1593 are inside the same transaction and see a SERIALIZABLE-isolation snapshot per the Postgres default for explicit BEGIN/COMMIT (Drizzle's `db.transaction` defaults to READ COMMITTED — M2.2 S1 architectural fold: upgrade the adjournment transaction's isolation level to SERIALIZABLE, parity with the M2.1 T-ML40 mitigation pattern). A direct SQL insert bypassing the route is the same bound as 1.6 T-AI2; the verifier `--check-meetings` Gate 2 (per M2.1 review §C) cross-checks the metrics shape against the underlying rows and would flag the divergence. | SERIALIZABLE isolation upgrade is an S1 fold; direct-SQL is the documented bound. Acceptable. |
| T-IM31 | `action_item.closure_verified` chain anchor missing on a closed item — a bug in the closure-verification route's transactional discipline could write the closure-verification row + flip the action item's status WITHOUT emitting the chain anchor, breaking non-negotiable #2 chain-of-custody | new `POST /api/action-items/:id/closure-verifications` route; `audit_log` `action_item.closure_verified` kind | The closure-verification route opens a `db.transaction` that (a) verifies step-up freshness + WebAuthn assertion, (b) verifies the action item's pre-state allows `→ Closed`, (c) INSERTs the `action_item_closure_verifications` row with the Ed25519 attestation, (d) UPDATEs `action_items.status = 'Closed'` + `closure_verification_id = <new id>` + version bump, (e) EMITS `action_item.closure_verified` + `action_item.status_changed` chain rows in the same tx, (f) COMMITs. All six steps inside one transaction; a failure on any rolls back all. The `audit-log-verify --check-action-items` extension (M2.2 S2) cross-checks every `action_items` row with `status='Closed'` against the existence of `action_item.closure_verified` chain row referencing the same actionItemId (parity with M2.1 review §C Gate 1 "4-of-4 signature presence by role for `meeting.finalized`"). A missing chain row trips the verifier with `closed_missing_verification_anchor`. | Same transactional discipline as M2.1 finalize + adjourn; documented. |
| T-IM32 | Multiple closure-verifications recorded for the same action item — a rep accidentally taps "verify closure" twice; the route writes two `action_item_closure_verifications` rows; the chain shows two `action_item.closure_verified` events for one item and an arbitrator sees ambiguity about which is authoritative | new `action_item_closure_verifications` table; new `POST /api/action-items/:id/closure-verifications` route; idempotency middleware | The closure-verification route is wrapped by `idempotencyKey` middleware (per ADR-0009 §3.4 + parity with the action-items route header); a retry with the same key returns the cached response. For semantically-distinct double-taps (fresh idempotency keys), the DB enforces a partial UNIQUE on `(action_item_id) WHERE superseded_at IS NULL` on the `action_item_closure_verifications` table — only one ACTIVE verification per action item. A second tap with a fresh key hits the partial UNIQUE and returns 409 `closure_verification_already_exists` with the existing verification's id; the UI surfaces the existing verification rather than creating a duplicate. Re-open (T-IM4) flips `superseded_at = now()` on the old row, allowing a new verification on subsequent closure. Integration test asserts double-tap produces exactly one row + one chain row. | Same posture as M2.1 `meeting_signatures_meeting_role_unique` partial UNIQUE (T-ML8 mitigation parity); documented. |
| T-IM33 | Closure-verification attestation Ed25519 sig is forged via workplace signing key compromise — an attacker with the workplace signing key could craft an attestation signature over a closure-verification row that wasn't actually signed by the rep, binding a fake verification to a real action item | `action_item_closure_verifications.attestation_signed_ct`; `workplace_signing_keys` table; key residency | The workplace signing key is loaded from Fly Secrets per the 1.9 + M2.1 signing-key posture (per `apps/api/src/evidence/workplace-signing-key.ts`); the key lives in API process memory only during the signature operation and is `sodium.memzero`ed after (per M2.1 review F-S6). The key never leaves the API process. Key compromise = Fly Secrets compromise; the bound is the Fly-side secret-management posture (per SECURITY.md §3 Authentication + the deploy runbook). The `signing_key_id` FK on `action_item_closure_verifications` (parity with `meeting_signatures.signing_key_id`) records which key version signed; key rotation lands new signatures under the new key; the verifier independently re-verifies each signature against the right public key (parity with M2.1 review F-L2 multi-key residual). M2.2 S1 architectural fold: the `meeting.finalized` payload's `signingKeyIds: string[]` array (M2.1 F-L2 fix forward) is extended to `action_item.closure_verified` payloads with `signingKeyId: string` field. | Fly Secrets compromise is the bound (parity with M2.1 + 1.9); documented. |
| T-IM34 | In-meeting status PATCH writes a snapshot under the WRONG meeting_id — a rep with two meetings in scheduled state (rare but possible — the M2.1 single-active-meeting UNIQUE per `apps/api/src/db/schema.ts:1273+` constrains in_progress + pending_finalization, but not scheduled) PATCHes an action item with `meetingId=<wrong>` body field; the snapshot lands under the wrong meeting | `PATCH /api/action-items/:id` `meetingId` body field; `writeLiveActionItemSnapshot` helper | The `writeLiveActionItemSnapshot` helper (per `apps/api/src/routes/meetings/index.ts:2129-2134`) SELECTs the meeting's status and short-circuits when status is NOT `in_progress`; a `meetingId` pointing at a `scheduled` (or `pending_finalization`, `finalized`) meeting writes no snapshot row and emits no chain row. The M2.1 single-active-meeting partial UNIQUE on `(workplace_singleton) WHERE status IN ('in_progress','pending_finalization')` (per linkage review verified-clean §) means at most one meeting is in `in_progress` at a time; a wrong-meeting PATCH against a non-in_progress meeting is a no-op. M2.2 S2 adds a Zod refine on `PATCH /api/action-items/:id` body: if `meetingId` is provided, the route verifies the meeting exists AND is `in_progress` BEFORE entering the transaction; a stale `meetingId` returns 422 `meeting_not_in_progress` (parity with the helper's short-circuit but surfaced as an explicit error). | Single-active-meeting invariant + helper short-circuit + route-level Zod refine = defense-in-depth. Documented. |
| T-IM35 | Closure-verification on an action item whose `meeting_id` differs from the verifying meeting context — a rep is in Meeting B's live view but verifies the closure of an action item that was raised in Meeting A; the closure-verification row binds Meeting B (via the route's meeting context) while the action item's provenance is Meeting A; arbitrator confusion | new `POST /api/action-items/:id/closure-verifications` route; meeting context binding | The closure-verification is intentionally INDEPENDENT of meeting context — an action item can be closed at any time, in or out of a meeting (parity with non-negotiable #12 first-class status + M2.1 ADR-0012 §3.9 rights-protective copy "action items themselves do not wait on finalization"). The `action_item_closure_verifications` row does NOT carry a `meeting_id` column; the closure verification is a property of the action item, not the meeting. The chain payload `action_item.closure_verified` carries `{actionItemId, verifierActorId, verificationId}` — NO meeting_id (because the verification is meeting-independent). If the closure happens during a meeting, the in-meeting status PATCH ALSO writes a `live` snapshot per T-IM11 mitigation; the snapshot table separately captures the meeting context. An arbitrator reading the chain sees the closure-verification as an action-item-scoped event AND the meeting snapshot as a meeting-scoped event; the two events are independently auditable. | Decoupling closure from meeting context preserves non-negotiable #12; documented in the M2.2 runbook. |
| T-IM36 | Live-snapshot writer fires during a finalized meeting due to a race between adjournment commit and a pending PATCH — a PATCH arrives at the API after the `meeting.adjourned` transaction committed but before the client's Dexie cache invalidates; the helper's status check at `apps/api/src/routes/meetings/index.ts:2131-2134` reads `pending_finalization` and short-circuits, but the chain payload's `snapshot_at` could still be confusing | `writeLiveActionItemSnapshot` helper; `meeting_action_item_state` table; concurrent PATCH window | The helper's status check (per `apps/api/src/routes/meetings/index.ts:2131-2134`) reads the meeting status INSIDE the action-item PATCH transaction; the read sees the post-commit `pending_finalization` (or `finalized`) status and short-circuits — NO snapshot row, NO chain row. The action item's column PATCH still succeeds (the action item is unaffected by meeting finalization per non-negotiable #12) but the meeting-context snapshot does not land. The verifier `--check-action-items` extension cross-checks `action_item.status_changed` chain rows against `meeting_action_item_state` rows; a status change with a non-in_progress meeting context legitimately produces no snapshot, and the verifier expects this. The client's Dexie cache invalidates on next sync (per ADR-0009 §3.7 version-ratchet); the rep sees the consistent post-adjournment state. | Helper short-circuit + verifier expectation alignment = consistent. Documented. |
| T-IM37 | Counter-sign rate-limiting could chill legitimate batch closure at end-of-meeting — the adjournment section of a meeting may close 10-15 action items in rapid sequence; a per-actor rate-limit on the closure-verification route could rate-limit the rep into a UX dead-end | new `POST /api/action-items/:id/closure-verifications` rate-limit | The rate-limit posture mirrors the action-items route per `apps/api/src/routes/action-items/index.ts:64-68`: rateLimit BEFORE bodyLimit, bucket sized for a 90-minute meeting × 30 action items × 1 closure-verification per item × 3 retries = ~90 reqs/hour budget per actor. M2.2 S2 sizes the bucket at 120 reqs/hour (per-actor) with a burst of 20; the rep batch-closing 15 items in 5 minutes does not hit the limit. The step-up freshness window (60s, T-IM2 mitigation) is the more-constraining UX friction (rep re-step-ups every ~60s of batch-closing); the rate-limit is the safety floor. | Bucket sized for batch closure; documented. |
| T-IM38 | `action_item.closure_verified` chain payload divergence under cross-region replication — the Neon Postgres replica (ca-central-1 read replica per ARCHITECTURE.md) lags the primary; a verifier walking the chain via the replica could see closure-verification rows without their corresponding `action_item.closure_verified` chain rows (or vice versa) | `audit-log-verify --check-action-items` extension; Neon replica lag | The verifier ALWAYS runs against the PRIMARY (per ADR-0011 §3.7 + the deploy runbook); the `audit-log-verify` script connects to the primary connection string, not the replica. Production reads via the replica are read-only operational reads (the live-metrics endpoint, the meeting-detail GET); the chain integrity check runs scheduled against the primary. The replica's eventual consistency window (~100ms typical) is the bound for read-time stale data on the operational reads; the chain-integrity check is unaffected. | Primary-only verifier posture; documented in the M2.2 runbook + ADR-0011. |
| T-IM39 | A rep deletes their own session mid-counter-sign, leaving an in-flight transaction holding a partial state — the rep signs out from a different device during the closure-verification flow; the in-flight transaction's auth context is invalidated; the transaction rolls back; no row, no chain | session invalidation; closure-verification transaction; auth middleware | The auth middleware (per `apps/api/src/auth/step-up`) validates the session at request entry; a sign-out during a long-running request keeps the request's auth context valid (the request has its own session snapshot). The transaction either commits (the closure-verification lands + the chain row emits) or rolls back (nothing lands); there is no partial-write scenario. Subsequent requests under the invalidated session fail at the auth middleware (401). The chain integrity is preserved (a failed transaction = no chain row, parity with M2.1 verified-clean §C "transactions roll back together"). | Atomic transaction + session-snapshot pattern = no partial state. Documented. |
| T-IM40 | The new `closure_verification_id` FK on `action_items` is exposed in the GET response, leaking the verification's existence to a viewer who lacks permission to see the verification row — a forward-seam role-separation scenario where some reps can see the action item but not the closure-verification narrative | `GET /api/action-items/:id` projection; `action_items.closure_verification_id` column | Single-tenant scope: every authenticated rep sees the same data; the closure_verification_id FK is returned in the GET projection alongside the other action-item fields. The narrative ciphertext lives in `action_item_closure_verifications.narrative_ct` and is decrypted client-side under the workplace public key (parity with M2.1 attendee-name posture). When role-separation lands (forward-seam to Release 2.x per M2.1 §2.13 gap #2), the GET projection will conditionally omit the FK + the verification details based on the requester's role; the column-level access pattern is structurally compatible with that future change. The chain payload `action_item.closure_verified` is the audit-of-record; an authenticated rep walking the chain sees the verification events regardless of GET-projection visibility (parity with M2.1 attendance ⁠— the chain records the truth; the GET surfaces what the role permits). | Forward-seam role-separation will gate the FK in the projection; today's single-tenant scope reveals all. Documented. |
| T-IM41 | The closure-verification's WebAuthn challenge is bound to `actionItemId` but NOT to the action item's pre-closure content hash; an attacker who can replay a step-up grant within the freshness window could close a DIFFERENT action item than the rep intended by swapping the path parameter | T-IM1 + T-IM2 follow-on; WebAuthn assertion challenge composition | Per T-IM1's deepening fold (parity with M2.1 review F-S4) the WebAuthn `clientDataJSON` challenge for the closure-verification flow includes `actionItemId` AND the action item's `version` (the optimistic-concurrency etag at the time of the rep's tap). A replay attempt against a DIFFERENT action item fails because the challenge embedded in the WebAuthn assertion does not match the path parameter's actionItemId; the route verifies the assertion's challenge equals `H(actionItemId || version || sessionId || meetingContextId)` before committing the transaction. The `version` binding means a stale assertion (the item was modified between tap and submit) fails too — the rep re-step-ups against the current state. | WebAuthn challenge composition includes per-resource binding; documented as the T-IM1+T-IM2 deepening. |
| T-IM42 | The M2.2 metrics live-update endpoint reveals the existence of in-progress meetings to a non-co-chair rep who could otherwise be unaware — a future multi-rep role-separation scenario where some reps shouldn't know a meeting is happening | `GET /api/meetings/:id/metrics/live`; single-tenant scope | Single-tenant scope + single-co-chair scope (per ADR-0001) means there is one rep operator; the "non-co-chair rep who shouldn't know" scenario doesn't exist in M2.2. Forward-seam: when role-separation lands (M2.1 §2.13 gap #2 + T-IM20 family), the live-metrics endpoint will gate on the requesting rep's role (e.g., only the worker co-chair + worker reps assigned to the meeting can read); the structural shape is ready (the endpoint already authenticates; adding a role-check is additive). | Forward-seam to Release 2.x role-separation; documented. |
| T-IM43 | Closure-verification narrative reveals a worker's identity that should be protected (e.g., "Accommodation for [name] resolved — counter-signed") — the rep types a name into the narrative field; the field is envelope-encrypted but every authenticated rep can decrypt it via the same workplace KEK | `action_item_closure_verifications.narrative_ct`; rep input discipline; multi-tier visibility forward-seam | Single-tenant scope per M2.1 T-ML25 — every authenticated rep can decrypt the narrative. The rights-protective copy in the narrative field's helper text directs reps to the appropriate confidential surfaces: "For accommodation, reprisal, or critical-injury content, use the dedicated trackers (M2.7 Reprisal, M2.8 Accommodation) rather than capturing names in closure narratives." The helper text is the structural cue; the multi-tier visibility forward-seam (gap #2 from M2.1 §2.13 + T-IM20 / T-IM40) is the eventual close-out. The chain payload carries `narrativeHash` only, not plaintext (T-IM5). | Forward-seam to M2.7/M2.8 + role-separation; helper text is the structural cue. Documented. |
| T-IM44 | The action-item PATCH route's status-transition graph is the new gate (per T-IM3); a regression that loosens the graph silently permits direct `→ Closed` PATCH bypassing the closure-verification flow | `packages/shared-types/src/action-item-transitions.ts` (extended in M2.2 S1); PATCH route | The transition graph is a pure function in shared-types (parity with M2.1 `meeting-transitions.ts` per ADR-0012 §3.1); the graph asserts the legal status transitions. M2.2 S1 extends the graph to ENCODE that `* → Closed` is reachable ONLY via the closure-verification route (the graph function gains a `via: 'patch' | 'closure_verification'` parameter; calling with `via='patch'` for any `→ Closed` returns false). Exhaustive unit tests in `packages/shared-types/src/action-item-transitions.test.ts` assert legal/illegal pairs for all 6 statuses × 2 via-paths (parity with M2.1 pure-function unit test pattern). A regression that loosens the graph trips the test suite in CI; the DB CHECK on `action_items.status='Closed' ⇒ closure_verification_id IS NOT NULL` (T-IM3 mitigation) is the structural backstop if the graph regresses past CI. | Pure function + exhaustive test + DB CHECK = defense in depth. Documented. |

#### Cross-cutting controls

- **Step-up freshness on closure-verification.** The new `POST /api/action-items/:id/closure-verifications` route requires `factorRequired = 'passkey'` (TOTP rejected) + `maxAgeSeconds = 60` + a fresh WebAuthn assertion whose `clientDataJSON` challenge includes `actionItemId + version + sessionId + meetingContextId` (T-IM1 + T-IM41). The PATCH route's new step-up gate for `Closed → *` re-open paths (T-IM4) requires `action='action_item.reopen'` + same 60s window. All other M2.2 routes (in-meeting PATCH status/section, live-metrics GET, move-history GET) are NOT step-up gated — matching ADR-0012 §3.10's "routine operations are not gated" pattern.
- **Envelope encryption + cross-chain anchor reuse.** All new sensitive fields (`action_item_closure_verifications.narrative_ct`) are envelope-encrypted at the application layer with per-row DEKs under the workplace KEK; the `attestation_signed_ct` column is the Ed25519 detached signature per the M2.1 TM-fold-4 pattern. The cross-chain anchor `meeting.action_item_status_changed` reuses `computeChainEntryHash` (per `apps/api/src/routes/meetings/index.ts:2179`) for hash composition. KEK rotation runbook is extended with the new table.
- **Audit chain on every state transition.** M2.2 adds the following chain kinds: `action_item.closure_verified` (closure verification event), `action_item.reopened` (re-open from Closed), `action_item.status_changed` (in-meeting status PATCH — extending the existing 1.6 status-change semantics with the meeting context binding), `meeting.action_item_status_changed` (cross-chain anchor wrapping the action_item.status_changed when emitted inside a meeting). Each kind has a documented payload in `packages/shared-types/src/audit-event-kind.ts` with the T-AC9-class no-PI discipline; the verifier `--check-action-items` extension (M2.2 S2) walks the kinds end-to-end.
- **Rights-protective copy review checklist.** Extended from M2.1 §2.13 to cover: (a) no "wait for JHSC approval" framing on the closure-verification UI (T-IM25); (b) no "why" framing on the narrative field (T-IM26); (c) no per-actor counts in dashboards (T-IM27); (d) narrative-field helper text directs reprisal/accommodation/critical-injury content to dedicated trackers (T-IM43); (e) the closure-verification copy frames the rep as records custodian, not as supplicant (T-IM25 + T-IM26).

#### Known gaps (forward seams)

1. **Multi-tier visibility (co-chair-only / role-gated) does not structurally exist in M2.2.** Single-tenant scope means every authenticated rep can decrypt every closure-verification narrative + read every move-history actor + read every metrics dashboard. The forward-seam is the multi-tier role-separation pattern (M2.1 §2.13 gap #2 + T-IM20 / T-IM40 / T-IM42 / T-IM43); the M2.2 schema is structurally ready (the `closure_verification_id` FK + the `verifier_actor_id` columns + the metrics endpoint's role-blind authentication all accommodate a future role check without schema migration).
2. **Closure-verification evidence Tigris orphan-ciphertext GC** is deferred to Release 2.x hardening (T-IM6); the same GC job that handles 1.7 evidence + M2.1 off-app signature evidence + closure-verification evidence is the single forward-seam.
3. **Multi-key meeting attestation** (M2.1 review F-L2) extension to closure-verifications — if the workplace KEK rotates between a closure-verification and the meeting's finalization, the meeting carries closure-verifications under multiple signing-key versions; the `meeting.finalized` payload (per M2.1 F-L2 fix) should be extended to include `closureVerificationSigningKeyIds: string[]`. M2.2 S1 architectural fold: this fold lands in S1 to keep the meeting finalization's key-of-record auditing complete.
4. **Live-metrics endpoint caching layer** is documented-deferred (T-IM18); a future Release 2.x perf optimization that adds a cache MUST include the meeting `version` in the cache key + a per-workplace namespace.
5. **Custom action-item sections** are deferred to Release 3 per M2.1 S0 user-decision (T-IM9); M2.2 preserves the closed-section-enum invariant.
6. **Release 3 absorbs:** (a) E2EE messaging between reps about a specific action item's closure-verification (currently single-rep scope; multi-rep deliberation on whether to counter-sign is R3 per the M2.1 Release 3 forward-seam list); (b) AI-assisted closure-verification narrative drafting via the Adversarial Lens ("how would a hostile arbitrator read this closure narrative?" generates counter-arguments before the rep records the basis); (c) push notifications for "your closure-verification is pending review" (forward-seam to a multi-rep workflow); (d) the closure-verification audit-row-redaction pattern (per M2.1 §2.13 gap T-ML24 forward-seam — the redaction table is post-Release-1 backlog).

#### S1 architectural folds

The M2.2 threat model surfaces five architectural concerns that need to land in S1 to satisfy the threat coverage:

1. **TM-fold-1 (T-IM3 / T-IM44) — `closure_verification_id` FK column + DB CHECK on `action_items`.** S1 adds `action_items.closure_verification_id UUID` (nullable; FK to `action_item_closure_verifications.id`, ON DELETE RESTRICT) + a DB CHECK `(status = 'Closed') = (closure_verification_id IS NOT NULL)` enforcing the bi-directional invariant. The migration includes an integration test asserting the CHECK rejects `status='Closed' + closure_verification_id=NULL` AND `status!='Closed' + closure_verification_id != NULL`.
2. **TM-fold-2 (T-IM11) — `writeLiveActionItemSnapshot` dedupe.** S1 modifies the helper at `apps/api/src/routes/meetings/index.ts:2116-2166` to read the most-recent live snapshot for the (meeting_id, action_item_id) tuple and short-circuit (no INSERT, no chain row) if `(snapshot_status, snapshot_section, assignee_hash)` matches; only ACTUAL state changes write rows. Unit test asserts a fresh-key retry with unchanged state writes no row.
3. **TM-fold-3 (T-IM27 + T-IM18) — live-metrics payload Zod schema + no-cache route header.** S1 lands the Zod schema for the live-metrics response that explicitly excludes per-actor fields AND adds a route-header comment ("no cache layer; metrics are recomputed on each GET; if added, key MUST include meeting.version") to prevent drift.
4. **TM-fold-4 (T-IM30) — SERIALIZABLE isolation on the adjournment transaction.** S1 upgrades the `db.transaction` block in the adjournment route (per `apps/api/src/routes/meetings/index.ts:1559-1709`) to SERIALIZABLE isolation level (parity with the T-ML40 mitigation pattern); integration test asserts a concurrent live-snapshot INSERT during the adjournment transaction either serializes-and-loses or is included in the snapshot (no phantom rows post-COUNT-pre-chain-emit).
5. **TM-fold-5 (T-IM33 + M2.1 F-L2 forward) — `signingKeyId` on `action_item_closure_verifications` + extension of `meeting.finalized` payload.** S1 adds `action_item_closure_verifications.signing_key_id UUID NOT NULL` FK to `workplace_signing_keys.id` (parity with `meeting_signatures.signing_key_id`); S1 also extends the `meeting.finalized` chain payload to include `closureVerificationSigningKeyIds: string[]` aggregating the signing-key ids for the meeting's closure verifications (M2.1 F-L2 deepening).

**M2.2 adds 4 new audit event kinds: `action_item.closure_verified`, `action_item.reopened`, `action_item.status_changed` (extends the in-meeting status PATCH semantics; the existing 1.6 emit kind is reused with the meeting-context payload extension), `meeting.action_item_status_changed` (cross-chain anchor parallel to M2.1's `meeting.recommendation_drafted`).** The deploy runbook's `audit-log-verify --full` is extended with `--check-action-items` (parity with M2.1's `--check-meetings`) covering: (1) every `action_items.status='Closed'` row has a `action_item.closure_verified` chain row; (2) every `action_item.reopened` chain row has a corresponding superseded `closure_verification` row; (3) every `meeting.action_item_status_changed` cross-chain anchor's payload hash matches the upstream `action_item.status_changed` event's canonical hash; (4) the `action_items.first_raised_meeting_id` column matches the `action_item.created` chain row's payload (T-IM12 mitigation). The prefix space `T-IM*` does NOT collide with M2.1's `T-ML*` (44 T-ML* threats in §2.13 + 44 T-IM* threats in §2.14); the two prefix families are orthogonal and the verifier walks both kinds independently.

### 2.15 Minutes Document Generation (M2.3)

#### Surface summary

Milestone 2.3 is the first time the M2.1 + M2.2 meeting substrate (encrypted notes, attendee identities, attendance roster, 4-signer attestations, action item snapshot, closure verifications, adjournment metrics) is rendered into an **externally-distributable artifact**: the canonical minutes PDF that lands in front of management, the JHSC, the union, and — when a dispute escalates — the MLITSD or an arbitrator. The threat model pivots: prior milestones defended the in-app substrate against tamper and exfiltration; M2.3 defends the **shape of the document the rep distributes** against forgery, content-vs-chain divergence, and rights-protective copy regressions that turn the distribution UX into management-side pressure. M2.3 is the canonical surface for non-negotiable #16 (step-up + audit + document hash) applied to the meeting record, and inherits the §2.8 (inspection PDF, ADR-0007 §3.9) + §2.9 (recommendation PDF, ADR-0008 §3.7) prior-art baseline — every threat below cites the inherited control or names the new M2.3 deepening.

#### Threats — T-MD1..T-MD46

**A. PDF generation pipeline integrity**

| # | What / Where | Mitigation | Residual |
|---|---|---|---|
| T-MD1 | **Document hash collision** — an attacker generates a "twin" PDF whose bytes SHA-256 to the same value as a legitimate minutes PDF, then swaps in distribution. Where: `POST /api/meetings/:id/minutes-document` rendered-bytes hash; chain payload `documentHash` field. | SHA-256 collision resistance is the cryptographic assumption (parity with §2.8 T-I23 + §2.9 T-R26 + §2.13 T-ML23). A practical second-preimage attack is not known; a future hash-algorithm upgrade rides the standard rewrap pattern (1.3 §3a runbook). The document hash composes with the workplace signing-key Ed25519 detached signature (T-MD7 mitigation reuse) so an attacker needs to break SHA-256 AND forge the workplace signing key. | SHA-256 break = bound. Acceptable; same posture as the inherited PDF surfaces. |
| T-MD2 | **Same-meeting-different-document race** — two concurrent `POST /api/meetings/:id/minutes-document` requests render two PDFs with non-identical bytes (different `now()`-stamped footer timestamps), both upload to Tigris, both anchor in the chain — leaving the rep with two "canonical" docs and an arbitrator with two divergent hashes. Where: minutes-document POST handler; Tigris PUT; chain emit. | The route opens a `db.transaction` with `isolationLevel: 'serializable'` (TM-fold-4 pattern from M2.2 §2.14) and `SELECT … FROM meetings WHERE id=$1 FOR UPDATE` to serialize the rendering. The route is wrapped by `idempotencyKey()` middleware (ADR-0009 §3.4) so a retry returns the cached response. The body schema accepts an optional `clientId UUID` (ADR-0009 §3.3) so the client-side queue can de-duplicate at the queue layer. The second concurrent caller serializes and either (a) gets the first commit's response via the idempotency cache, or (b) receives 409 `minutes_document_already_generated_for_version` keyed on the meeting's `version` column. | Same bound as M2.1 T-ML32 (adjourn-race). Documented. |
| T-MD3 | **Render-failure rollback — orphan chain anchor** — Tigris PUT succeeds, the `db.transaction` commits the `minutes_documents` row + `minutes_document.generated` chain anchor, then the response-write fails; OR the chain anchor commits but a follow-up Tigris PUT fails and the chain references a `storage_key` that doesn't exist. Where: minutes-document POST handler ordering of PUT vs INSERT vs `append()`. | Ordering follows §2.8 T-I42 close-out: (1) render the PDF bytes in memory; (2) compute the bytes-SHA-256 (T-MD15 binding); (3) Tigris PUT under `exports/<minutes_document.id>/minutes-<uuid>.pdf`; (4) open `db.transaction`; (5) INSERT `minutes_documents`; (6) emit `minutes_document.generated` chain row carrying `documentHash`; (7) COMMIT. The PUT happens BEFORE the transaction so the transaction's rollback can best-effort `deleteEvidenceObject(storageKey)` in catch (same shape as §2.8 sec-F6). The chain row is never emitted without the row, and the row is never written without the PUT having returned 200. | Tigris best-effort delete on rollback can fail (NoSuchKey, network); the lifecycle/orphan-GC posture (T-MD25) is the residual cleanup. |
| T-MD4 | **Forward-state plaintext leak via error body** — the renderer decrypts attendee names + section notes + signer display names, hits a mid-render exception (font load failure, signature embed failure, OOM on a large attachment), and the exception's message bubbles up through Hono's `onError` carrying a stack frame that captured the decrypted plaintext in a closure or local var. Where: `renderMinutesPdf()` exception path; Hono error middleware. | The render function wraps every decrypt-touching block in try/finally with `sodium.memzero` on every plaintext buffer that backs a `Uint8Array` (parity with §2.8 T-I23, recommendation §2.9 T-R23). JS strings (attendee display name, section notes plaintext) cannot be `memzero`'d — same documented tradeoff as 1.5 hazards descriptionCt; the route's error handler returns a **fixed-shape body** `{error: 'minutes_document_render_failed', reason: <enum>}` and NEVER includes `err.message` or `err.stack` in the response (the existing Hono `onError` middleware redacts; M2.3 S1 adds an integration test asserting the response body contains none of the input plaintext markers — parity with 1.5 T-H4 redaction test). The chain emits `minutes_document.render_failed` (no payload PI; just `{meetingId, reasonEnum}`) for diagnosability — parity with the §2.8 T-I24 close-out that consolidated into the HTTP-response failure surface. | None material; same bound as the inherited PDF error paths. |
| T-MD5 | **Source Serif 4 font load failure** — the Fly Machine's font file is missing/corrupted; the PDF renders with `pdfkit`'s fallback Helvetica and looks visually distinct from prior minutes, raising authenticity questions in arbitration. Where: `renderMinutesPdf()` font-load; Fly Machine filesystem. | Source Serif 4 TTF is bundled into the API docker image at build time (NOT downloaded at runtime; no third-party CDN per non-negotiable #3). The renderer registers the font with `pdfkit.font('SourceSerif4')` at process boot in a one-time `prepareRenderer()` helper that throws on registration failure — the process exits and the deployment health check fails. A render-time font swap is structurally impossible because `pdfkit.registerFont` is called once. Golden-PDF test (per §2.8 T-I25 pattern) asserts the font name in the embedded font dictionary equals `SourceSerif4-Regular` on every PR. | Font-name impersonation by an attacker who controls a future PR is bounded by code review + the golden-PDF test. |
| T-MD6 | **Page X of Y miscount across re-runs** — the same finalized meeting generates a PDF on day 1 with "Page 3 of 14" and a re-generation on day 30 with "Page 3 of 15" because `pdfkit`'s layout engine produced different page-break boundaries (font-metric drift, sub-pixel rounding); non-determinism breaks the T-MD17 idempotency hash. Where: `renderMinutesPdf()` layout pass; page-footer string. | The renderer pins (a) `pdfkit` version in `package.json`, (b) the Source Serif 4 TTF bytes (same docker layer), (c) every `pdfkit` layout option (`pageBreaks`, `lineGap`, `paragraphGap`, `widows`, `orphans`). The page-footer string is rendered AFTER the layout pass closes via `pdfkit`'s second-pass API (per §2.8 T-I27 footer-hash two-pass dance) so the footer's "Page X of Y" + the document-hash placeholder are filled into reserved slots with byte-identical widths. A golden-PDF determinism test runs the renderer twice on the same fixture and asserts byte-equality on every PR. | Library/font upgrade that changes layout would trip the test; documented as a deployment-checklist item paralleling §2.8 T-I27. |

**B. Decryption-at-render**

| # | What / Where | Mitigation | Residual |
|---|---|---|---|
| T-MD7 | **Workplace KEK + signing private key in memory during render** — the render decrypts every `meeting_attendance.display_name_ct`, `meeting_sections.notes_ct`, `meeting_signatures.signer_display_name_ct`, `meeting_signatures.evidence_envelope_ct`, `action_item_closure_verifications.narrative_ct` per the M2.1 + M2.2 substrate, AND opens the workplace Ed25519 signing private key to detached-sign the document hash; the KEK + signing key co-reside in the Fly Machine's JS heap for the duration of one request. Where: `renderMinutesPdf()`; `@jhsc/crypto/sealField`; `openWorkplaceSigningPrivateKey`. | Per §2.8 T-I23 + §2.9 T-R23 + M2.1 §2.13 F-S6 honest stance: both keys live in `sodium_malloc`-backed buffers from `@jhsc/crypto`; the KEK is process-loaded once at boot from Fly Secrets; the signing private key is opened per-request and `sodium.memzero`'d in the `finally` block of the render handler. The render transaction is bounded (sub-second target; serializable lock prevents pile-up). The signing key is opened AFTER all decrypts complete and IMMEDIATELY before the detached signature, narrowing the co-residence window. | Bun GC may copy buffers before `memzero`; same bound as §2.8 T-I23. The KEK rotation runbook (1.3 §3a) covers the post-incident rotation path. |
| T-MD8 | **Render-time decryption leaks PII to API logs** — Hono's request logger captures `c.req.json()` body + route handler `console.log` lines; a forgotten debug log inside the render path emits a decrypted attendee name into the API log stream, escaping the chain payload's no-PI invariant (T-ML class extension to the render surface). Where: `renderMinutesPdf()`; route handler; Pino logger middleware. | The CLAUDE.md "no `console.log` in committed code" pre-merge gate is the structural rule; the M2.3 S1 lint extends the existing 1.12 grep-for-console.log to flag `apps/api/src/routes/meetings/minutes-document*.ts` AND `apps/api/src/meetings/pdf-renderer.ts`. The Pino logger is configured with a `redact` list that includes `attendees[].displayName`, `sections[].notes`, `signers[].displayName`, `closureVerifications[].narrative` — any log entry whose JSON shape matches gets the field replaced with `[REDACTED]` (parity with the 1.2 auth redact list). Integration test asserts a happy-path render emits no log line containing the input plaintext marker. | Operator-side log scraping is the trust boundary; same bound as §2.9 T-R28. Documented. |
| T-MD9 | **Envelope-encryption auth failure mid-render** — a `meeting_sections.notes_ct` row has a corrupted GCM/XChaCha20-Poly1305 tag (DB-level tamper, disk-bit-rot on Neon's replica, partial KEK rotation that left a row's DEK encrypted under an old KEK); the render fails halfway through, the rep gets a partial PDF, AND the partial bytes get a chain anchor. Where: `openField()` decrypt call inside render loop. | Per §2.8 T-I24 close-out pattern: the render is "all or nothing" — every decrypt happens inside the `try` block before any byte is written to `pdfkit`. A single `openField` AEAD failure throws `EnvelopeAuthFailed`; the catch aborts the render, no bytes leave memory, no Tigris PUT happens, no chain row emits. The route returns 500 `minutes_document_render_failed` with `reason: 'envelope_auth_failed'` and `{meetingId, fieldRef: <opaque locator>}` for operator diagnosis (no plaintext). The KEK rotation runbook (1.3 §3a) is the post-incident path. | A genuine bit-rot on Neon's storage is bounded by Postgres checksums + Neon's own replication; documented in the deploy runbook as an operator-side detect path. |
| T-MD10 | **Cross-meeting KEK / signing-key reuse leak** — the renderer mistakenly opens meeting B's signing key while rendering meeting A's PDF; the detached signature in meeting A's PDF is computed under the wrong key, and the verifier's `--check-minutes-documents` Gate (T-MD40) flags but a rep distributing the PDF has already shipped an unverifiable artifact. Where: `renderMinutesPdf()` signing key resolution; `meetings.signing_key_id` projection. | The workplace signing key is single-tenant per CLAUDE.md (one workplace, one active signing key at a time, identified by `workplace_signing_keys.id`). The render reads `meetings.signing_key_id` from the meeting row via the same FOR UPDATE row lock (T-MD2) and passes it to `openWorkplaceSigningPrivateKey(db, keyId)`. There is NO meeting-A-vs-meeting-B selection drift because there is one active key. If KEK rotation happens between adjournment and minutes-document generation, the route uses the meeting's pinned `signing_key_id` (NOT the workplace's current active key) — parity with §2.9 T-R32 / M2.1 §2.13 F-L2 deepening + M2.2 TM-fold-5. The chain anchor `minutes_document.generated` carries `signingKeyId` so the verifier can re-look-up. | Same bound as M2.1/M2.2 signing-key surfaces. |
| T-MD11 | **Closure-reason ciphertext rendered to externally-distributed PDF without key-holder opt-out** — M2.2 framed closure-verification narratives (`narrative_ct`) as the rep's evidence of what was actually closed; an arbitrator-bound PDF distributing every closure narrative verbatim escalates the T-IM26 surveillance framing to the management-distribution surface. Where: `renderMinutesPdf()` closure-verification section; published-export vs internal-export branching. | The render emits **TWO** outputs per request (the M2.3 body schema field `audience: 'internal' | 'published'`): the **internal** version retains every closure narrative verbatim; the **published** version replaces each narrative body with the structured CLOSE-VERIFIED stub `"Closure verified: {actionItemRef} (counter-signed {role} {timestamp})"` and omits the freetext narrative. Both versions get distinct document hashes + distinct chain anchors + distinct Tigris keys. The rep's distribution flow (T-MD18..T-MD23) records WHICH version each recipient received. The published version is the management-co-chair-distributable default; the internal version is co-chair-only and is what the rep retains in personal-evidence custody. Rights-protective copy on the audience selector explicitly says: "The published version omits closure narratives. You may include them only if you have re-verified that the narrative content is non-PI and that you intend to share it externally." | Worker-co-chair-discretion to ship the internal version outside the workplace is the residual; documented as a usage-policy bound paralleling M2.1 T-ML9 (in_camera redaction). |

**C. Document hash + chain anchor**

| # | What / Where | Mitigation | Residual |
|---|---|---|---|
| T-MD12 | **Document-hash forgery via collision crafting** — variant of T-MD1 framed at the chain level: an attacker generates a PDF whose footer-embedded hash matches a legitimate prior minutes document's hash. Where: chain anchor `documentHash` field; PDF footer rendering. | The chain anchor's `documentHash` is **the SHA-256 of the final rendered bytes after** the page-footer "Document hash: <full sha256>" is two-pass-filled (T-MD6 / T-I27 dance). A second-preimage attack needs to produce bytes whose SHA-256 matches AND whose footer string matches AND whose Ed25519 detached signature (from the workplace signing key) verifies (T-MD10). All three constraints are computationally bounded by SHA-256 + Ed25519. The published PDF embeds the **full** 64-char hex hash in the footer (NOT truncated; see T-MD16). | Same as T-MD1. |
| T-MD13 | **Successful generation does not emit chain row** — the route writes the `minutes_documents` row + Tigris PUT, but the `append('minutes_document.generated', payload)` call is forgotten, silently regressing under code drift; verifier `--check-minutes-documents` cross-walks rows-vs-chain and catches AFTER the fact, but the rep has already distributed an un-anchored PDF. Where: minutes-document POST handler; chain emit. | The route opens a `db.transaction` that wraps INSERT + `append()` together; the test (M2.3 S1 lands as parity with M2.1 F-S3) asserts that a successful POST emits exactly one `minutes_document.generated` chain row with the matching `documentHash`. The migration includes an integration test asserting the chain row's payload-shape map (1.12 T-HD28) covers `minutes_document.generated`. The verifier `--check-minutes-documents` gate (T-MD40) is the structural backstop: every `minutes_documents` row MUST have a `minutes_document.generated` chain row whose payload's `documentHash` matches the row's `document_hash` column. | Same bound as M2.1 T-ML22 + M2.2 T-IM31; documented. |
| T-MD14 | **Chain anchor present but Tigris object missing** — the chain emits `minutes_document.generated` with the storage key, the Tigris PUT then 5xx's, the catch fires the best-effort delete (a no-op since the key was never written), the route returns 500, but the chain row is committed because the PUT happened BEFORE the transaction (T-MD3) — wait, in the T-MD3 ordering the PUT happens BEFORE the txn, so a PUT failure aborts pre-txn and no chain row writes. The inverse race: the transaction commits the chain row + the row's `storage_key`, then the chain log replicas serialize but Tigris's eventually-consistent metadata shows the object as missing for several seconds; a verifier run during that window flags a false positive. Where: `--check-minutes-documents` verifier vs Tigris HEAD; eventual consistency window. | The verifier's `--check-minutes-documents --check-tigris` mode (M2.3 S2) does a `HeadObject` against every storage_key referenced in a `minutes_document.generated` chain row; the gate accepts a 5-minute eventual-consistency grace window (the row's `chain_emitted_at` must be > 5 minutes old for a missing-object to register as failure). The route's transaction order (PUT THEN INSERT THEN append THEN COMMIT) means a successful chain commit implies a 200 from the PUT. | Tigris durability is the trust boundary; the AES256 SSE setting (§2.8 priv-F1 close-out) is inherited. |
| T-MD15 | **Footer-embedded hash != actual byte hash** — the page footer renders "Document hash: <hex>" but a layout regression places the hash in a buffer that is NOT the buffer SHA-256'd for the chain anchor; the rep distributes a PDF whose footer claims hash H1 but whose actual bytes hash to H2. Where: two-pass footer fill in `renderMinutesPdf()`. | Per §2.8 T-I27 two-pass dance: the renderer writes the PDF with a `__HASH__` 64-char placeholder in the footer, computes SHA-256 over the rendered-with-placeholder bytes, then does an in-buffer byte-substitution of the placeholder with the hex hash; the post-replace hash is recomputed and stored as `documentHash`. The route asserts `footer_hash_field == post_replace_hash` before any chain emit; a mismatch throws `FooterHashMismatch` and aborts. Golden-PDF test asserts the relationship on every PR. | The two-pass dance is fiddly (§2.8 Risks); golden test is the bound. |
| T-MD16 | **Page-footer hash truncation collision** — to fit the footer line width, the rendered "Document hash: <prefix>" displays only the first N hex chars; over N=12 (48 bits), 2^24 documents expected before a birthday-bound collision; over the workplace's expected 24 meetings/year × 30 years = 720 documents, a 12-char truncation is comfortable but a future operator could reduce it for layout reasons. Where: footer hash display width. | The PDF footer carries the **full 64-char SHA-256 hex** (no truncation), rendered in JetBrains Mono 7pt across two lines if needed (parity with the inspections PDF footer per §2.8). The body schema rejects any `displayHashWidth` configuration. The chain payload carries the full hash; the footer carries the full hash; both match by the T-MD15 two-pass discipline. The UI's "share this document hash" affordance (in the rep's minutes-document detail view) copies the full 64-char hex. | None material; documented. |
| T-MD17 | **Idempotent re-generation produces same document hash if content matches** — re-running generation on a finalized meeting whose content has not changed should produce a byte-identical PDF (T-MD6 determinism), and therefore the same `documentHash`. A rep who generates the doc twice and worries about "two different hashes" sees that the chain shows two `minutes_document.generated` events with the same `documentHash` — confirming determinism. Where: chain payload `documentHash` field; verifier semantics. | Documented posture, not a vulnerability. The verifier `--check-minutes-documents` Gate 4 (T-MD40) accepts multiple `minutes_document.generated` events per meeting with the same `documentHash`; a divergent `documentHash` for the same meeting's `version` is the anomaly (T-MD29 race / T-MD30 format-version mismatch). The Tigris layer stores one object per chain event (one storage_key per row); a re-generation that hashes identically still gets a fresh storage_key + chain row to preserve audit-row indices. | None material. |

**D. Distribution tracking**

| # | What / Where | Mitigation | Residual |
|---|---|---|---|
| T-MD18 | **Distribution chain payload PI leak** — the rep records "sent to <Recipient Display Name>" via `POST /api/meetings/:id/minutes-document/distributions` and the chain payload carries the recipient's plaintext name, escalating the T-ML class no-PI invariant. Where: `minutes_document.distributed` chain anchor payload. | The chain payload carries `{meetingId, minutesDocumentId, documentHash, recipientHash, recipientRoleEnum, distributionMethodEnum, distributedAtRecorded}`. `recipientHash` is SHA-256 of the canonicalized recipient label (lower-cased, trim-whitespace, NFC-normalized); the plaintext label lives ONLY in the `minutes_document_distributions.recipient_label_ct` envelope-encrypted column. The `recipientRoleEnum` is the structural enum (`mgmt_co_chair | warehouse_mgr | plant_mgr | union_rep | jhsc_committee_member | mlitsd_inspector | arbitrator | other`); no free-text role goes in the chain. Mirrors the T-ML class discipline. Integration test asserts the chain payload JSON contains no plaintext recipient marker. | None material; same bound as M2.1 T-ML24 + M2.2 T-IM27. |
| T-MD19 | **Distribution event for a non-existent minutes-document** — a hand-crafted POST records a distribution against a `minutes_document_id` UUID that does not exist (a typo, a stale client cache, a malicious caller); the chain row anchors a distribution-of-nothing. Where: `POST /api/meetings/:id/minutes-document/distributions`. | The route opens a `db.transaction` that runs `SELECT id, status, document_hash FROM minutes_documents WHERE id=$1 AND meeting_id=$2 FOR SHARE`; absence returns 422 `minutes_document_not_found`. The `minutes_document_distributions.minutes_document_id` column FKs with `ON DELETE RESTRICT`. The chain emit is inside the same transaction as the INSERT; the row + the chain row land together. | None material. |
| T-MD20 | **Distribution against a never-finalized meeting** — the rep tries to distribute a PDF for a meeting in `adjourned` or `pending_finalization`; the PDF was never canonically signed and should not leave the workplace as "the minutes." Where: `POST /api/meetings/:id/minutes-document` (generation gate); `POST /api/meetings/:id/minutes-document/distributions` (distribution gate). | Both routes assert `meetings.status = 'finalized'` in their `FOR UPDATE` projection (parity with §2.8 T-I35 `inspection.state = 'complete'` gate). A 422 `meeting_not_finalized` is returned before any decrypt or any byte renders. The body schema validation happens after the state gate, so a forged POST cannot even reach the decrypt path. The PDF generator surface explicitly carries the per-ADR-0012 §3.9 finalization contract. | None material — the state gate is structural per ADR-0012 §3.9. |
| T-MD21 | **Distribution recipient impersonation — paper handoff claim** — the rep records `distributionMethod: 'paper_handoff'` to `recipientLabel: 'Mgmt Co-Chair'` but did not actually hand the paper to the management co-chair; the chain records the CLAIM, not the actual transmission. Where: `minutes_document_distributions.distribution_method`; chain payload `distributionMethodEnum`. | The chain payload records the rep's CLAIMED distribution faithfully (`distributionMethodEnum`, `recipientHash`, `distributedAtRecorded`). The route does NOT pretend to verify physical delivery. The body schema includes an optional `evidenceEnvelopeCt` (envelope-encrypted attestation that the rep was able to capture — a signed delivery receipt photo, an email body screenshot) with the same Tigris evidence pipeline as M2.1 external-signer attestations (§2.13 T-ML5). If supplied, the chain payload carries `evidenceHash`. The rep's worker-side narrative is "I distributed; this is the evidence I captured." An arbitrator weighs the rep's discipline; same evidentiary posture as the T-ML5 paper-attestation residual. | Documented residual; same shape as the inherited T-ML5 paper-trust bound. |
| T-MD22 | **Distribution method spoof without delivery evidence** — variant of T-MD21 where the rep records `distributionMethod: 'email'` to `recipient: 'mlitsd_inspector'` with no `evidenceEnvelopeCt`; the chain shows the method but no delivery proof. Where: distribution route; `evidenceEnvelopeCt` optionality. | The route accepts a distribution event with `evidenceEnvelopeCt` absent — the rep's claim is recorded faithfully. The UI surfaces an optional "Attach delivery evidence (delivery receipt photo, email screenshot, certified mail tracking)" capture field; the rights-protective copy explicitly says "Evidence of delivery is recommended for MLITSD-bound or arbitration-bound distributions but is not required for routine internal distribution." For high-stakes recipient enums (`mlitsd_inspector | arbitrator`), the UI surfaces a soft prompt: "Distributions to MLITSD or arbitrators benefit from delivery evidence — would you like to attach now or proceed?" — NOT a hard gate (per non-negotiable #7, the rep is the privileged party). The chain row carries `evidenceHash: null` honestly; a verifier or arbitrator sees the absence and weighs accordingly. | Documented residual; soft-prompt is the rights-protective behavior. |
| T-MD23 | **Multi-recipient single-event vs per-recipient anchor** — the rep distributes the same PDF to 3 recipients in one motion; if the route emits ONE `minutes_document.distributed` chain row with `recipientHashes: [3]`, the verifier cannot independently re-derive each recipient's hash without the row; an arbitrator probing a single recipient's claim of receipt has to walk both. Where: distribution-bulk endpoint design. | Each recipient is its own chain row — `minutes_document.distributed` is emitted N times for an N-recipient distribution, each carrying a single `recipientHash`. The UI's bulk distribution affordance loops at the API level; the body schema is `POST /api/meetings/:id/minutes-document/distributions` with `recipients: Array<{label_ct, role_enum, method_enum, evidence?}>`, and the route iterates inside a single `db.transaction` to keep the rep's "single submit" UX while preserving per-recipient verifiability. An idempotency key keyed on `(minutes_document_id, recipient_hash)` prevents double-anchoring on retry. | None material; per-recipient discipline matches T-ML / T-IM payload practice. |

**E. Retention + storage**

| # | What / Where | Mitigation | Residual |
|---|---|---|---|
| T-MD24 | **Tigris bucket enumeration via storage_key shape** — the storage_key follows a discoverable pattern that leaks meeting metadata (date, sequence number); an attacker who can enumerate the bucket can map keys to meetings without authn. Where: Tigris key construction in minutes-document POST. | The storage_key is `exports/<minutes_document_id_uuid>/minutes-<random_uuid>.pdf` (parity with §2.8 T-I26 + §2.9 T-R24). Both UUIDs are 122-bit entropy `gen_random_uuid()`. The Tigris bucket has no public-read policy; access requires presigned URLs minted by `GET /api/meetings/:id/minutes-document/:doc_id/download`. The storage-key shape regex is enforced at INSERT time by a DB CHECK on `minutes_documents.storage_key` (inheriting the M2.1 F-L1 pattern that landed for `meeting_signatures.evidence_storage_key`); the regex is `^exports/[0-9a-f-]{36}/minutes-[0-9a-f-]{36}\.pdf$`. | UUID guessing bounded by 122-bit entropy. |
| T-MD25 | **Tigris orphan-document GC at retention boundary** — at the 2-year OHSA retention boundary (T-MD26), the `minutes_documents` row + chain anchors are retained; the Tigris object may need to be retired per the workplace's distribution-cost / cold-storage policy. A misconfigured GC job could delete the row before the retention boundary. Where: Tigris lifecycle policy; M2.1 F-L1-pattern GC for evidence orphans; future ops cron. | The Tigris bucket lifecycle policy is documented in the deploy runbook (forward-seam: `docs/runbooks/minutes-document.md` — M2.3 S5 lands the document). The bucket has NO automatic-expiry policy on `exports/*` (the lifecycle config explicitly excludes the prefix). Retention deletions are operator-initiated via a `scripts/retire-minutes-document.ts` cron that walks `minutes_documents WHERE finalized_at < now() - interval '2 years' AND retention_hold_state = 'released'` and (a) does `DeleteObject` on Tigris, (b) UPDATEs `minutes_documents.storage_key = NULL + retired_at = now()`, (c) emits `minutes_document.retired` chain anchor. The chain anchor for the original document stays; the Tigris bytes go; the rep retains the document hash + the chain provenance forever. | Operator discipline + the script is the bound; documented as the canonical retention path. |
| T-MD26 | **Retention statement legal accuracy — OHSA vs CLC mismatch** — the rendered PDF carries a retention statement ("These minutes are retained for 2 years per OHSA s.X" or "per CLC s.X"); a workplace whose `WORKPLACE_JURISDICTION` env says `ontario` but whose statutory reality is federal (rare misconfiguration) ships a PDF citing the wrong statute. Where: retention-statement render block; `loadWorkplaceConfig().jurisdiction`. | The retention citation comes from `packages/legal-corpus` per non-negotiable #5 — the renderer looks up the entry by `(jurisdiction, topic='records_retention')` and renders the corpus entry's clause text + version_date + source_url verbatim. The legal-corpus seed for M2.3 lands both Ontario (OHSA Reg 834 + s.9 disclosure) and federal (CLC Part II + COHSR) entries (M1.4 + M2.3 corpus extension). The render fail-closes with `retention_citation_missing` if the corpus lookup returns no row for the workplace's jurisdiction; the route returns 500 and the deploy runbook covers the corpus-seed pre-flight check. | Misconfigured `WORKPLACE_JURISDICTION` env is the bound; same posture as M2.1 T-ML41 (workplace-config rotation). |
| T-MD27 | **Retention deletion vs subpoena hold** — an MLITSD subpoena or OLRB hold lands at year 1.5; the rep must extend retention beyond the default 2-year boundary; if the retire script (T-MD25) is on a cron, it could delete the document on day 730 without checking the hold state. Where: retire script; hold state. | The `minutes_documents.retention_hold_state` column is an enum `('released' | 'held_subpoena' | 'held_olrb' | 'held_arbitration' | 'held_internal_review')` with default `'released'`. The retire script's WHERE clause filters `retention_hold_state = 'released'` (T-MD25 mitigation). A rep-initiated `POST /api/meetings/:id/minutes-document/:doc_id/hold` route (M2.3 S3, step-up gated) sets the column to a non-released enum value, captures a `hold_reason_ct` envelope, and emits a `minutes_document.hold_placed` chain anchor. A `POST .../release-hold` (step-up gated, S3) reverses with `minutes_document.hold_released`. The runbook documents the procedure for MLITSD / OLRB / arbitration subpoena handling. | None material; documented runbook path. |
| T-MD28 | **Tigris signed-URL expiry / leak** — the download path mints a presigned URL that an attacker who intercepts (browser tab share, copy-paste in chat) can use until expiry. Where: `GET /api/meetings/:id/minutes-document/:doc_id/download` presign mint. | The download path mints a presigned URL with `expiresIn: 60s` (parity with §2.8 T-I26 + §2.9 T-R26). The route is step-up gated `maxAgeSeconds=60` AND `X-Requested-With: jhsc-web` (csrf header) AND emits a `minutes_document.downloaded` chain anchor per re-download (M2.3 lands the kind from day one — closing the §2.8 1.8 forward-seam pattern in the new milestone). A leaked URL is bounded by the 60s window. | Same bound as the inherited PDF surfaces. |

**F. Re-generation + format versioning**

| # | What / Where | Mitigation | Residual |
|---|---|---|---|
| T-MD29 | **Re-generation race — two reps trigger generation simultaneously, both succeed** — two reps tap "Generate minutes PDF" within seconds; the serializable lock (T-MD2) serializes the two, but the SECOND caller could legitimately want a fresh hash if the first lost its bytes; which is "the canonical doc"? Where: `POST /api/meetings/:id/minutes-document`; multi-row `minutes_documents` per meeting. | The schema allows multiple `minutes_documents` rows per `meeting_id` (history of re-generations); each row has its own `id`, `document_hash`, `storage_key`, `generated_at`, `format_version`, and `chain_anchor_idx`. The "canonical" doc is the `minutes_documents` row with the LATEST `generated_at` AND `format_version = meetings.current_format_version` AND `retention_hold_state IN ('released', 'held_*')`. The UI surfaces the regeneration history honestly: a rep distributing today sees "Latest generated 2026-06-03 (hash <H>); 3 prior versions on file" and the rights-protective copy says "Each generation is recorded in the chain; re-generating after a typo fix is the expected workflow." | The rep's discretion to choose which version to distribute is bounded by the UI's "latest is canonical" affordance; documented. |
| T-MD30 | **format_version drift across re-runs** — a finalized meeting was generated under `format_version = 1` at adjournment-time; six months later the renderer ships `format_version = 2` (new section layout, new signature block ordering); re-generating the same meeting under v2 produces a different document hash + different layout, and an arbitrator comparing two PDFs for the same meeting sees structural divergence. Where: renderer `format_version`; pin-vs-current resolution. | The render route accepts `formatVersion?: number` in the body (default: `meetings.pinned_format_version`, which is set at meeting finalization). A rep generating under a non-pinned version explicitly opts in via the UI's "Use latest format" toggle, which surfaces a confirmation: "This will produce a PDF in format v2; the original v1 hash is preserved in the chain and remains the canonical record of the finalization-time render." The chain payload `minutes_document.generated` carries `formatVersion` so the verifier can distinguish. The renderer's `format_version` is a versioned constant in `packages/shared-types/src/minutes-format.ts` (parity with §2.8 T-I1 template immutability — historical formats stay renderable). | None material — explicit version-pinning + opt-in UI + chain payload field cover the audit need. |
| T-MD31 | **format_version chain payload mismatch** — the `minutes_documents.format_version` column says v1 but the chain row's payload says v2 (data-migration drift, code regression). Where: chain payload `formatVersion` field. | The verifier `--check-minutes-documents` Gate (T-MD40) cross-walks `minutes_documents.format_version == chain_payload.formatVersion` for every row and reports `format_version_mismatch` on drift. Integration test asserts the relationship on every PR. The render path emits the chain row inside the same transaction as the INSERT, so a successful row write implies a chain-row write with matching `formatVersion`. | Same bound as M2.2 cross-chain mismatch detection. |

**G. Rights protection (non-negotiable #7)**

| # | What / Where | Mitigation | Residual |
|---|---|---|---|
| T-MD32 | **Distribution UX as adversarial pressure** — the minutes-document detail view's primary CTA is "Send to Management Co-Chair" with red-amber urgency styling, implying the rep MUST distribute upon generation; chills the rep's discretion over distribution. Where: minutes-document detail view; distribution affordance copy. | The distribution affordance is presented as a NEUTRAL list of recipient roles ("Record distributions") with no urgency framing; the CTA copy is "Record a distribution" (not "Send"). The "decline to distribute" path (T-MD34) is a first-class affordance on the same surface. The rights-protective copy review checklist (extended from M2.1 §2.13 + M2.2 §2.14) covers: (a) no "you must distribute" framing; (b) no "management is waiting" framing; (c) no recipient-role-prominence (the four signer roles + the JHSC committee + external regulators are all listed flat); (d) the rep's discretion is the structural default. S5 reviewer pass walks every copy string. | Same copy-discipline bound as M2.1 T-ML20; documented in the checklist. |
| T-MD33 | **Re-generation UX as "ass-covering" framing** — every re-generation surfaces in the chain; a copy regression that says "Re-generation will be recorded in the audit log" with cautionary styling could shame the rep into not fixing a legitimate typo. Where: re-generation confirmation modal; copy strings. | The re-generation modal's copy explicitly says: "Re-generation is the expected workflow for typo fixes, updated signer information, or format-version migration. Every generation is recorded in the chain; this is your evidentiary record, not a watchpoint." No cautionary styling on the affordance. The S5 reviewer pass covers the modal copy. CLAUDE.md non-negotiable #7. | Same bound as M2.1 T-ML20 / M2.2 T-IM25; documented. |
| T-MD34 | **Distribution method picker omits "Decline to distribute"** — the rep needs a documented path for "this meeting was finalized but I do not intend to distribute the PDF beyond personal-evidence custody"; without an explicit affordance, the rep is implicitly pressured toward distribution.
