Where: distribution method enum; UI affordance. | The `minutes_document_distributions` table includes a `distribution_method_enum` value `decline_to_distribute` (alongside `paper_handoff | email | secure_messaging | mail | in_person_briefing | other`). The rep records a "no distribution" event with an optional `reason_ct` envelope-encrypted basis. The chain anchor `minutes_document.distribution_declined` is emitted; the chain shows the rep affirmatively chose non-distribution. The UI's distribution panel surfaces "I do not intend to distribute this version" as a peer affordance to the recipient list. | None material; structural enum + UI affordance cover the rights-protective need. |

**H. Workplace identity (non-negotiable #1)**

| # | What / Where | Mitigation | Residual |
|---|---|---|---|
| T-MD35 | **Cover page hardcodes workplace name** — the cover-page renderer falls back to a hardcoded literal ("JHSC Worker Hub") when `WORKPLACE_DISPLAY_NAME` env is unset, leaking that the deployment is from this codebase or worse pinning a real workplace name into source. Where: `renderMinutesPdf()` cover page; `loadWorkplaceConfig()`. | The cover page reads `loadWorkplaceConfig().displayName` (env-driven per non-negotiable #1, M2.1 §2.13 T-ML19 pattern). `loadWorkplaceConfig` THROWS on unset required env vars at process boot — no fallback literal. The CI lint (per 1.12 T-HD39 + M2.1 T-ML19) asserts no `'JHSC Worker Hub'`-shape literal in `apps/api/src/meetings/pdf-renderer.ts`. PDF metadata `/Author`, `/Title`, `/Producer` follow the §2.8 T-I28 + §2.9 deployment-checklist pattern: set from runtime config, never hardcoded. Golden-PDF test asserts `/Author` matches runtime config. | Operator misconfiguring env to `"TEST"` would ship `"TEST"` into the PDF; documented as deployment-checklist item (parity with §2.8 T-I28). |
| T-MD36 | **Signer-role labels hardcoded** — the signature block renders "Plant Manager" as a hardcoded literal instead of reading from `workplace.minutesSignerRoles[*].displayRoleLabel` (ADR-0012 §3.9 explicitly env-drives this). Where: signature block in `renderMinutesPdf()`. | The signature block iterates `loadWorkplaceConfig().minutesSignerRoles` and renders each entry's `displayRoleLabel` from config. The structural role enum (`worker_co_chair | mgmt_co_chair | warehouse_mgr | plant_mgr`) backs the data lookup; the rendered label is env-driven. CI lint flags any `'Plant Manager'` / `'Warehouse Manager'` / `'Worker Co-Chair'` / `'Management Co-Chair'` literal in the renderer. | None material; structural config-driven. |
| T-MD37 | **Recipient display names in distribution chain not hashed** — variant of T-MD18 specifically scoped to non-negotiable #1: if the recipient label is a real human's name and the chain carries plaintext, it violates the env-driven-identity invariant for both the workplace's signer roles AND the rep's distribution recipients. Where: distribution chain payload. | T-MD18 mitigation reiterated: the recipient label is envelope-encrypted at rest (`recipient_label_ct`) and only the SHA-256 hash lives in the chain payload. The decrypt path requires authn + workplace KEK + workplace-rep-only authorization. Integration test asserts `pg_dump` of test rows + chain rows contains no plaintext recipient marker. | None material; same shape as T-ML / T-IM payload discipline. |

**I. Audit chain (non-negotiable #2)**

| # | What / Where | Mitigation | Residual |
|---|---|---|---|
| T-MD38 | **`minutes_document.generated` payload missing `documentHash` binding** — the chain row carries `meetingId` + `storageKey` but no `documentHash`, defeating the verifier's ability to re-check the document by re-hashing the Tigris bytes. Where: chain payload shape; `packages/shared-types/src/audit-event-kind.ts`. | The `minutes_document.generated` payload shape is `{meetingId, minutesDocumentId, documentHash (sha256 hex), storageKey, formatVersion, signingKeyId, attestationSigHash, generatedAt}`. The `documentHash` is the canonical integrity anchor; the verifier `--check-minutes-documents` Gate fetches the Tigris bytes, re-hashes, and asserts equality with the chain row's `documentHash` (T-MD14 binding). The payload-shape map (1.12 T-HD28) covers the kind. Mirrors §2.8 T-I29 `inspection.exported` shape with the `documentHash` field name unified across the meeting + inspection + recommendation surfaces. | None material; structural payload-shape map. |
| T-MD39 | **`minutes_document.distributed` payload missing `documentHash` binding** — a distribution chain row that carries the recipient hash but not the document hash leaves an arbitrator unable to bind "this distribution went to X" with "the document was this hash." Where: distribution chain payload shape. | The `minutes_document.distributed` payload shape is `{meetingId, minutesDocumentId, documentHash, recipientHash, recipientRoleEnum, distributionMethodEnum, evidenceHash?, distributedAtRecorded}`. The `documentHash` + the `recipientHash` together bind "this content went to this recipient" — the arbitrator can verify both ends independently. Distribution + content provenance are bound at the chain row level. | None material. |
| T-MD40 | **Chain verifier `--check-minutes-documents` extension missing** — the verifier walks meetings + action items + closure verifications but doesn't gate `minutes_documents`-vs-chain; a regression that orphaned the linkage is detected only when an arbitrator probes. Where: `scripts/audit-log-verify.ts` extension. | M2.3 S2 extends the verifier with `--check-minutes-documents` (parity with M2.1 `--check-meetings` + M2.2 `--check-action-items`). Gates: (1) every `minutes_documents` row has a `minutes_document.generated` chain row with matching `documentHash` + `formatVersion` + `signingKeyId`; (2) every `minutes_document.generated` row's `storageKey` returns 200 from Tigris HEAD (subject to T-MD14 grace window); (3) every `minutes_document.distributed` row's `minutesDocumentId` matches an existing `minutes_documents` row + the `documentHash` matches; (4) every `minutes_document.distributed` row's `meetingId` matches the upstream `meeting.finalized` row's `meetingId`; (5) every `minutes_documents.retention_hold_state != 'released'` row has a corresponding `minutes_document.hold_placed` chain row (and no superseding `hold_released`); (6) every Ed25519 detached signature in `minutes_documents.attestation_sig_ct` verifies against the workplace public key referenced by `signing_key_id`. | None material; verifier-gate coverage is the structural backstop. |

**J. Rate limit + DoS**

| # | What / Where | Mitigation | Residual |
|---|---|---|---|
| T-MD41 | **Generation rate-limit DoS** — minutes-document render is expensive (decrypt N attendee names + N section notes + N closure narratives + N signature envelopes + Ed25519 sign); a malicious client could spam `POST /api/meetings/:id/minutes-document` and pin the API CPU. Where: minutes-document POST handler; rate-limit middleware. | The route is wrapped by the existing 1.5 middleware stack: `rateLimit({name: 'meetings-minutes-document', capacity: 30, refillPerSecond: 5})` (parity with §2.8 inspections-exports + §2.9 recommendations-exports). The per-actor abuse bucket is layered: `consumeActorToken({capacity: 10, refillPerHour: 10})` — 10 minutes-document generations per hour per actor (looser than §2.8's 5/hour because re-generation is the documented workflow for typo fixes per T-MD33; tighter than the meetings PATCH rate). The pg-boss-backed cross-process variant is the 1.12 follow-up (consistent with §2.8). The route requires step-up `maxAgeSeconds = 60` per non-negotiable #16 — a bot would need a fresh passkey assertion every request, raising the cost above brute-force economics. | Same bound as §2.8 / §2.9 export rate-limit posture. |
| T-MD42 | **Enumeration via timing** — the route's response time differs between "meeting exists, generation succeeded" vs "meeting exists but not finalized" vs "meeting does not exist"; an attacker could enumerate meeting UUIDs by timing. Where: route timing characteristics. | The route's `assertMinutesDocumentReady(meetingId)` helper (parity with §2.8 `assertInspectionExportReady`) runs BEFORE step-up verification and BEFORE any decrypt, doing a single FOR UPDATE projection that always touches the same row count regardless of state. Return paths: 404 `meeting_not_found`, 422 `meeting_not_finalized`, 401 `step_up_required`, 429 `rate_limited`. The "not found" vs "not finalized" timing differs by < 1ms (a single column inspection); the "not finalized" vs "happy path" differs by the render duration (seconds). An enumeration attempt is bounded by the rate limit (T-MD41) and step-up requirement; an unauthenticated probe hits the auth-middleware-401 before any DB touch. | Bounded by 122-bit UUID entropy + rate limit + step-up. Acceptable. |

**K. Print stylesheet posture**

| # | What / Where | Mitigation | Residual |
|---|---|---|---|
| T-MD43 | **Server-side render diverges from client print stylesheet** — the rep prints the in-app meeting detail view via the browser's `@media print` stylesheet (per CLAUDE.md "Print stylesheet for every printable view"), getting layout A; the M2.3 server-side renderer produces layout B; the chain anchors B but the rep distributes A. Where: client `@media print` block in `apps/web/src/index.css`; server `renderMinutesPdf()`. | The server-side renderer is the **canonical** distributable artifact per ROADMAP M2.3 "PDF export matching the Excel file's print layout" + non-negotiable #16. The client-side browser print is a fallback affordance for offline / on-the-go printing and is NOT a chain-anchored artifact. The UI explicitly labels the browser-print path as "Quick print (not chain-anchored)" and surfaces the server-generated download path as "Canonical minutes PDF (chain-anchored, document hash <H>)". The two paths are visually similar (Source Serif 4 + the same section layout via Tailwind classes the print stylesheet preserves), but only the server-rendered PDF carries the document hash + chain anchor + Ed25519 signature. The rights-protective copy on the print affordance directs reps to the canonical surface for any external distribution. | The rep's discretion to distribute the quick-print version is the bound; documented. |
| T-MD44 | **Print stylesheet `data-print` discipline regression** — the client-side meeting detail view's chrome (back-links, action buttons, capture FAB) is marked with `data-print="hide"` per the M2.1 + M2.2 convention; a server-side renderer that **reuses the same React tree** for the canonical PDF MUST also respect the convention or the PDF will carry app-chrome that should not surface in evidence. Where: server-side render path; React tree reuse. | The M2.3 server-side renderer does NOT reuse the React tree — it is a dedicated `pdfkit`-based render with its own layout primitives (parity with §2.8 inspections renderer + §2.9 recommendations renderer). The canonical PDF is built from the database row + decrypted envelopes, NOT from a server-rendered React tree. The `data-print="hide"` convention applies to the BROWSER print path (T-MD43); the canonical renderer has no equivalent chrome to hide because there is no app chrome in the renderer's input. Golden-PDF test asserts the rendered output has no rendered "Back" / "Edit" / "Add Section" / "FAB" strings. The `data-print="evidentiary"` convention surfaces in the BROWSER print path; the canonical renderer emits the evidentiary block (chain-anchor explanation, audit row indices, document hash) unconditionally (these are the chain-of-custody attestations per non-negotiable #16). | None material; convention applies to browser print, not to canonical render. |
| T-MD45 | **Print stylesheet `data-print="evidentiary"` block leaks pre-render plaintext into a browser-printed quick-print** — the in-browser meeting detail view shows decrypted attendee names + section notes (the rep is authenticated); the `@media print` block surfaces the evidentiary metadata; if the rep prints via browser BEFORE the M2.3 canonical generator has run, the printed page carries all the plaintext but no chain anchor, no document hash, no Ed25519 signature — a quasi-evidentiary artifact without the integrity guarantees. Where: browser print path; `@media print` block in `apps/web/src/index.css`. | The browser print path is explicitly labeled "Quick print (not chain-anchored)" per T-MD43; the print stylesheet appends a watermark footer "This is a quick print — not the canonical chain-anchored minutes document. For distribution, generate the canonical PDF from the Minutes Document panel." The watermark is mandatory via the `@media print` block; an integration test asserts the watermark string appears in the printable view's DOM under the print media query. The rep's discretion to distribute the quick-print remains, but the watermark surfaces the residual to the recipient. | Same bound as T-MD43; watermark is the structural cue. |
| T-MD46 | **Canonical-render-vs-quick-print hash divergence as positive feature** — variant of T-MD43: the rep generates a canonical PDF (hash H1) on Monday, then a quick-print on Tuesday (no hash, no chain), then a re-canonical-PDF on Wednesday (hash H2 != H1 if a typo got fixed); an arbitrator asks "which is canonical?" The chain answers honestly: H1 and H2 both have `minutes_document.generated` rows; the Tuesday quick-print is not on the chain. Where: chain-rendered docs vs print paths. | Documented posture, not a vulnerability. The verifier `--check-minutes-documents` Gate 1 (T-MD40) reports H1 + H2 as both canonical generations; the rep's distribution-tracking records (T-MD18..T-MD23) show which version went to which recipient. The Tuesday quick-print has no chain anchor and is structurally not a canonical record. An arbitrator probing the audit history sees the truth. | None material; the chain-vs-non-chain distinction is the structural cue. |

#### Cross-cutting controls

Re-uses the controls layered across §2.7 (1.7 evidence step-up + Tigris SSE), §2.8 (1.8 inspection PDF render + audit chain + step-up freshness + Tigris signed-URL TTL + per-actor token bucket + 30-day TTL), §2.9 (1.9 recommendation Ed25519 detached signature over PDF + workplace signing-key reuse), §2.13 (M2.1 meeting envelope encryption + 4-signer attestation + 60s step-up freshness + serializable adjournment isolation + chain-payload PI discipline), and §2.14 (M2.2 closure-verification step-up + cross-chain anchors + closure-row payload-shape PI discipline). Documented don't-duplicate. **New cross-cutting controls specific to M2.3:**

- **Document hash anchored in chain.** Every `minutes_document.generated` chain row carries `documentHash` (SHA-256 hex of the rendered bytes after the T-MD15 two-pass footer fill). The hash is ALSO embedded in the PDF footer as plaintext (full 64 chars, JetBrains Mono) so an offline reader can re-verify by hashing the file. The chain row's payload-shape map (1.12 T-HD28) covers the kind with `documentHash` as a required field. The verifier `--check-minutes-documents` Gate 1 (T-MD40) re-hashes the Tigris bytes and asserts equality.

- **Workplace Ed25519 detached signature over the document hash.** The `minutes_documents.attestation_sig_ct` column carries the 64-byte Ed25519 detached signature of the canonical `{meetingId, documentHash, generatedAt, formatVersion, signingKeyId}` JSON, signed under the workplace signing key (same key registry as 1.9 recommendation signing + M2.1 meeting attestation per M2.1 F-S6 / M2.2 TM-fold-5). The chain row carries `signingKeyId` + `attestationSigHash`; the verifier Gate 6 re-verifies the signature against the workplace public key. Cross-meeting / cross-milestone signing-key consistency is enforced (T-MD10).

- **Tigris storage_key regex discipline.** `minutes_documents.storage_key` is constrained by DB CHECK to `^exports/[0-9a-f-]{36}/minutes-[0-9a-f-]{36}\.pdf$` (M2.1 F-L1 pattern inherited). Tigris bucket has no public-read; access requires per-request 60s presigned URLs minted under step-up gating (T-MD28). Tigris SSE AES256 is set on every PUT (§2.8 priv-F1 close-out inherited).

- **Workplace decryption key lifecycle in Fly Machine.** The render request opens the workplace KEK + the workplace signing private key in `sodium_malloc`-backed buffers, performs all decrypts + the Ed25519 sign within one bounded transaction, and `sodium.memzero`'s both in `finally` (parity with §2.8 T-I23 + M2.1 §2.13 F-S6 + M2.2 close-verification `:464-466`). Bun GC residency is the documented residual; the KEK rotation runbook (1.3 §3a) covers post-incident rotation. The signing private key open happens AFTER all decrypts complete, narrowing the dual-key co-residence window (T-MD7).

- **Rights-protective copy review checklist extension.** The M2.1 checklist + M2.2 extension carries forward; M2.3 adds: (a) no "you must distribute" framing on the distribution affordance (T-MD32); (b) no cautionary styling on re-generation (T-MD33); (c) explicit "decline to distribute" affordance (T-MD34); (d) recipient list is flat without role-prominence (T-MD32); (e) the quick-print path carries the "not chain-anchored" watermark (T-MD45); (f) retention statement is corpus-driven, not hardcoded (T-MD26).

#### Known gaps (forward seams)

1. **M2.4 Excel re-import vs minutes-document re-generation.** When a finalized meeting is re-imported from an Excel update (M2.4 absorbs the re-import flow), the minutes-document needs re-generation under the next `format_version` OR explicit re-anchoring; the architect should flag whether re-import implies forced re-generation OR whether the prior minutes-document remains canonical with the Excel update producing a separate `meeting.amendment` chain anchor. M2.3 ships with `formatVersion` + the chain row's distinguishing fields ready for M2.4 to land the policy.
2. **M2.5+ work-refusal minutes** (work-refusal proceedings under OHSA s.43 / CLC s.128 may produce a distinct "refusal record" PDF that overlays minutes-document mechanics with refusal-specific rights-protective copy). The M2.5 ADR will flag whether to reuse the M2.3 substrate or fork; the `minutes_documents` table's `document_kind` enum is forward-seamed (M2.3 ships with `document_kind = 'minutes'` and the column ready for `'work_refusal_record'`).
3. **Release 3 E2EE distribution to other reps.** Multi-rep doc review + E2EE delivery to a peer rep (Signal-protocol-based per CLAUDE.md `libsignal-protocol-typescript`) is R3 scope; M2.3 records distribution events under the rep's claim, not a cryptographic delivery receipt. The `distribution_method_enum` carries `secure_messaging` as a forward-seam value.
4. **Release 3 multi-rep co-chair counter-sign on minutes-document re-generation.** Today the worker co-chair re-generates unilaterally; R3 may require peer-rep counter-sign on re-generation under a major `formatVersion` bump. The `minutes_documents` schema can accommodate a future `regeneration_counter_sig_ct` column without migration disruption.
5. **PAdES-embedded signatures inside the PDF.** Today the Ed25519 detached signature lives in `minutes_documents.attestation_sig_ct` (database-side) + the chain anchor (audit-side); the PDF itself is unsigned-at-the-PDF-level. PAdES (PDF Advanced Electronic Signatures) embedding is the eventual close-out for in-PDF signature verification by third-party PDF viewers (parity with M2.1 §2.13 known-gap #1 forward-seam to 1.12 ADR-0011 backlog). M2.3 ships without PAdES; the document hash + chain provenance is the bound.
6. **Per-action / per-resource step-up binding.** M2.2 §2.14 F-S7 documented the honest contract that `checkStepUpFreshness` does NOT verify the `action` claim matches the called endpoint (60s freshness is actor+time only). M2.3 inherits this residual; per-resource binding for `meeting.minutes_document.generate` is a forward-seam to the 1.12 hardening item.
7. **Audit-row redaction for accidentally-captured PI in distribution recipient labels.** Per M2.1 §2.13 T-ML24 + M2.2 §2.14 forward-seam: the redaction table is post-Release-1 backlog; T-MD37's hash-only invariant is the structural defense; the redaction need does not arise. A future bug that emitted recipient plaintext would trip the same forensic procedure.

#### S1 architectural folds

The M2.3 threat model surfaces seven architectural concerns that need to land in S1 to satisfy the threat coverage:

1. **TM-fold-1 (T-MD2 + T-MD15) — serializable isolation on the minutes-document POST + two-pass footer dance.** S1 wraps the `POST /api/meetings/:id/minutes-document` handler in `db.transaction({ isolationLevel: 'serializable' })` (parity with M2.2 TM-fold-4) AND lands the two-pass footer dance (placeholder render → byte hash → in-buffer substitution → re-hash → chain emit) as the canonical `renderMinutesPdf()` shape. Integration test asserts byte-determinism on identical fixture re-runs.
2. **TM-fold-2 (T-MD11) — `audience: 'internal' | 'published'` body field + dual-render output.** S1 ships the `audience` enum in the body schema + the renderer's branching for closure-narrative redaction in `'published'` mode. The audience selection is a chain payload field on `minutes_document.generated`. Integration test asserts the published-mode PDF contains no closure narrative plaintext.
3. **TM-fold-3 (T-MD18 + T-MD37) — distribution chain payload PI discipline + recipient label canonicalization.** S1 lands `packages/shared-types/src/recipient-canonicalization.ts` (lowercase + trim + NFC) for `recipientHash` derivation; the chain payload's TypeScript discriminated-union enumerates `recipientHash`, NOT `recipientLabel`. Integration test asserts `pg_dump` of the chain rows contains no recipient plaintext.
4. **TM-fold-4 (T-MD24) — `minutes_documents.storage_key` DB CHECK regex.** S1 adds the migration with the explicit regex check `storage_key ~ '^exports/[0-9a-f-]{36}/minutes-[0-9a-f-]{36}\.pdf$'`. Integration test asserts INSERT with a malformed key fails 23514.
5. **TM-fold-5 (T-MD26) — legal-corpus retention-citation pre-flight.** S1 extends the `packages/legal-corpus` seed with retention-statement entries for both Ontario (OHSA + Reg 834) and federal (CLC Part II + COHSR) jurisdictions; the renderer's `loadRetentionCitation(jurisdiction)` helper fail-closes if the corpus lookup returns no row. Deploy runbook gains the corpus pre-flight check (parity with M2.1 known-gap #4 quorum-citation forward-seam closure).
6. **TM-fold-6 (T-MD27) — `minutes_documents.retention_hold_state` enum + hold/release routes.** S1 adds the column + the `POST .../hold` + `POST .../release-hold` routes (step-up gated) + the `minutes_document.hold_placed` + `minutes_document.hold_released` chain kinds. The retire-cron's WHERE clause filters `retention_hold_state = 'released'`.
7. **TM-fold-7 (T-MD40) — verifier `--check-minutes-documents` extension.** S1 lands the verifier extension with all six gates enumerated under T-MD40. The fixture-generator script (1.12 T-HD27) regenerates the synthetic full-dataset to include the M2.3 kinds before S5 close-out.

**M2.3 adds 6 new audit event kinds: `minutes_document.generated`, `minutes_document.distributed`, `minutes_document.downloaded`, `minutes_document.hold_placed`, `minutes_document.hold_released`, `minutes_document.retired` (plus `minutes_document.distribution_declined` from T-MD34 as a structural sibling of `.distributed`, taking the count to 7 if S1 elects to ship it as a distinct kind — the user-decision is flagged in the ADR-0014 S0 addendum).** The minimum-viable kind set per the user-prompt's "2 estimated" target is `{generated, distributed}`; the threat coverage surfaces the additional five as load-bearing (downloaded → §2.8 1.8 forward-seam closure; hold_placed + hold_released → T-MD27 subpoena procedure; retired → T-MD25 GC chain trail; distribution_declined → T-MD34 rights-protective default). The deploy runbook's `audit-log-verify --full` is extended with `--check-minutes-documents` (parity with M2.1 `--check-meetings` + M2.2 `--check-action-items`). **The prefix space `T-MD*` does NOT collide with M2.1's `T-ML*` (44 T-ML* threats in §2.13) or M2.2's `T-IM*` (44 T-IM* threats in §2.14) — `T-MD*` is structurally distinct (Minutes Document, the externally-distributable artifact); the three prefix families are orthogonal and the verifier walks all three kinds independently.

---

## 3. Security Controls

### Authentication

- **Primary:** Passkey/WebAuthn (FIDO2). Phishing-resistant. Bound to origin.
- **Fallback:** Username + password (Argon2id: 64MB mem, 3 iter) + mandatory TOTP (RFC 6238).
- **Session:** JWT (EdDSA, 30 min access) + refresh token (HttpOnly, Secure, SameSite=Strict, 14 days). Rotates on use.
- **Step-up auth:** Re-prompt for passkey/TOTP before exports, identity decryption, deletions, **Excel import commits, Excel import reverts, action item archival**.
- **Device registration:** Optional but tenant admin can require it.
- **Brute force protection:** 5 failed = 15 min lockout; 10 = 1 hour; 20 = manual unlock required.

### Encryption

- **In transit:** TLS 1.3 only. HSTS preload. No HTTP fallback.
- **At rest (sensitive fields):** XChaCha20-Poly1305 via libsodium, application-layer, before Postgres write.
- **At rest (files):** Client-side encryption before Tigris upload. Tigris stores ciphertext only.
- **Local cache:** IndexedDB sensitive fields encrypted with session-derived key. Cache cleared on logout.
- **Master key:** Fly Secrets, accessible only to `api` Machine process. Never logged. Never returned by API.
- **Key rotation:** Annual rotation of derived keys. Master key rotation triggers re-encryption sweep.
- **Excel import encryption:** Sensitive fields encrypted in the browser via libsodium-wrappers BEFORE any API call. The raw Excel file never leaves the device.

### Tenant Boundaries (Single-Tenant)

User-level access controls still apply:

- Every query is scoped to the authenticated user's role
- A `worker_rep` cannot read another rep's practice journal
- A `read_only` reviewer cannot decrypt member identities without re-consent
- Audit log writes are immutable; users cannot delete their own entries
- **Action item moves cannot be silently rolled back — every move is permanent in the audit log even if the item is moved again**

### Audit & Logging

- **Tamper-evident audit log** (hash chain, HMAC-seeded).
- **What gets logged:** all writes to sensitive tables, all reads of decrypted sensitive fields, all exports, all auth events, all config changes, **all Excel import lifecycle events, all action item section moves**.
- **What does NOT get logged:** sensitive field contents, encryption keys, passwords, full request bodies for sensitive endpoints. Logs contain identifiers and metadata only.
- **Log retention:**
  - **`audit_log` (tamper-evident chain):** rows retained **indefinitely** (the chain is the evidentiary record). The `ip` and `user_agent` columns redact to `NULL` at 1 year via the annual sweep + `audit.ip_redacted` chain anchor — see `.context/decisions.md` 2026-05-29 entry and `docs/runbooks/auth.md` §4a/§7. The redaction script lands in 1.12 hardening; until then, IP/UA persist for the full chain age (documented residual).
  - **`auth_events` (1.2 flat table):** read-only legacy preserved for hash-anchored reference from the 1.3 backfill anchor. Same retention posture as `audit_log`.
  - **`login_attempts` and `webauthn_challenges`:** operational; pruned by `auth-retention.ts` (2× hard-tier window for `login_attempts`, expires_at + 1h grace for `webauthn_challenges`).
  - **Application logs (Pino):** 90 days hot, 1 year cold per the pre-1.3 baseline.
- **Verification:** `scripts/audit-log-verify.ts` runs nightly via cron.

### Headers & Transport

(Unchanged. CSP strict mode, HSTS preload, Permissions-Policy blocking unneeded APIs, COEP/COOP for cross-origin isolation.)

### Input Validation

- All API inputs validated with Zod schemas
- Server-side validation is the source of truth
- File uploads (evidence): type-sniffed, size-limited (50 MB default), hashed
- HTML user input rendered with proper escaping; rich text passed through DOMPurify
- **Excel parsing: see § Excel Import Security below**

### Rate Limiting

- Auth endpoints: 10 requests / minute / IP
- API write endpoints: 60 / minute / user
- AI proxy: 30 / hour / user
- Export endpoints: 5 / hour / user
- **Excel import preview: 10 / hour / user** (preview is cheap; commits require step-up auth anyway)

### Dependency & Supply Chain

- `pnpm audit` runs on every CI build; high/critical vulns block merge
- Dependabot enabled
- Gitleaks scans every push for committed secrets
- Lockfile committed; changes reviewed
- Minimal dependency footprint
- No analytics SDKs, no telemetry, no third-party tracking
- **SheetJS is the only Excel-parsing dependency; pinned to a specific version with regular review of CVEs**

### Browser & Mobile Hardening

(Unchanged. Service worker integrity checks, IndexedDB cleared on logout, camera-captured photos never written to device library, biometric prompt after idle, auto-logout.)

---

## 4. Excel Import Security

### Why This Needs Its Own Section

Excel files are an attack surface. .xlsm files can contain VBA macros (we don't execute them, but the file can also contain crafted content that targets parser bugs). Even .xlsx files can contain XXE attacks, zip bomb attacks, formula injection attacks, and embedded executables.

The fact that we parse client-side instead of server-side is a meaningful mitigation — a parser exploit attacks one rep's browser, not the whole platform. But we still defend.

### Supported File Family

One file family is recognized and parsed; everything else is rejected:

1. **Minutes files** (.xlsm or .xlsx) — meeting minutes with action item tracking

Inspection file imports are not supported in Release 1. Inspections are conducted natively in-app.

### Controls

1. **Pure parsing only.** SheetJS is configured with `cellFormula: false` and `cellHTML: false`. We never evaluate formulas or interpret HTML in cells.
2. **No macro execution.** VBA macros in .xlsm files are ignored. They are not interpreted, not displayed, not stored.
3. **Zip bomb protection.** Files >10 MB rejected at file-picker time. Decompressed size capped at 100 MB.
4. **Schema-first parsing.** We don't attempt to "interpret" arbitrary Excel files. The parser looks for our documented schema (`docs/excel-import-format.md`) and rejects anything that doesn't match. Files that look hostile but happen to match the schema would have to look like valid JHSC minutes — a high bar.
5. **Sanitization at parse.** Cell values are coerced to expected types. Strings are trimmed and length-capped (descriptions: 5000 chars, names: 200 chars).
6. **Formula injection prevention.** If a string cell begins with `=`, `+`, `-`, `@`, or tab, prepend a single quote when storing. This is defense for any downstream Excel exports.
7. **HTML injection prevention.** All imported text is treated as plain text and properly escaped wherever rendered.
8. **Hash-based provenance.** The SHA-256 of the imported file is stored (not the file itself). This lets us prove later "this action item came from this specific file at this time."
9. **No execution of imported content.** Imported text is never `eval`'d, never rendered as HTML without escaping, never used as a template string, never passed to a query builder as raw SQL.
10. **Preview before commit.** Every import shows the rep what will happen before anything is created. Conflicts and surprises surface to the rep.
11. **Reversible for 30 days.** If a malicious import is discovered, it can be reverted within 30 days (creates an audit entry of the revert).
12. **No bulk auto-import.** Files must be selected one at a time via file picker. No "watch this folder" automation.
13. **PII scanning on imports.** Each imported field is run through the client-side PII heuristic. Fields detected as likely containing names or identifying info are encrypted before they leave the browser.

### What We Don't Defend Against

- A rep importing their own legitimate file with embedded names of real workers. That's the intended use case. The fact that names are in the file means they need to be encrypted, but not blocked.
- A rep importing a file given to them by a third party who modified it maliciously. We trust the rep's choice of file. We do warn (via the file hash and source documentation) that imports are tied to specific source files.
- An attacker with rep credentials importing a malicious file. The step-up auth on commit, the preview, and the audit log are the mitigations here.

---

## 4a. Export Security

Inspection PDF exports are a new attack surface — once a document leaves the app, the rep is responsible for handling it. The app's job is to make exports auditable and tamper-evident.

### Controls

1. **Step-up auth before export.** Re-authentication required (passkey or TOTP) before generating any PDF.
2. **Audit-logged.** Every export creates an `export_records` entry with: exporter identity, exported_at timestamp, IDs of records included, output document hash (SHA-256), audit chain anchor. The audit entry is immutable.
3. **Tamper-evident output.** Every generated PDF includes a footer on every page:
   - Exported by [user] on [ISO date]
   - Document hash: sha256 [hash]
   - Audit anchor: [hash]
   This makes after-the-fact modification detectable.
4. **Decryption is in-memory only.** Sensitive fields are decrypted only long enough to render to PDF, then zeroed in memory. No plaintext copy persists.
5. **Rate-limited.** Maximum 5 exports per hour per user (matches general export rate limit). Batch exports capped at 100 inspections per call.
6. **No background or scheduled exports.** Every export is initiated by a logged-in user with step-up auth. No cron-job exports, no automatic "send me my data weekly" features.
7. **Photos in PDFs are decrypted and embedded** — this is the necessary purpose of export. The footer disclosure makes downstream leaks traceable to the exporter.
8. **Exports do not include audit log content** by default. The audit chain anchor is included so the chain can be verified, but the chain itself stays in the database. A separate audit-log export endpoint exists for the rare case where the chain must travel with the document.

### What This Doesn't Defend Against

- A rep exporting and then carelessly sharing a PDF. Once the PDF leaves the app, it's the rep's responsibility.
- A subpoenaed disclosure of an exported PDF. The export was authorized by the rep at the time; the audit log proves what was exported. If the rep is later forced to disclose, the disclosure is the issue, not the export.
- An attacker with rep credentials exporting and exfiltrating. The step-up auth and rate limits are the mitigations; the audit log lets you detect this after the fact.

---

## 5. Action Item Move Integrity

The action item section lifecycle is operationally critical. Each move (e.g., New Business → Old Business) is:

1. **Recorded in `action_item_moves`** with timestamp, actor, from/to sections, optional reason
2. **Linked into the audit chain** with hash continuity
3. **Counter-signed by the meeting context** — moves happen "in a meeting," and the meeting ID is part of the audit metadata
4. **Subject to step-up auth for archival** — moving an item out of normal view (to "archived") requires re-authentication

Why this matters: a rep needs to be able to prove later, in front of an arbitrator, that an item was raised on date X, moved to old business on date Y, and closed on date Z. The audit chain provides that proof. Tamper would be detected by the chain verification routine.

---

## 6. Privacy Controls

(Largely unchanged. Data minimization, consent capture, pseudonymization at intake, PIPEDA rights.)

### Excel Import Privacy

- **The raw Excel file never leaves the device.** It's parsed in the browser.
- **Imported content is encrypted at the application layer** before any sync to the server.
- **Imports respect the same retention rules** as direct data entry. If a record is purged, its source-file reference is purged too.
- **A rep can revert an import** to remove all records that came from a specific file. The audit log retains the revert event but the content is cryptographically erased.

### Cross-Border Disclosure (Honest Statement)

Fly.io and Neon are US-incorporated. CLOUD Act applies. The encryption mitigates substantially — a compelled disclosure yields ciphertext for sensitive fields. **Excel import data is in the same category** — once it's in the database, it benefits from the same encryption guarantees and faces the same theoretical compelled-disclosure exposure.

---

## 7. Incident Response

(Unchanged from prior spec. P0–P3 classification, detect/triage/contain/eradicate/recover/notify/post-mortem.)

### New Incident Types

- **Malicious Excel import discovered** — treat as P2 unless the import affected the audit chain (then P0). Revert the import. Audit affected records. Notify the rep.
- **Action item move integrity failure** — audit chain verification finds a missing or inconsistent move. Treat as P1. Investigate, restore from chain backup if possible, document.
- **PII heuristic false negative on import** — sensitive content imported in plaintext column. Treat as P1. Immediately encrypt affected fields, re-key if needed, audit the import.

### Breach Notification

PIPEDA s.10.1 still applies. For JHSC worker data, the threshold is generally met if member identities or medical information are exposed, including via a compromised import.

### Backup & Recovery

- Neon point-in-time recovery: 7-30 days
- Nightly encrypted `pg_dump` to Tigris
- Monthly local cold-storage copy
- Quarterly restoration drill
- **Action item move history is included in all backups and verified during restoration drills**

---

## 8. Pre-Launch Security Checklist

Before going live with real worker data:

- [ ] All sensitive fields encrypted at application layer (verified by Neon query inspection)
- [ ] Audit log verification passes on full dataset
- [ ] CSP strict mode active, no inline scripts
- [ ] All security headers verified (observatory.mozilla.org)
- [ ] HSTS preload submitted
- [ ] Passkey enrollment tested on iOS and Android
- [ ] TOTP fallback tested
- [ ] Step-up auth tested for all sensitive operations
- [ ] Rate limits verified
- [ ] Backup and restore tested end-to-end
- [ ] Disaster recovery: full app rebuilt from scratch using only backups
- [ ] `pnpm audit` clean
- [ ] Gitleaks clean
- [ ] Penetration test attempted (OWASP ZAP minimum)
- [ ] Incident response playbook reviewed
- [ ] Privacy notice drafted
- [ ] Cold-storage backup procedure tested
- [ ] Logout / session expiry tested mobile + desktop
- [ ] Biometric re-auth tested after idle timeout
- [ ] Workplace config loads from env, not committed
- [ ] Camera photos bypass device library (verified)
- [ ] **Excel import: malicious file fuzzing performed against parser**
- [ ] **Excel import: zip bomb rejection tested with crafted file**
- [ ] **Excel import: formula injection prevention verified in downstream exports**
- [ ] **Excel import: PII heuristic tested with realistic minutes content**
- [ ] **Excel import: preview-then-commit flow tested end-to-end**
- [ ] **Excel import: reversal within 30 days tested with audit log verification**
- [ ] **Action item move audit chain verified across 100+ simulated moves**
- [ ] **Inspection template versioning tested — historical inspection rendered correctly under old template version after template upgrade**
- [ ] **Inspection manual promotion tested — one-tap promotion creates correctly-linked action item in new_business section**
- [ ] **Inspection PDF export — single inspection produces evidence-grade output with hash footer**
- [ ] **Inspection PDF export — date-range batch (100 inspections) renders correctly with table of contents**
- [ ] **Inspection PDF export — step-up auth enforced, audit log entry created with output hash**
- [ ] **Inspection PDF export — verified that modifying the exported PDF causes hash mismatch detectable on re-verify**

---

## 9. Ongoing Security Operations

(Unchanged: weekly audit log review, dependency checks, monthly audit, quarterly pen test, annual key rotation.)

Additions:

- **Monthly:** Review Excel import logs. Confirm no unexpected high-volume imports.
- **Quarterly:** Re-fuzz the Excel parser with the latest SheetJS version.
- **Annually:** Review the schema in `docs/excel-import-format.md` against actual workplace files. Update as the rep's workflow evolves.
